September 4, 2019) was an American singer-songwriter.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.wideopencountry.com/kylie-rae-harris-fashion-playlist/|title=Texas Artist Kylie Rae Harris Shares Festival Fashion Looks and Summer-Ready Playlist [Exclusive]|last=Sawyer|first=Bobbie Jean|date=June 12, 2019|website=Wide Open Country|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.dallasobserver.com/music/kylie-rae-harris-on-singing-with-zane-williams-and-her-excellent-new-ep-7053584|title=Kylie Rae Harris on Singing with Zane Williams and Her (Excellent) New EP|last=Dearmore|first=Kelly|date=September 20, 2013|website=[[Dallas Observer]]|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite Learned|date=March 26, 2019|website=Guitar Girl Magazine|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.centraltrack.com/song-of-the-day-kylie-rae-harris-big-ol-heartache/|title=Song of the Day: Kylie Rae Harris \u2013 \"Big Ol' Heartache.\"|last=Graves|first=Cory|date=February 4, 2019|website=Central Track|access-date=7 September 2019}}</ref> She was born in [[Wylie, Texas]].\n\n== Career ==\nAt age twelve, Harris was enrolled in a vocal camp and began crafting her own songs and playing guitar. By the time she graduated from high school, Harris earned a music scholarship and a welding scholarship, but took neither and decided to press on with her musical career. She was one of the featured artists in ''[[Troubadour, TX]]'', a television show documenting her rising career as a Texas country singer-songwriter.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://popculture.com/country-music/2019/09/05/kylie-rae-harris-country-singer-reveals-was-approached-abc-reality-show/|title=Country Singer Kylie Rae Harris Reveals She Was Approached for ABC Reality Show|website=Country Music}}</ref>\n\nOn July 1, 2010, Harris released her debut album titled ''All the Right Reasons'',<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.discogs.com/Kylie-Rae-Harris-All-The-Right-Reasons/release/13373990|title=Kylie Rae Harris \u2013 All The Right Reasons|date=2010 |publisher=discogs}}</ref> followed by an EP in 2013 titled ''Taking It Back''.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.discogs.com/Kylie-Rae-Harris-Taking-It-Back/release/13373975|title=Kylie Rae Harris \u2013 Taking It Back|date=2013 |publisher=discogs}}</ref>\n\nIn 2013, Harris began working on material for a second full-length album and toured with fellow ''Troubadour, TX'' star [[Zane Williams]] throughout the state.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.earnthenecklace.com/kylie-rae-harris-wiki/|title=Who Is Kylie Rae Harris: Wiki and Facts About the Deceased Country Singer|last=John|first=Caroline |date=September 6, 2019|website=Earn The Necklace|access-date=September 11, 2019}}</ref> Then in March 2019, she released a new self titled EP.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.dallasobserver.com/music/wylies-kylie-rae-harris-has-a-new-self-titled-ep-out-11627825|title=Kylie Rae Harris Looks Back and Moves Forward on Her New EP|last=Dearmore|first=Kelly|date=March 29, 2019|website=[[Dallas Observer]]|access-date=September 7, 2019}}</ref>\n\n== Death ==\nHarris died on September 4, 2019, when her car collided with another near [[Taos, New Mexico]]. She was 30 years old<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.taosnews.com/stories/sheriff-speed-likely-contributed-to-crash-that-killed-taos-high-teen-texas-singer,59343 |title=Sheriff: Speed likely contributed to crash that killed Taos High teen, Texas singer |last=Matlock |first=Staci |date=September 5, 2019 |work=[[Taos News]] |access-date=September 7, 2019|url-access=subscription}}</ref><ref name=\"cnn._Coun\">{{Cite web|title=Country singer Kylie Rae Harris dies in car accident|last=Gonzalez|first=Sandra|website=[[CNN]]|date=September 5, 2019| access-date=September 5, 2019|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/09/05/entertainment/kylie-rae-harris-country-singer-dead-trnd/index.html}}</ref> and is survived by her daughter.<ref name=\"bill_Kyli\">{{Cite magazine|title=Kylie Rae Harris Dead: Country Singer Dies In Car Accident|last=Reuter |first=Annie|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|date=September 5, 2019|access-date=September 5, 2019|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/8529184/kylie-rae-harris-dies-country-singer-dead-car-accident}}</ref> A subsequent investigation, completed in December 2019, revealed she had been driving up to {{convert|102|mph|km/h|abbr=on}} ({{convert|95|mph|km/h|abbr=on}} when the crash occurred), confirmed by her vehicle's computer, and had a blood alcohol level three times the legal limit. Harris clipped the rear end of a vehicle in the right lane, swerved into oncoming traffic,<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/country-singer-kylie-rae-harris-was-drunk-speeding-deadly-new-n1096906|title=Country singer Kylie Rae Harris was drunk, speeding at over 100 mph before deadly crash|website=[[NBC News]]|date=December 6, 2019 |language=en|access-date=December 6, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.foxnews.com/entertainment/country-singer-kylie-rae-harris-drunk-speeding-fatal-crash-police|title=Country singer Kylie Rae Harris' alcohol level was 3 times legal limit, driving 102 mph at time of crash|website=Fox News|language=en|access-date=December 6, 2019|date=December 6, 2019}}</ref> and hit another car head-on.  The driver of the other car, 16-year-old Taos High School student Maria Elena Cruz, was also killed.<ref>{{cite news |title=Country singer Kylie Rae Harris caused \"senseless\" crash that killed her and teen, sheriff says |url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/kylie-rae-harris-crash-deadly-crash-cause-by-country-singer-taos-county-sheriff-says/ |accessdate=September 9, 2019 |website=[[CBS News]] |date=September 9, 2019}}</ref> Cruz's father, Deputy Chief Pedro Cruz of the San Cristobal Fire District, responded to the call not knowing his daughter had been involved in the accident.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Stimson |first=Brie |date=2019-09-08 |title=Kylie Rae Harris crash a shock for NM fire chief; learns his 16-year-old daughter also died |url=https://www.foxnews.com/entertainment/emt-responds-to-country-singers-fatal-crash-unaware-his-16-year-old-daughter-also-killed |access-date=2023-08-25 |website=Fox News |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nHarris had a drunk driving conviction from 2017. As part of her conviction, she was ordered to have an [[ignition interlock device]] installed in her car.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.foxnews.com/entertainment/kylie-rae-harris-dead-crash-speeding-sheriff|title=Kylie Rae Harris was driving 102 mph at time of fatal crash, authorities say|last=Sager|first=Jessica|date=September 23, 2019|website=[[Fox News]]|language=en-US|access-date=December 6, 2019}}</ref>{{Relevance inline|date=December 2019}}\n\n== References ==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Harris, Kylie Rae}}\n[[Category:1989 births]]\n[[Category:2019 deaths]]\n[[Category:21st-century American women singers]]\n[[Category:American country singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:American women country singers]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from New Mexico]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from Texas]]\n[[Category:Road incident deaths in New Mexico]]\n[[Category:Singer-songwriters from Texas]]\n[[Category:People from Wylie, Texas]]\n[[Category:21st-century American singer-songwriters]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Active since 2019, he has released two [[extended play]]s and charted one single through Combustion Music.\n\n==Biography==\nKolby Cooper was born in [[Bradford, Texas]]. He grew up listening to both [[outlaw country]] and [[grunge]], both of which inspired him to learn to play guitar and write songs. Although he initially wanted to be a football player, a high school classmate persuaded him to focus on music instead.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/2022/08/19/kolby-cooper-boy-anderson-county-moon-talks-new-album/10284329002/ | title=Kolby Cooper rides a country music silver lining 'From Anderson County to the Moon' | publisher=The Tennessean | date=August 19, 2022 | accessdate=April 10, 2023}}</ref>\n\nBy the time he finished high school, Cooper was married and had begun writing songs full-time. After entering some of his songs in local talent competitions, he released his debut single \"Every Single Kiss\" in 2017 followed by an [[extended play]] a year later. He continued to release songs through Combustion Music throughout the 2010s.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/kolby-cooper-mn0003961524/biography | title=Kolby Cooper biography | publisher=AllMusic | accessdate=April 10, 2023}}</ref>\n\nBy 2022, Cooper was signed to [[BBR Music Group]]'s Wheelhouse imprint, which sent the single \"Excuses\" to radio late in the year. He wrote the song with Brett Tyler and Jordan Walker.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://tasteofcountry.com/kolby-cooper-excuses/ | title=Kolby Cooper, 'Excuses' Explores the Frayed Emotions of a Breakup | publisher=Taste of Country | date=December 13, 2022 | accessdate=April 10, 2023}}</ref> It served as the lead single to Cooper's debut album, ''Boy from Anderson County to the Moon'', which was released on August 19, 2022.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/2022/08/19/kolby-cooper-boy-anderson-county-moon-talks-new-album/10284329002/|title=Kolby Cooper rides a country music silver lining 'From Anderson County to the Moon'|author=Marcus K. Dowling|date=August 19, 2022|publisher=The Tennessean|accessdate=May 25, 2023}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" border=\"1\"\n|+ List of albums, showing other relevant details\n! scope=\"col\" style=\"width:18em;\"| Title\n! scope=\"col\" style=\"width:20em;\"| Details\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| ''Boy from Anderson County to the Moon''\n|\n* Release: August 19, 2022\n* Label: [[BBR Music Group|Wheelhouse Records]]/Combustion\n* Formats: digital download, streaming\n|-\n|}\n\n===Singles===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\"| Year\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:14em;\"| Single\n! colspan=\"2\"| Peak chart<br />positions\n|- style=\"font-size:smaller;\"\n! width=\"45\"| [[Country Airplay|US Country Airplay]] \n|-\n| 2022\n! scope=\"row\"| \"Excuses\"\n| 35<ref>{{cite web | url=https://s3.amazonaws.com/bulletins.billboard.com/country/country_update_2023_0407.pdf | title=Billboard Country Update | publisher=Billboard | date=April 7, 2023 | accessdate=April 10, 2023}}</ref>\n|}\n\n==References==\n{{reflist}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Cooper, Kolby}}\n[[Category:American male singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:BBR Music Group artists]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from Texas]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:People from Anderson County, Texas]]\n[[Category:1999 births]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Keith_Gattis","to":"Keith Gattis"}],"pages":{"19570341":{"pageid":19570341,"ns":0,"title":"Keith Gattis","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country music singer-songwriter (1970\u20132023)}}\n{{More citations needed|date=April 2023}}\n{{Use American English|date=April 2023}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=April 2023}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Keith Gattis\n| background        = solo_singer\n| image             = \n| image_size        = \n| birth_name        = Quenton Keith Gattis\n| birth_date        = {{Birth date|1970|5|26}}\n| birth_place = [[Georgetown, Texas]], U.S.\n| origin = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| death_date        = {{Death date and age|2023|4|23|1970|5|26}}\n| genre             = [[Country music|Country]]\n| occupation        = {{hlist|Musician|songwriter|record producer}}\n| instrument        = {{hlist|Vocals|guitar}}\n| years_active      = 1996\u20132023\n| label             = [[RCA Records Nashville|RCA Nashville]]<br />Smith Music Group\n}}\n'''Quenton Keith Gattis''' (May 26, 1970 \u2013 April 23, 2023)<ref name=\"obiQKG\">{{cite web |url=https://www.springhillfh.com/obituaries/Quenton-Gattis/#!/Obituary|title=Quenton 'Keith' Gattis May 26, 1970 - April 23, 2023|date=|accessdate=April 28, 2023|website=Spring Hill Funeral Home & Cemetery}}</ref> was an American [[country music]] singer-songwriter, guitarist, and record producer. He released two studio albums and charted one single, \"Little Drops of My Heart\", on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs|Hot Country Singles & Tracks]] chart while signed to [[RCA Records Nashville|RCA Nashville]]. In 2002, Gattis joined [[Dwight Yoakam|Dwight Yoakam's]] band as band leader and lead electric guitar player and is credited on Yoakam's studio album ''[[Blame the Vain]]''. In 2005, Gattis released his record ''Big City Blues.''\n\nGattis collaborated on records with [[George Jones]], [[George Strait]], [[Kenny Chesney]], [[Willie Nelson]], [[Kid Rock]], [[Randy Houser]], [[Charlie Robison]], [[Gary Allan]], [[Ashley Monroe]], [[Allison Moorer]], [[Waylon Payne]], [[Miranda Lambert]], [[Wade Bowen]], [[Sara Evans]], [[Dwight Yoakam]], [[Brandy Clark]], [[Randy Rogers Band]], [[Randy Travis]], [[Eli Young Band]], and others.{{Citation needed|date=April 2023}}\n\n[[Kenny Chesney]] recorded two of Gattis' songs for his 2012 album ''[[Welcome to the Fishbowl]]''. One of the songs, \"[[El Cerrito Place]]\", previously on Gattis' ''Big City Blues'' record, was released by Chesney and charted as a ''Billboard'' top 20 single. \"El Cerrito Place\" was also recorded by [[Charlie Robison]] featuring [[Natalie Maines]]. Gattis co-wrote Chesney's 2013 single \"[[When I See This Bar]]\" from the album ''[[Life on a Rock]]'', and [[George Strait]]'s 2013 single \"[[I Got a Car]]\". Gattis had numerous film and television placements including songs in ''[[The Jacket]]'', ''[[Sicario (2015 film)|Sicario]]'', and ''[[Nashville (2012 TV series)|Nashville]]''. Gattis produced and co-wrote projects for many artists including [[Waylon Payne]], Kendell Marvel, [[Wade Bowen]], [[Randy Houser]], and [[Micky & the Motorcars]].{{Citation needed|date=April 2023}}\n\nGattis died in a tractor accident on April 23, 2023, at the age of 52.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://americansongwriter.com/country-music-artist-keith-gattis-dead-at-52/ |title=Country Music Artist Keith Gattis Dead at 52 |first=Tiffany |last=Goldstein |date=April 23, 2023 |website=[[American Songwriter]] |access-date=April 24, 2023}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/keith-gattis-nashville-songwriter-dead-obit-1234722344/|title=Songwriter Keith Gattis, Whose Songs Were Cut by Kenny Chesney and George Strait, Dead at 52|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=April 24, 2023|first=Joseph|last=Hodak}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Whiskey_Myers","to":"Whiskey Myers"}],"pages":{"36599558":{"pageid":36599558,"ns":0,"title":"Whiskey Myers","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|U.S. musical group}}\n{{More citations needed|date=December 2018}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Whiskey Myers\n| image_size        = \n| image             = Whiskey Myers .jpg\n| landscape         = yes\n| alt               = \n| caption           = \n| alias             = \n| origin            = [[East Texas]]\n| genre             = [[Rock music|Rock]], [[Southern rock]],[[Country]], [[hard rock]]\n| years_active      = 2007\u2013present\n| label             = Wiggy Thump Records\n| associated_acts   = \n| website           = [http://www.whiskeymyers.com www.whiskeymyers.com]\n| current_members   = Cody Cannon<br />Cody Tate<br />John Jeffers<br />Jeff Hogg<br />Tony Kent<br /> Jamey Gleaves\n| past_members      = Gary Brown\n}}\n\n'''Whiskey Myers''' is an American rock and roll band from [[Palestine, Texas]] composed of Cody Cannon (lead vocals and acoustic guitar), John Jeffers (lead guitar, slide guitar, lap steel guitar, vocals), Cody Tate (lead and rhythm guitar, vocals), Jeff Hogg (drums), Tony Kent (percussion/drums), and Jamey Gleaves (bass). They have released six albums, the latest being ''[[Tornillo_(album)|Tornillo]]'' released in July 2022.\n\n==Music career==\nIn 2008, the band released their debut album, ''Road of Life''.<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web |url={{Allmusic|class=artist|id=mn0001002713|pure_url=yes}} |title=Whiskey Myers Biography |last=Leggett |first=Steve |work=[[Allmusic]] |access-date=July 31, 2012}}</ref> Their second album, ''Firewater'', was released by Wiggy Thump in 2011 and debuted in the Top 30 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Top Country Albums]] chart, largely thanks to the single \"Ballad of a Southern Man\". On February 4, 2014, the album, ''Early Morning Shakes'', was released and received mostly positive reviews. In September 2016, their fourth album ''Mud'' was released. The band's self-titled album was released on September 27, 2019 followed by \"Tornillo\" in July 29, 2022.\n\nThe band started when friends Cody Cannon and John Jeffers began learning guitar together, inspired by the music of [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]], [[Hank Williams Jr.]], [[Waylon Jennings]], amongst many other artists. After being joined by Cannon's co-worker and friend Cody Tate. After playing together for a while, the three decided to start a more serious band. They enlisted friend Jeff Hogg to play drums, and asked Cannon's cousin Gary Brown to play bass (although he did not know how to play the instrument at the time). They began playing shows around their hometown and native state of Texas, slowly starting to build a following on the Texas/Red Dirt scene.\n\nIn 2018, the band was featured in four episodes of the [[Kevin Costner]] [[Paramount Network]] series [[Yellowstone (American TV series)|''Yellowstone'']]. Shortly afterwards, the band's three available albums moved into the top 10 iTunes country chart. Their most recent album at the time, ''Mud'', reached No. 1 on the charts, and its song \"Stone\" reached No. 9 in all genres. \n\nOn September 27, 2019, the band released the self-titled album, ''[[Whiskey Myers (album)|Whiskey Myers]]''. It debuted at No. 1 on ''Billboard'' Country,<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/8532434/whiskey-myers-no-1-top-country-albums |title=Whiskey Myers Scores First Top Country Albums No. 1, Jon Pardi & Sturgill Simpson Debut in Top 3|date=October 8, 2019 |first= Jim |last=Asker|magazine=Billboard }}</ref> No. 2 on ''Billboard'' active rock,<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/charts/hot-mainstream-rock-tracks|title= Mainstream Rock Songs |magazine=Billboard }}</ref> and No. 6 on the ''Billboard'' 200.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.entertainment-focus.com/music-section/ef-country/whiskey-myers-hit-billboard-200-top-10-with-new-self-titled-album/ |title=Whiskey Myers hit Billboard 200 Top 10 with new self-titled album |work=Entertainment Focus |date=15 October 2019 }}</ref>\n\n==Band members==\n<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.whiskeymyers.com/about|title=About - Whiskey Myers|access-date=June 29, Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Rob_Baird","to":"Rob Baird"}],"pages":{"34438582":{"pageid":34438582,"ns":0,"title":"Rob Baird","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n\n{{Use mdy dates|date=June 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Rob Baird\n<!-- Commented out because image was deleted: | image               = File:Rob_Baird_Picture2.jpg \n| image_size          = 250px |upright|-->\n| birth_name      =\n| alias           =\n| birth_date      =\n| birth_place     = [[Memphis, Tennessee]]\n| instrument      =\n| genre           = [[Americana (music)|Americana]]\n| occupation      = Singer-songwriter\n| years_active    = 2010\u2013present\n| label           = Carnival Recording Company, Hard Luck Recording Company\n| associated_acts =\n| website         = http://www.robbairdmusic.com/\n}}\n\n'''Rob Baird''' is an [[Americana (music)|Americana]] and [[country music]] singer-songwriter, producer, and musician<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.robbairdmusic.com/ |title=Home |website=robbairdmusic.com}}</ref> from [[Memphis, Tennessee]]. He released his debut album, ''Blue Eyed Angels'' (Carnival Recording Company),<ref>http://www.carnivalrecordingcompany.com/ {{Dead link|date=March 2022}}</ref> in 2010 and his sophomore effort, ''I Swear It's the Truth'', in May 2012. His third record, ''Wrong Side of The River,'' was released on May 13, 2016. His fourth album, ''After All'', was released on January 11, 2019. His fifth record, ''Anthems'', was released on May 19, 2022.\n\n==Biography==\n\nBaird relocated from [[Memphis, Tennessee]] to [[Fort Worth, Texas]] in 2005 to attend [[Texas Christian University]], where he earned a degree in Entrepreneurial Management. During his time at Texas Christian, at the age of 21, he recorded his debut project. The album ''Blue Eyed Angels'' was produced by Scott Davis and featured musicians from [[Hayes Carll]]'s band. That initial effort featured the singles, \"Fade Away\" (a top 5 single on the Texas Music Chart), \"Could Have Been My Baby,\" and the title track.\n\nIn 2012 Baird followed up ''Blue Eyed Angels'' with ''I Swear It's The Truth'', named one of the top twenty albums of the year by [[Spin Magazine]].<ref name=\"121217-19-rob-baird\">{{cite web| url = https://www.spin.com/2012/12/best-country-albums-2012/121217-19-rob-baird/| url-status = dead| archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20160326072337/http://www.spin.com/2012/12/best-country-albums-2012/121217-19-rob-baird/| archive-date = 2016-03-26| title = Rob Baird \u2013 I Swear It's the Truth (Carnival) SPIN}}</ref>  ''I Swear It's The Truth'' featured the hit single, \u201cDreams and Gasoline\u201d which was added to [[XM]]\u2019s \"[[The Highway (Sirius XM)|The Highway]]\" and was featured in the ABC drama ''[[Nashville (2012 TV series)|Nashville]]''. The video for the single was shot in [[Joshua Tree, CA]] and was supported by [[Country Music Television|CMT]] and their multiple platforms.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/rob-baird/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130613172933/http://www.cmt.com/artists/rob-baird/|url-status=dead|archive-date=June 13, 2013|title = Country Music \u2013 Music News, New Songs, Videos, Music Shows and Playlists from CMT}}</ref>\n\nIn 2013 Baird's \"More Than Willing\" was featured on [[Lifetime (TV network)|Lifetime]]'s ''[[Army Wives]]''. Three of his songs have also been used in season three of [[The CW|CW]]'s ''[[Hart of Dixie]]'' (\"Same Damn Thing\" in episode 10, \"More Than Willing\" in episode 17, and \"40 Days and 40 Nights\" in episode 20).\n\nOver the years, Baird has kept an active touring schedule balancing support slots with [[Jason Isbell]], [[Billy Joe Shaver]], [[The Steeldrivers]], [[Don Williams]], and many others with developing an impressive string of headlining dates in several major markets.\n\nBaird relocated to Austin, Texas in 2015 and recorded his third record, ''Wrong Side of the River,'' released on May, 13th, 2016 on Baird's label Hard Luck Recording Company. Produced by Brian Douglas Phillips, the album presents a stark contrast to some of Baird's previous work. ''Wrong Side of the River'' is laden with the blues of Memphis and the outlaw [[alt-country]].\n\nIn 2016 \"Mississippi Moon\" and \"Cowboy Clich\u00e9\" from ''Wrong Side of the River'' were featured on the Netflix original series ''The Ranch''.\n\nBaird's highly anticipated fourth record ''After All'' was released January 11, 2019.\n\n==Critical reception==\n\nRoughstock Country gave ''I Swear It's the Truth'' 4.5/5 stars, saying \"Everything about ''I Swear It's The Truth'' suggests a young artist ready to break into the big leagues.\"<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.roughstock.com/reviews/album-review-rob-baird-i-swear-it-s-the-truth |title=Album Review: Rob Baird - I Swear It's the Truth &#124; Country Music Reviews, Taylor Swift to Lady Antebellum &#124; Roughstock.com |access-date=June 19, 2014 |archive-date=April 15, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130415064019/http://www.roughstock.com/reviews/album-review-rob-baird-i-swear-it-s-the-truth |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\n[[Spin Magazine]] included ''I Swear It's the Truth'' on their \"Top Albums of 2012\" list, calling him a \"young, affable folk-pop charmer.\"<ref name=\"121217-19-rob-baird\"/>\n\nBaird was featured in ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]''{{'}}s \"Spotlight\" section in May 2012 covering the release of ''I Swear It's the Truth''.<ref>{{Cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/the-615/485451/spotlight-rob-baird-spreads-truth-with-new-album|title=Spotlight: Rob Baird Spreads 'Truth' with New Album|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|date=May 30, 2012}}</ref>\n\nIn 2015 the Dallas Observer slated Baird's \"Dreams and Gasoline\" to be one of the 50 best Texas Red Dirt Songs<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.dallasobserver.com/music/the-50-best-red-dirt-texas-country-songs-7055741|title=The 50 Best Red Dirt Texas Country Songs}}</ref>\n\nIn 2016, Baird premiered a three-part video series featuring songs from ''Wrong Side of The River'' on NPR, stating that the videos and the music were \"a thematic journey from defiance to reflection to the hope for redemption\".<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.npr.org/event/music/476464506/rob-baird-wrong-side-of-the-river-trilogy|title = First Watch: Rob Baird, 'Wrong Side of the River' Trilogy|newspaper = NPR|date = May 3, 2016|last1 = Sinnenberg|first1 = Jackson}}</ref> No Depression stated that ''Wrong Side of The River'' as \"Wrenching punches to the gut, with powerhouse blues rock and soul, as well as poignant pulls on our hearts with heart-rending ballads\".<ref>{{cite web |url=http://nodepression.com/article/rob-baird-has-run-good-luck |title=Rob Baird Has a Run of Good Luck {{!}} No Depression |website=nodepression.com |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160619155022/http://nodepression.com/article/rob-baird-has-run-good-luck |archive-date=2016-06-19}}</ref> Spin Magazine described ''Wrong Side of The River'' as \"Baird takes his traditional country to a deeper place, with sparse acoustic chords allowing his reflective lyricism to breathe\".<ref>{{Cite Robison"}],"pages":{"5949182":{"pageid":5949182,"ns":0,"title":"Charlie Robison","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American singer-songwriter (1964\u20132023)}}\n{{redirect|I Want You Bad|The Offspring song|Want You Bad}}\n{{for|the Australian television and radio presenter|Charli Robinson}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=December 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Charlie Robison\n| image             = Charlie Robison.jpg\n| caption           = Robison performing in 2007\n|alt = Robison playing guitar and singing\n| birth_name        = Charles Fitzgerald Robison\n| birth_date        = {{Birth date|1964|9|1}}\n| birth_place       = [[Houston, Texas]], U.S.\n| origin            = [[Bandera, Texas]], U.S.\n| death_date        = {{Death date and age|2023|9|10|1964|9|1}}\n| death_place       = [[San Antonio, Texas]], U.S.\n| genre             = [[Country music|Country]]\n| occupation        = Singer-songwriter\n| years_active      = 1996\u20132018, 2022\u20132023\n| label             = Viero<br />Lucky Dog<br />[[Columbia Records|Columbia]]<br />[[Dualtone Records|Dualtone]]\n| spouse            = {{marriage|[[Emily Strayer]]|1999|2008|end=div}}\n| website           = {{URL|charlierobison.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Charles Fitzgerald Robison''' (September 1, 1964 \u2013 September 10, 2023)<ref>{{Cite news |last=Andrew |first=Dansby |date=September 10, 2023 |title=Charlie Robison, Texas country singer-songwriter behind 'My Hometown,' dies at 59 |work=Houston Chronicle |url=https://www.houstonchronicle.com/entertainment/music/article/charlie-robison-dies-at-59-18358663.php |access-date=September 11, 2023}}</ref> was an American [[country music]] [[singer-songwriter]].\n\n==Career==\nAfter a knee injury at [[Southwest Texas State University]]<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/d/articlex.asp?xid=723&p=2|title=Charlie Robison steps right up \u2013 March 2001|website=Countrystandardtime.com}}</ref> ended a potential football career, Charlie Robison came to Austin, Texas in the late 1980s and had stints in the bands Chaparral, Millionaire Playboys, and Two Hoots and a Holler.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/robison_charlie/bio.jhtml|archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20040216034312/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/robison_charlie/bio.jhtml|archive-date = February 16, 2004|title = Country Music \u2013 Music News, New Songs, Videos, Music Shows and Playlists from CMT}}</ref> He went solo with his album \"Bandera\" in 1996. He subsequently signed with Sony and released \"Life of the Party\" on Sony's subsidiary Lucky Dog Records. The album gave him three of his biggest hits including \"My Hometown.\" His next release was a live disc called \"Unleashed Live,\" which is credited to Charlie, brother Bruce, and Jack Ingram. He then signed with Columbia Records for \"Step Right Up\" and another live album.\n\nIn 2003, Robison was a judge on the first season of the TV singing competition ''[[Nashville Star]]''.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.usanetwork.com/series/nashvillestar/theshow/characterprofiles/robison/index.html |title=USA Network &#124; Nashville Star - Character Profile: Charlie Robison - Judge |website=www.usanetwork.com |access-date=13 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20061113050913/http://www.usanetwork.com/series/nashvillestar/theshow/characterprofiles/robison/index.html |archive-date=13 November 2006 |url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nUnhappy with the expectations and limitations of being a Nashville country artist, he moved to a smaller independent label, Dualtone, for ''Good Times'' in 2004, followed by extensive touring and newfound control over his career. Accordingly, his sound began to evolve away from mainstream/Nashville country and toward more [[Southern rock|Southern]] and [[hard rock]] influences.\n\nFive years after the release of \"Good Times,\" Robison released ''Beautiful Day'' on June 23, 2009, on Dualtone. This was the first album he self-produced. Both albums featured several songs written by Nashville singer-songwriter Keith Gattis.\n\nHis song \"Good Times\" was featured in the credits of [[HBO]]'s original series ''[[True Blood]]'' in the first season's third episode.\n\nIn 2009, he embarked on an [[East Coast of the United States|East Coast]] tour with stops in Little Rock, Nashville, Atlanta, Raleigh, New York City, Philadelphia, Chicago, Minneapolis, Iowa City, and Memphis to promote ''Beautiful Day''. Since then he has played primarily in Texas, with occasional shows in Louisiana, Arkansas, Oklahoma, and Colorado.\n\nRobison was known for playing [[classic rock]] covers during his live shows.\n\nHis live band included Mark Tokach (lead guitar), Abe Combest (drums), Zeke Benenate (bass) J.C. Burt (steel guitar) and Chris Valdez (road manager and additional guitar). Prior to Beautiful Day, his band was known as The Enablers, and included Keith Robinson (drums), Scott Esbeck (bass) and Travis Woodard (drums). Other notable members have included Kim Deschamps (pedal & lap steel, mandolin and guitar from 2000\u20132009), Kevin Carroll (guitar), Jason Bryl (bass), Chris Grady (bass), Louis Landry (keyboards and accordion), and Kris Brown (bass). His recordings have also featured special guests Lloyd Maines (who produced \"Step Right Up\" and \"Good Times\"), Rich Brotherton, Charlie Sexton, and Natalie Maines (duet on \"The Wedding Song\" and harmony vocals on \"El Cerrito Place\").\n\nIn September 2014, Robison opened Alamo Icehouse in San Antonio, Texas, with former Major League Baseball player [[Brooks Kieschnick]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=Lucio |first=Valentino |date=September 13, 2014 |title=Downtown ice house & BBQ joint opens |url=https://blog.mysanantonio.com/food/2014/09/downtown-ice-house-bbq-joint-opens/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210412225612/https://blog.mysanantonio.com/food/2014/09/downtown-ice-house-bbq-joint-opens/ |archive-date=April 12, 2021 |website=Blog.mysanantonio.com}}</ref>\n\nOn September 24, 2018, Robison announced that due to complications from surgery, he was permanently unable to sing, and that he was officially retiring from stage and studio.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://tasteofcountry.com/charlie-robison-retirement-lost-voice-surgery/|title=Untitled|website=tasteofcountry.com|date=September 24, 2018}}</ref> Robison resumed his music career in 2022.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Trigger |date=2022-09-28 |title=Texas Country Legend Charlie Robison is Exploring a Comeback |url=https://www.savingcountrymusic.com/texas-country-legend-charlie-robison-is-exploring-a-comeback/ |access-date=2023-04-10 |website=Saving Country Music |language=en-US}}</ref> He returned to Billy Bob's as part of his first tour since 2018, playing at the same venue where he first played in 1999.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Charlie Robison |url=https://billybobstexas.com/events/charlie-robison |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230604032706/https://billybobstexas.com/events/charlie-robison |archive-date=June 4, 2023 |access-date=2023-04-10 |website=Billy Bob's Texas |language=en}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life and death==\nRobison's brother, [[Bruce Robison]], and his sister, Robyn Ludwick, are also singer-songwriters.\n\nRobison married [[Emily Robison|Emily Erwin]] of [[The Chicks]] at the [[Cibolo Creek Ranch]] in May 1999,<ref name=\"dixiechicksmemberwedsinwesttexas\">{{cite news|title=Dixie Chicks member weds in West Texas|url=https://www.newspapers.com/image/18936484/?terms=%22Cibolo%2BCreek%2BRanch%22|accessdate=February 16, 2016|work=The Kerrville Times|page=16|location=Kerrville, Texas|via=[[Newspapers.com]]|url-access=registration |quote=Emily Erwin of the Texas-born group married fellow Texan and musician Charlie Robison on Saturday at Cibolo Creek Ranch in the Big Bend.}}</ref> with whom he had three children. The couple divorced in August 2008.<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.mysanantonio.com/entertainment/music/Dixie_Chick_in_divorce_court.html |title=Dixie Chicks in divorce court |access-date=October 12, 2008 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080817030724/http://www.mysanantonio.com/entertainment/music/Dixie_Chick_in_divorce_court.html |archive-date=August 17, 2008 |url-status=dead }}</ref> He and his second wife had a son in February 2020.\n\nRobison died after suffering from [[cardiac arrest]] and other complications at a [[San Antonio, Texas]], hospital on September 10, 2023, at the age of 59.<ref>{{cite news|first=|last=|title=Country Singer-Songwriter Charlie Robison Dies at 59|url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/music-news/charlie-robison-dead-country-music-singer-songwriter-dies-1235586841/|access-date=September 11, 2023 |publisher=The Hollywood Reporter|date=September 10, 2023}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Great_Divide_(band)","to":"The Great Divide (band)"}],"pages":{"3418253":{"pageid":3418253,"ns":0,"title":"The Great Divide (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American Red Dirt music group}}\n{{More citations needed|date=September 2010}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=September 2022}}\n{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name             = The Great Divide\n| image            = The Great Divide promotional photo.jpg\n| caption          = The Great Divide, 1998\n| image_size       = <!-- Only for images narrower than 220 pixels -->\n| background       = group_or_band\n| alias            = \n| origin           = [[Stillwater, Oklahoma]], [[United States]]\n| genre            = [[Country music|Country]], [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]]\n| years_active     = 1992\u20132007, 2011 - Present\n| label            = Campfire<br/>[[Atlantic Records|Atlantic]]<br/>[[Broken Bow Records|Broken Bow]]\n| associated_acts  = \n| website          = https://www.tgdmusic.com\n                            https://www.facebook.com/thegreatdividemusic\n| current_members  = [[Mike McClure]]<br/>Scott Lester<br/>Kelley Green<br/>J. J. Lester<br/>Bryce Conway<br/>\n| past_members     = Micah Aills\n}}\n'''The Great Divide''' is an American [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]] music group, originally from [[Stillwater, Oklahoma]]. The Great Divide formed its own [[record label]], publishing company and operating company, and began recording. The group's first two albums, ''Goin' For Broke'' and ''Break In The Storm'', were independent releases. [[Atlantic Records]] signed the group and re-released ''Break In The Storm'' as well as the band's third album, ''Revolutions''. ''Remain'', the group's fifth album, was released independently at the end of 2002.\n\nThe Great Divide originally consisted of bassist Kelley Green, singer-songwriter [[Mike McClure]] and brothers Scott and J.J. Lester (rhythm guitar and drums, respectively). McClure left the band in early 2003 to pursue a career highlighting his originals and helping other bands record albums. The band continued with new singer Micah Aills but broke up after the release of \"Under Your Own Sun\" in 2005.<ref>{{cite news|first= Chip |last= Chandler |title= Great Divide makes amends, joins for reunion shows |date= February 8, 2012 |access-date= June 14, 2022 |url= \nhttps://www.amarillo.com/story/entertainment/local/2012/02/08/divide-makes-amends-joins-reunion-shows/13135190007/}}</ref>\n\nOn August 26, 2011, the original members reunited for an appearance and are still together today touring.<ref>{{cite news|first= Laurie |last= James |title= Bridging the Great Divide Seminal Red Dirt band reunites for Stillwater show |date= September 1, 2011 |access-date= June 14, 2022 |url= \nhttps://lonestarmusicmagazine.com/bridging-the-great-divide/}}</ref> The album \"25 Years of the Great Divide\", comprising 31 tracks, was released to celebrate their 25th anniversary in 2018. On August 26, 2022, the band released \"Good Side\" as a single from the \"Providence\" album. <ref>{{cite news|work= Vivascene |title= The Great Divide 'Providence' Album Preview |date= August 25, 2022 |access-date= September 7, 2022 |url= \nhttps://www.vivascene.com/the-great-divide-providence-album-preview/}}</ref> \"Good Side\" was recognized as the Texas County Music Association's single of the year for 2023. The same year The Great Divide was recognized as the band of the year.\n\nThe band made their debut on the [[Grand Ole Opry]] on July 10, 2024. The band opened with the song Never Could and played Mr. Devil.\n\n== Awards and achievements ==\n:2023 Country Band of the Year - Texas Country Music Association\n:2023 Single of the Year - Good Side - Texas County Music Association\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Steel_Woods","to":"The Steel Woods"}],"pages":{"55290108":{"pageid":55290108,"ns":0,"title":"The Steel Woods","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country music group}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = The Steel Woods\n| image            = Main Photo - Shot by @colecreasy.jpg\n| landscape        = yes\n| alt              = \n| caption          = Wes Bayliss, Tyler Powers and Johnny Stanton\n| alias            = \n| origin           = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], United States\n| genre            = {{hlist|[[Country music|Country]]|[[southern rock]]|[[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]]|[[Americana (music)|Americana]]}}\n| years_active     = 2016\u2013present\n| label            = {{hlist|Woods Music|[[Thirty Tigers]]}}\n| associated_acts  = {{flatlist|\n*[[Jamey Johnson]], [[Brent Cobb]]\n}}\n| website          = {{URL|http://thesteelwoods.com}}\n| current_members  = Wes Bayliss<br/>Johnny Stanton<br/>Tyler Powers<br/>\n| past_members     = Jason \"Rowdy\" Cope<br/>Jay Tooke\n}}\n'''The Steel Woods''' are an American [[country music]] group.<ref name=\":0\">{{Citation |date=May 9, 2017 |title=10 New Country Artists You Need to Know: May 2017 |magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/country/lists/10-new-country-artists-you-need-to-know-may-2017-w481172/steel-woods-w481175 |access-date=September 19, 2017 }}</ref> from [[Nashville, Tennessee]].<ref>{{Citation |last=Stroud |first=Scott |date=June 1, 2017 |title=Review: The Steel Woods honor southern rock tradition |publisher=[[Associated Press]] |url=http://www.news-sentinel.com/20170601/review-the-steel-woods-honor-southern-rock-tradition&profile=1042M |access-date= September 19, 2017}}</ref> Their debut album, ''Straw in the Wind'', was released in 2017.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.kmuw.org/post/steel-woods-plead-civility-old-news|title=The Steel Woods Plead For Civility With 'Old News'|last=Beaudoin|first=Jedd|website=www.kmuw.org|date=19 June 2019 |language=en|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref>\n\nThe band has cited influences such as [[Willie Nelson]], [[Waylon Jennings]] and [[Led Zeppelin]],<ref name=\":3\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.wideopencountry.com/artist-to-watch-the-steel-woods/|title=Band to Watch: The Steel Woods, One of Southern Rock's New Revivalists|last=Burchard|first=Jeremy|date=2017-05-17|website=Wide Open Country|language=en-US|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.popmatters.com/the-steel-woods-straw-in-the-wind-2495386212.html|title=The Steel Woods: Straw in the Wind|date=2017-07-19|website=PopMatters|language=en|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref> and have toured [[Opening act|in support]] of artists such as [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]], [[Dwight Yoakam]], [[Jamey Johnson]], [[Cody Jinks]], [[Miranda Lambert]], and [[Blackberry Smoke]].<ref name=\":2\">{{Cite web|url=https://bozone.com/interview-steel-woods-live-divide-eagles-bozeman-june-2019/|title=Interview: Steel Woods @ Live Divide/Eagles Bozeman \u2013 June 2019|date=2019-06-14|website=The BoZone|language=en-US|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref>\n\nFounding member and guitarist Jason \"Rowdy\" Cope died on January 16, 2021.<ref name=\"Hudak\">{{Cite magazine |last=Hudak |first=Joseph |date=2021-05-20 |title=The Metalhead Who Played Country Guitar |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/jason-rowdy-cope-steel-woods-all-of-your-stones-1172058/ |access-date=2022-09-10 |magazine=Rolling Stone |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n== History ==\nThe Steel Woods were cofounded by Wes Bayliss and Jason \"Rowdy\" Cope. Cope was the creative lead of the band as well as its [[lead guitar]]ist, songwriter and co-producer, while Bayliss is a multi-instrumentalist, lead singer and co-producer.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2019-02-04 |title=Hotstar: The Steel Woods Build A Career Show By Show - Pollstar News |url=https://news.pollstar.com/2019/02/04/hotstar-the-steel-woods-build-a-career-show-by-show/ |access-date=2022-09-12 |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nBayliss grew up in [[Woodland, Alabama]], playing music in his family's gospel band and learned to play harmonica, mandolin, and guitar. In 2007, he moved to [[Mobile, Alabama]], where he experimented further on different instruments. Cope began to learn guitar at the age of 11 in his hometown of [[Asheville, North Carolina]]. He later worked as a [[Los Angeles]]-based musician before moving to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] in 2007 and joined [[Jamey Johnson]]'s band. In his nine years with Johnson, Cope co-wrote \"Can't Cash My Checks\" and helped Johnson make the [[Grammy Award|Grammy]]-nominated \"[[That Lonesome Song]]\" (2008) and \"[[The Guitar Song]]\" (2010).<ref name=\":1\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.pisgahbrewing.com/shows/the-steel-woods/|title=The Steel Woods|last=Pisgah|first=Brewing|date=July 29, 2019|website=Pisgah Brewing|access-date=April 16, 2020|archive-date=April 8, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170408015228/http://www.pisgahbrewing.com/shows/the-steel-woods/|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn the early days of The Steel Woods, Bayliss and Cope spent a lot of time fishing and writing what would eventually evolve into the bands first studio album, ''Straw in the Wind'' (2017) released on [[Thirty Tigers]]/Woods Music. The album featured a guest vocal appearance by [[Lindi Ortega]], and [[Brent Cobb]] also contributed as a songwriter. On June 10, 2017, it reached number 42 on the [[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] Independent Albums chart.<ref>{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/charts/independent-albums/2017-06-09|title=Independent Albums Chart|magazine=Billboard|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref>\n\nIn the subsequent years, the band toured with fellow [[Southern rock]] artists [[Cody Johnson]], [[Cody Jinks]], [[Whiskey Myers]], and [[Blackberry Smoke]] as well as inspirations such as [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]] and [[Miranda Lambert]].<ref name=\":4\">{{Cite web |title=The Steel Woods \u2013 MoxieTalk with Kirt Jacobs |url=https://moxietalk.com/episodes/thesteelwoods/ |access-date=2020-04-16 |website=MoxieTalk |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nThey recorded their second album, ''Old News'', in [[Asheville, North Carolina|Asheville]] at the site of an old church during a break in their touring schedule. The album was released on January 18, 2019.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://glidemagazine.com/218932/southern-rockers-the-steel-woods-take-a-big-leap-forward-with-riveting-old-news-album-review/ | title=Southern Rockers The Steel Woods Take a Big Leap Forward|website=glidemagazine.com| date=17 January 2019|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref>\n\nCope died in January 2021.<ref name=\"Hudak\"/> The band's third album, ''All of Your Stones'', was released in May 2021.<ref name=\"ASAOYS\">{{cite web|url=https://americansongwriter.com/review-the-steel-woods-new-album-is-sadly-a-final-testament-to-its-late-co-founder/|title=Review: The Steel Woods' New Album Is Sadly A Final Testament To {{sic|I|t's|nolink=y}} Late Co-Founder|work=[[American Songwriter]]|last=Horowitz|first=Hal|date=May 12, 2021|access-date=May 14, 2021}}</ref>\n\nOn March 28, 2024, Wes Bayliss announced that after the completion of a final United States tour throughout 2024, The Steel Woods would disband, citing personal reasons to end the band and cancelling a scheduled autumn 2024 UK and European tour with fellow Southern rockers [[Blackberry Smoke]].<ref>{{Cite web |title=The Steel Woods Announce They\u2019ll Stop Touring At The End Of 2024 |url=https://www.msn.com/en-us/music/news/the-steel-woods-announce-they-ll-stop-touring-at-the-end-of-2024/ar-BB1kH9nY |access-date=2024-03-29 |website=www.msn.com}}</ref>\n\n==Personnel ==\n* Wes Bayliss \u2013 guitar and vocals\n* Jason Cope \u2013 guitar (d. 2021) \n* Johnny Stanton \u2013 bassist\n* Tyler Powers \u2013 guitar\n* Isaac Senty - drummer\n\n==Discography==\n'''Albums'''\n*''Straw in the Wind'' (2017)\n*''Old News'' (2019)\n*''All of Your Stones'' (2021)<ref name=\"ASAOYS\"/>\n*On Your Time (2023)\n\n==See also==\n* [[List of country music performers]]\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* [https://open.spotify.com/artist/69B1gu9EjC0rNb59YYNVPM Spotify]\n* [https://itunes.apple.com/us/artist/the-steel-woods/1073094331?ign-gact=3&ls=1 Apple Music] \n* [https://www.pandora.com/station/play/4477864228065669439 Pandora]\n* [https://play.google.com/music/listen#/wst/artist/A46com75qthwwdnm4wr2arjlvci Google Play Music]\n* {{Discogs artist|The Steel Woods}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Steel Woods, The}}\n[[Category:American country rock groups]]\n[[Category:Musical groups established in 2016]]\n[[Category:2016 establishments in Tennessee]]\n[[Category:Musical groups from Nashville, Tennessee]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Flatland_Cavalry","to":"Flatland Cavalry"}],"pages":{"52778873":{"pageid":52778873,"ns":0,"title":"Flatland Cavalry","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country and Americana band}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Flatland Cavalry\n| image           =\n| image_size      =\n| landscape       =\n| alt             =\n| caption         =\n| origin          = [[Lubbock, Texas|Lubbock]], [[Texas]]\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]], [[Americana (music)|americana]], [[folk rock]], [[Texas country music|Texas country]]\n| years_active    = 2012\u2013present\n| label           =\n| associated_acts =\n| website         = https://www.flatlandcavalry.com/\n| current_members = Cleto Cordero<br />Reid Dillon<br />Wesley Hall<br />Jonathan Saenz<br />Jason Albers<br />Adam Gallegos\n| past_members    = Laura Jane\n}}\n\n'''Flatland Cavalry''' is a [[country music|country]] and [[Americana (music)|Americana]] band from [[Lubbock, Texas]].<ref name=\":0\">{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/flatland-cavalry-mn0003425378/biography|title=Flatland Cavalry|publisher=Allmusic|accessdate=January 5, 2017}}</ref>  The band's original members were vocalist Cleto Cordero, drummer Jason Albers, bassist Jonathan Saenz, guitarist Reid Dillon, and violinist Laura Jane. Jane departed the band in July 2018 and was replaced by Wesley Hall.<ref name=\":1\">{{cite web | url=https://www.savingcountrymusic.com/fiddle-player-laura-jane-houle-leaves-flatland-cavalry/ | title=Fiddle Player Laura Jane Houle Leaves Flatland Cavalry | publisher=Saving Country Music | date=July 31, 2018 | accessdate=November 19, 2018}}</ref><ref name=\"koke\">{{cite web | url=http://kokefm.com/flatland-cavalry-announce-homeland-insecurity/ | title=Flatland Cavalry Announce 'Homeland Insecurity' | publisher=KOKE FM | accessdate=19 November 2018}}</ref>\n\nFlatland Cavalry was formed in 2012 by Cordero and Albers, who were college roommates in [[Midland, Texas|Midland]] and performed together before moving to Lubbock, where the rest of the members came together by 2014.<ref name=\"lo\">{{cite web|url=http://lubbockonline.com/go/music/2015-05-07/flatland-cavalry-performing-cd-release-party-thursday-blue-light|title=Flatland Cavalry performing CD release party Thursday at the Blue Light |publisher=Lubbock Online|date=May 7, 2015|accessdate=January 5, 2017}}</ref><ref name=\"kcbd\">{{cite web|url=http://www.kcbd.com/story/31672180/lubbock-band-flatland-cavalry-rises-to-no-2-on-itunes-country-chart|title=Lubbock band Flatland Cavalry rises to No. 2 on iTunes Country Chart|publisher=KCBD|date=April 7, 2016|accessdate=January 5, 2017}}</ref>  In May 2015, the band's debut [[extended play|EP]], titled ''Come May'', was released after a [[crowd-funding]] campaign was used to finance its production.<Ref name=\"lo\"/>  On April 1, 2016, their first full-length album, ''Humble Folks'', was released<ref name=\"kcbd\"/> to positive reviews and comparisons to the music of the [[Turnpike Troubadours]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://lonestarmusicmagazine.com/8906-2/|title=Flatland Cavalry: \"Humble Folks\"|publisher=Lone Star Music Magazine|date=April 4, 2016|accessdate=January 5, 2017}}</ref>  ''Humble Folks'' peaked at number 17 on the Billboard Americana/Folk albums chart<ref name=\":2\">{{cite web|url=http://www.billboard.com/artist/7327275/flatland-cavalry/chart?f=1071|title=Flatland Cavalry - Chart History (American/Folk albums)|publisher=Billboard|accessdate=January 5, 2017}}</ref> and number 38 on the Top Country Albums chart.<ref name=\":3\">{{cite web|url=http://www.billboard.com/artist/7327275/flatland-cavalry/chart?f=320|title=Flatland Cavalry - Chart History (Top Country Albums)|publisher=Billboard|accessdate=January 5, 2017}}</ref>  The band's second studio album, ''Homeland Insecurity'', was released on January 18, 2019.<ref name=\"koke\"/>\n\n[[Kaitlin Butts]], who is married to Cordero and an accomplished musician in her own right, is a frequent collaborator with the band and a oft-seen part of their live shows. <ref>{{Cite web|title=Shots with the Band Featuring Kaitlin Butts & Cleto Cordero of Flatland Cavalry {{!}}|url=http://texasmusicpickers.com/shots-with-the-band-featuring-kaitlin-butts-cleto-cordero-of-flatland-cavalry/|access-date=2021-01-20|language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n== Formation ==\nThe roots for the formation of Flatland Cavalry were first laid when Cleto Cordero and Jason Albers began playing at local venues while rooming together at [[Midland College]].<ref name=\":5\">{{Cite web|url=http://www.midlandlivingmagazine.com/2019/05/28/200570/flatland-cavalry-takes-texas-by-storm|title=Flatland Cavalry takes Texas by Storm {{!}} Midland Living|last=|first=|date=|website=Midland Living|language=en|archive-url=|archive-date=|access-date=2019-10-30}}</ref><ref name=\":0\" /> The two had been jamming together since junior high but it was not until they moved to Lubbock in 2012 that the band began to take shape. It was here, while studying at [[Texas Tech University]], that the duo met Laura Jane at a house party. Jonathan Saenz and Reid Dillon joined the rest in 2014 and the band's lineup was complete.<ref name=\":5\" /><ref name=\":0\" />\n\nCordero himself began playing the guitar at age 14 and wrote his first song by the time he was 17 years old for Lee High School's Rebel Lee Court Awards Ceremony.<ref name=\":5\" /> He writes most of the band's songs apart from playing the role of lead guitarist and singer with Jason Albers on drums, Jonathan Saenz on bass, Reid Dillon on guitar and Wesley Hall on fiddle. Hall took the place of Laura Jane when she parted ways with the band in 2018.<ref name=\":1\" /><ref name=\"koke\" />\n\n== Discography ==\n\n=== EPs ===\n\n==== ''Come May'' (2015) ====\nThe band released its first EP in 2015, gathering funds for its production via a crowdfunding platform.<ref name=\"lo\" /> The band reached its goal of $5,000 in just eight days, a testament to the fan following they had already mustered through live performances.<ref name=\"lo\" />\n\n'''Track list'''<ref name=\":6\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.flatlandcavalry.com/listen|title=LISTEN|website=Flatland Cavalry|language=en-US|access-date=2019-10-30}}</ref>\n# \"No Shade of Green\"\n# \"Love Me in the Water\"\n# \"Summertime Love\"\n# \"Missing You\"\n# \"Ain't Over You Yet\"\n\n==== ''Songs To Keep You Warm'' (EP) (2022) ====\n\n'''Track list'''<ref name=\":6\" />\n# \"Mountain Song\"\n# \"Damaged Goods\"\n# \"How Long\" (feat. Kaitlin Butts)\n# \"Parallel\" (feat. Ashley Monroe)\n# \"If We Said Goodbye\"\n# \"Show Me Now Which Way To Go\"\n\n=== Albums ===\n\n==== ''Humble Folks'' (2016) ====\nIt was the release of its debut EP followed by its first album, ''Humble Folks'', in 2016 that really got the ball rolling, with music insiders comparing Flatland to the likes of the [[Turnpike Troubadours]], lauding the band for its youthful blend of country, folk, Americana and rock. ''Humble Folks'' peaked at #38 on the Billboard Country Music Top 100 chart and #17 on the American/Folk Albums chart.<ref name=\":2\" /><ref name=\":3\" />\n\n'''Track list'''<ref name=\":6\" />\n# \"One I Want\"\n# \"A Good Memory\"\n# \"February Snow\"\n# \"Tall City Blues\"\n# \"Coyote (The Ballad of Roy Johnson)\"\n# \"Devil Off My Back\"\n# \"Stompin' Grounds\"\n# \"Goodbye Kiss\"\n# \"A Life Where We Work Out\" (feat. Kaitlin Butts)\n# \"Traveler's Song\"\n# \"Humble Folks\"\n\n==== ''Homeland Insecurity'' (2019) ====\nIn 2018, Laura Jane left the band and was soon replaced by Wesley Hall on fiddle.<ref name=\":1\" /> With the new lineup in place, the quintet released their second album, ''Homeland Insecurity'', in 2019; three years after the release of their debut.<ref name=\":4\">{{Cite web|url=https://eventseeker.com/artist/63269-flatland-cavalry|title=Flatland Cavalry - Artist Profile|last=|first=|date=|website=eventseeker.com|language=en|archive-url=|archive-date=|access-date=2019-10-30}}</ref> In the time that lapsed between the two, the band toured extensively, honing their skill as musicians and drawing on their experiences to craft their sophomore work.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://sixshootercountry.com/2019/01/22/flatland-cavalry-homeland-insecurity-review/|title=Flatland Cavalry - Homeland Insecurity {{!}} Review|date=2019-01-22|website=Six Shooter Country|language=en-GB|access-date=2019-10-30}}</ref> As the band's primary songwriter, Cordero penned lyrics for ''Homeland Insecurity'' are markedly more sophisticated than his previous songs. The album was widely well-received and praised for its distinctive sound.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.texasmusicpickers.com/homeland-insecurity-by-flatland-cavalry-was-well-worth-the-wait/|title=\"Homeland Insecurity\" by Flatland Cavalry was Well Worth the Wait|website=Texas Music Pickers|language=en-US|access-date=2019-10-30}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.savingcountrymusic.com/album-review-flatland-cavalrys-homeland-insecurity/|title=Album Review \u2013 Flatland Cavalry's \"Homeland Insecurity\"|first=|date=2019-01-23|website=Saving Country Music|language=en-US|archive-url=|archive-date=|access-date=2019-10-30}}</ref>\n\n'''Track list'''<ref name=\":6\" />\n# \"Come Back Down\"\n# \"Honeywine\"\n# \"Old School\"\n# \"Other Side of Lonesome\"\n# \"Back to Me\"\n# \"Living by Moonlight\"\n# \"Ashes\"\n# \"Lonely Then\"\n# \"Pretty Women\"\n# \"Sleeping Alone\"\n# \"Years from Now\"\n\n==== ''Welcome to Countryland'' (2021) ====\n\n'''Track list'''<ref name=\":6\" />\n# \"Country Is...\"\n# \"Some Things Never Change\"\n# \"A Cowboy Knows How\"\n# \"Gettin' By\"\n# \"Well-Spent Time\"\n# \"Life Without You\" (feat. Kaitlin Butts)\n# \"No Ace In the Hole\"\n# \"It's Good To Be Back ('Round Here Again)\"\n# \"Tilt Your Chair Back\"\n# \"Fallen Star\"\n# \"Daydreamer\"\n# \"Dancin' Around a Fire\"\n# \"Off Broadway\"\n# \"...Meantime\" (feat. Hailey Whitters)\n\n====''Wandering Stars'' (2023)====\n\nThe Texan country-Americana band announced the release of their fourth studio album, \u201cWandering Star\u201d on Oct, 27th 2023.<ref name=\":7\">{{Cite web |date=2023-11-01 |title=Flatland Cavalry Announces Fourth Studio LP: \"Wandering Star\" {{!}} TicketTaper Presale Codes, Concert Ticket, Tour Dates, Concert News |url=https://tickettaper.com/flatland-cavalry-announces-fourth-studio-lp-wandering-star/ |access-date=2023-11-01 |website=tickettaper.com |language=en-US}}</ref> The album, is their first release on Interscope Records, which follows their successful 2022 EP, \u201cSongs To Keep You Warm\u201d. \u201cWandering Star\u201d consists of 13 solo tracks and one collaborative track featuring Kaitlin Butts.<ref name=\":7\" />\n\n'''Track list<ref name=\":7\" />'''\n# \"The Provider\"\n# \"The Best Days\"\n# \"Only Thing At All\"\n# \"Last American Summer\"\n# \"Mornings With You\" (feat. Kaitlin Butts)\n# \"Let It Roll\"\n# \"Spinnin\u2019\"\n# \"Don\u2019t Have To Do This Like That\"\n# \"New American Dream\"\n# \"Oughta See You (The Way I Do)\"\n# \"A Thousand Miles An Hour\"\n# \"Burned Out Flame\"\n# \"Forgotten\"\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n[[Category:Country music groups from Texas]]\n[[Category:Musical groups from Lubbock, Texas]]\n[[Category:Musical groups established in 2012]]\n[[Category:2012 establishments in Texas]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Randy_Rogers_Band","to":"Randy Rogers Band"}],"pages":{"12975509":{"pageid":12975509,"ns":0,"title":"Randy Rogers Band","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{redirect|Randy Rogers|the Bahamian football manager|Randy Rogers (football manager)}}\n{{short description|American country music band}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Randy Rogers Band\n| background          = group_or_band\n| image               =Randy Rogers Band (cropped).jpg\n| caption           = Randy Rogers Band in 2009\n| landscape = yes\n| alt = An image of the Randy Rogers Band in concert\n| origin              = [[San Marcos, Texas]], United States\n| genre               = [[Texas country music|Texas country]], [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]], [[country music|country]]\n| years_active        = 2000-present\n| label               = [[Universal Music Group Nashville|Mercury Nashville]]<br />[[Universal Music Group Nashville|MCA Nashville]]<br />[[Thirty Tigers]]\n| website             = http://randyrogersband.com\n| current_members     = Randy Rogers <br />Brady Black<br />Geoffrey Hill<br />Les Lawless<br />Jon Richardson<br />Todd Stewart\n}}\n'''Randy Rogers Band''' is an American [[country music]] band from [[San Marcos, Texas]]. The band is composed of Randy Rogers (lead vocals), Geoffrey Hill (guitar), Jon Richardson (bass guitar), Brady Black (fiddle), Les Lawless (drums), and Todd Stewart (guitar, fiddle, mandolin, keyboards).<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web |url={{AllMusic|class=artist|id=p285190|pure_url=yes}} |title=allmusic ((( Randy Rogers > Overview ))) |access-date=2007-08-27 |last=Brown |first=Marisa |work=Allmusic}}</ref> They have recorded seven studio albums and two live albums, and have charted seven singles on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] charts.\n\n==Biography==\nRandy Rogers was born in [[Cleburne, Texas]]. At the age of 6 years, he learned to play the piano from his grandmother, and later started playing the guitar.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.thisistexasmusic.com/profiles/randyrogersband.html |title=Randy Rogers Band profile |access-date=2007-08-27 |work=ThisIsTexasMusic.com}}</ref>\n\nThe Randy Rogers Band recorded its debut album, ''Live at Cheatham Street Warehouse'', at a music hall of the same name in [[San Marcos, Texas]].<ref name=\"allmusic\"/><ref name=\"lonestar\">{{cite web |url=http://www.randyrogersband.com/band.php |title=Randy Rogers Band biography |access-date=2007-08-27 |work=Randyrogersband.com}}</ref> By 2002, the band was signed to the independent Downtime record label, on which they released the album ''Like It Used to Be''.  It was around this time that the band began performing outside of San Marcos, primarily at Nutty Brown Cafe and Amphitheatre in nearby Dripping Springs, Texas. Two years later, the album ''Rollercoaster'' was released, producing two minor entries on the ''Billboard'' [[Hot Country Songs]] charts in early 2005.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> Rogers also co-wrote \"Somebody Take Me Home\", a song recorded by [[Kenny Chesney]], on his 2005 album, ''[[The Road and the Radio]]''. Several of the songs on ''Rollercoaster'' were co-written by [[Radney Foster]], who also co-produced the album.<ref name=\"lonestar\"/> ''[[Just a Matter of Time (Randy Rogers Band album)|Just a Matter of Time]]'', the band's first major-label album, was released on [[Universal Music Group Nashville|Mercury Nashville Records]] in 2006.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> The band also released their self-titled album on September 23, 2008, also on Mercury Nashville Records. The first single \"In My Arms Instead\", was released in August.\n\nThe band's fifth album, ''[[Burning the Day]],'' was released on  August 24, 2010, on [[Universal Music Group Nashville|MCA Nashville]]. The album's first single was \"Too Late for Goodbye.\" It debuted at 55 on the U.S. ''Billboard'' [[Hot Country Songs]] chart and after four weeks on the chart, it peaked at 47.\n\n\"One More Sad Song\" was released in late 2012. The song became the band's first Billboard Top 40 hit, and the first single from their sixth album, ''[[Trouble (Randy Rogers Band album)|Trouble]]''.\n\n''Dreamer: A Tribute to Kent Finlay'', released in 2016 on Austin-based Eight 30 Records, features Randy Rogers and Sunny Sweeney's duet \"Between You and Me\".\n\n==Pop Culture==\nRandy Rogers Band and their song \u201cSpeak of the Devil\u201d referenced in Showtime TV series ''Billions'' (\u201cSTD\u201d 21:04). \n\n== Discography ==\n=== Studio albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Zane_Williams","to":"Zane Williams"}],"pages":{"17119056":{"pageid":17119056,"ns":0,"title":"Zane Williams","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American country music singer (born 1977)}}\n{{Use American English|date = September 2019}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name = Zane Williams\n| image = Zane Williams.jpg\n| caption = Williams performing in 2019\n| background = solo_singer\n| birth_place = [[Abilene, Texas]]\n| occupation = Singer-songwriter\n| genre = [[Country music|Country]]\n| instrument = Vocals, guitar, accordion\n| label = Hack Circle, Be Music, Texas Like That Records, Hill Country Music LLC\n| associated_acts= [[Jason Michael Carroll, The Wilder Blue, Cody Johnson, Pat Green, Luke Combs, Brent Cobb]]\n}}\n'''Zane Williams''' (born 1977) is an American [[country music]] singer. He has seven solo albums and is also a member of the Americana band \u201cThe Wilder Blue\u201d.\n\n==Career==\nZane Williams is an anomaly in today's country music scene, a modern-day \u201cthrowback\u201d who is equal parts bar-room entertainer and introspective poet.  Williams was a finalist in three categories at [[MerleFest]]'s Chris Austin Song Contest, claiming top slots in both the Country and General categories. \"Hurry Home\" was also selected as the $20,000 Maxell Song of the Year in the [[John Lennon Songwriting Contest]].<ref>[http://www.jlsc.com/winners/2005b/lennon_awards.php John Lennon Song Contest website Page for 2005 winners]. In 2006, Zane won Best Folk Award at the 2nd Annual IAMA (International Acoustic Music Awards) with his song \"Hurry Home\". Accessed October 5, 2009.</ref><ref>July 18, 2006, \"MACY GRAY GIVES CASH AWAY: Singer combines with NAMM to encourage aspiring musicians.\" Found at [http://emol.org/emclub/?q=macygrayhurryhomecd Entertainment Magazine website] and [http://www.eurweb.com/story/eur27523.cfm EurWeb website]{{dead link|date=July 2016 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}.  Both accessed October 5, 2009.</ref> Williams released the album ''Hurry Home'' in 2006. He signed a publishing deal with Big Yellow Dog Music in 2007. The album's [[Hurry Home|title track]] was released as a [[single (music)|single]] by [[Jason Michael Carroll]] in 2009.\n\nWilliams has toured extensively throughout the United States, including [[Missouri]],<ref>Shane Miller, \"Award winning artist to visit final Coffeehouse: Zane Williams has found more than fortune in his songwriting,\" November 11, 2006, ''The Mirror'' of [[Drury University]], found at [http://media.www.drurymirror.com/media/storage/paper740/news/2006/11/20/Life/Award.Winning.Artist.To.Visit.Final.Coffeehouse-2467992.shtml Drury Mirror website]{{dead link|date=July 2016 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}. Accessed October 5, 2009.</ref> [[Alabama]], and [[Texas]].<ref>[http://www.houseofwally.com/zw.htm House of Wally website with recent 2009 tour dates] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100505205059/http://www.houseofwally.com/zw.htm |date=May 5, 2010 }}. Accessed October 5, 2009.</ref>\n\nIn January 2010, Williams released an album titled ''The Right Place'', which he co-produced with [[Radney Foster]]. Jessica Phillips of ''[[Country Weekly]]'' magazine gave the album three-and-a-half stars out of five, saying, \"If you're in the mood for true honky-tonk music, you're in the right place.\"<ref>{{Cite journal|last=Phillips|first=Jessica|date=January 18, 2010|title=Reviews|journal=[[Country Weekly]]|volume=17|issue=3|page=54|issn=1074-3235}}</ref> ''Ride with Me'' followed in 2011.\n\nWilliams has received radio airplay on country stations across Texas that led to his first entry on the Texas Music Chart with \"Ride With Me\", from the 2011 album with the same title. He is also one of the featured artists on ''Troubadour Texas'', a television show documenting his rising career.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://troubadourtx.com/ |title=TroubadourTX Home |website=troubadourtx.com |access-date=14 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110128080732/http://troubadourtx.com/ |archive-date=28 January 2011 |url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn June 2013, Williams released an album titled ''Overnight Success''. He wrote all 11 songs on the album, and co-produced it with Tom Faulkner.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.musicnewsnashville.com/zane-williams-releases-overnight-success-single-to-radio |title=Zane Williams Releases \"Overnight Success\" Single to Radio |publisher=Music News Nashville |date=July 30, 2013 |access-date=January 27, 2014}}</ref> The album debuted on the ''Billboard'''s Heatseekers South Central chart at No. 4.  The video for the title track was on CMT Pure's 12-Pack Countdown for three weeks in a row and peaked at No.&nbsp;2. The video has also been featured on GAC's daily countdown along with The Nashville Network featuring William's \"Overnight Success\" music video in their Top 10 Rising Stars.{{Citation needed|date=January 2014}}\n\n===2015: ''Texas Like That''===\nIn 2015 Williams released another studio album, ''Texas Like That'', complete with 10 new self penned songs. The tracks in the album ranged from the romantic ballad \"She Is\" to the toe-tapping \"Just Gettin\u2019 Started\", and the fan tribute song \"Here\u2019s to You\".  Among the stronger tunes are \u201cJayton and Jill\u201d and the \"Kansas City Sunrise\".\n\n''Texas Like That'' was released on April 14, 2015, and debuted on Top Country Albums chart at No. 31 and Heatseeker Albums at No.8, his highest-charting album thus far, with 1,500 copies sold in its debut week.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://roughstock.com/news/2015/04/34486-country-album-chart-report-april-22-2015/ |title=Country Album Chart Report For April 22, 2015 |author= Matt Bjorke |date= April 22, 2015 |work=Roughstock }} Sales figure given [https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1bOYOZyLEOdMwI1iscGxXl8JaU5jEgdvt0SqHCgqAB_8/edit#gid=0 here]</ref>\n\n===2016: ''Bringin' Country Back''===\nIn 2016, the title track from his next album, ''Bringin' Country Back'', was released on July 8, 2016, as a single.  Williams wrote all eleven songs on the album, and produced the entire album himself.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.texasmusicpickers.com/single-spotlight-zane-williams-bringin-country-back/ |title=Single Spotlight: Zane Williams \u2013 Bringin' Country Back |date=August 10, 2016 |author=Chris Fox|work=Texas Music Pickers }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.wideopencountry.com/zane-williams-announces-bringin-country-back/ |title=Zane Williams Announces 'Bringin' Country Back' Album and Tour Dates |author=Jeremy Burchard |work=Wide Open Country |date=July 16, 2016}}</ref>  The album was released on October 21, 2016.  The album debuted at No. 46 on the Top Country Album chart, and No. 22 on the Heatseekers Album, with 800 copies sold in its debut week.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://roughstock.com/news/2016/10/41023-top-10-country-albums-chart-october-31-2016 |title=Top 10 Country Albums Sales Chart: October 31, 2016 |first= Matt |last=Bjorke |date= October 30, 2016 |work=Roughstock }}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n!
