Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Lindi_Ortega","to":"Lindi Ortega"}],"pages":{"24264834":{"pageid":24264834,"ns":0,"title":"Lindi Ortega","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|Canadian musician}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=August 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name             = Lindi Ortega\n| birth_date       = {{Birth date and age|1979|5|28}}\n| image            = Lindi Ortega Paris 2012.jpg\n| caption          = Ortega performing in Paris, France<br />February 24, 2012\n| Size             =\n| birth_place = [[Toronto]], [[Ontario]], Canada\n| origin = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| background       = solo_singer\n| instrument       = Vocals, guitar, piano\n| genre            = [[Country music|Country]]<!--Keep it simple to avoid disputes over genre-->\n| occupation       = Musician, songwriter\n| years_active     = 2000\u2013present\n| label            = Shadowbox Music\n| website          = {{URL|http://www.lindiortega.ca/|lindiortega.ca}}\n}}\n\n'''Lindi Marie Ortega'''<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ascap.com/repertory#/ace/search/workID/887077654 |title=ALL THESE CATS (PROMO) |website=ASCAP |publisher=American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers |access-date=March 13, 2023}}</ref> (born May 28, 1979) is a Canadian [[country music|country]] singer-songwriter from [[Toronto, Ontario]], who  had lived in [[Nashville, Tennessee]] then moved to [[Western Canada]] in 2017. She spent nearly a decade as an independent artist in the Toronto music scene,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.livingroomny.com/artist/lindi-ortega |title=Lindi Ortega |publisher=The Living Room |accessdate=September 7, 2009 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110721035321/http://www.livingroomny.com/artist/lindi-ortega |archivedate=July 21, 2011 }}</ref> releasing two albums and an EP in that time. She has been described as \"Toronto's best kept secret\"<ref name=\"Oxyfication 2007\"/> and nicknamed \"Indie Lindi\".<ref name=\"Oxyfication 2005\">{{cite web|url=http://www.oxyfication.net/featured/lindi-ortega/ |title=Lindi Ortega |publisher=oxyfication.com |date=October 25, 2005 |accessdate=June 28, 2010 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110724001302/http://www.oxyfication.net/featured/lindi-ortega/ |archivedate=July 24, 2011 }}</ref> Ortega left Last Gang management and records in November 2017. She has since released Til The Goin' Gets Gone EP and her full-length Liberty on her own label Shadowbox Music. Her voice has been described as a blend of [[Dolly Parton]]'s, [[Johnny Cash]]'s, and [[Emmylou Harris]]'.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.urchicago.com/blog/review-lindi-ortega-the-drifter-ep |title=REVIEW: Lindi Ortega \u2013 The Drifter EP |publisher=UR Chicago Online Magazine |last=Miller |first=Neil Jr.|accessdate=September 7, 2009 }}{{dead link|date=December 2017 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref>\n\nAt the end of 2010 and beginning of 2011, Ortega toured extensively as a backup singer for [[Brandon Flowers]], the lead singer of [[the Killers]], in support of his solo album, ''Flamingo''. The tour included dates in the United States, the United Kingdom, Germany, France, Italy, Spain and Mexico, as well as televised live performances on ''[[The Tonight Show with Jay Leno]]'', ''[[Jimmy Kimmel Live!]]'', ''[[Later... with Jools Holland]]'' and at [[Abbey Road Studios]]. There were also a number of festival dates in the United States and Europe, including [[Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival|Coachella]], [[T in the Park]] and [[Oxegen]].\n\nOn February 7, 2012, Ortega was nominated for two [[Juno Awards]]&nbsp;\u2013 New Artist of the Year and Roots & Traditional Album: Solo.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://junoawards.ca/nominees-winners/ |title=2012 JUNO Award Nominees |accessdate=February 7, 2012 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130221085934/http://junoawards.ca/nominees-winners/ |archivedate=February 21, 2013 }}</ref>\n\nOn June 14, 2012, Ortega's album ''[[Little Red Boots]]'' was named as a longlisted nominee for the [[2012 Polaris Music Prize]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.polarismusicprize.ca/article/416/the-2012-polaris-music-prize-long-list-is-here/ |title=The 2012 Polaris Music Prize Long List Is Here |accessdate=June 14, 2012 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120616223208/http://www.polarismusicprize.ca/article/416/the-2012-polaris-music-prize-long-list-is-here |archivedate=June 16, 2012 }}</ref> In June 2013, her album ''[[Cigarettes & Truckstops]]'' was longlisted for the [[2013 Polaris Music Prize]].\n\nIn July 2014, Ortega was nominated for two [[Canadian Country Music Association Awards]]&nbsp;\u2013 Female Artist of the Year and Roots Artist of the Year. Her album, ''[[Tin Star (album)|Tin Star]]'' was also nominated for Album Design of the Year.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ccma.org/_Library/CMW_2014/2014_CCMA_Award_Nominees_FINAL_v2.pdf|title=2014 CCMA Award Nominees|website=Ccma.org|accessdate=17 May 2018}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life and career beginnings==\nLindi Ortega was born on May 28, 1979<ref>{{Cite tweet|number=736404519928627200|user=lindiortega|title=It's my birthday in ten minutes...|author=Lindi Ortega|date=May 27, 2016|access-date=July 19, 2023}}</ref><ref>{{Cite tweet|number=1681734751470911488|user=lindiortega|title=... I am proudly my 44 years of age! ...|author=Lindi Ortega|date=July 19, 2023|access-date=July 19, 2023}}</ref> and is from Toronto, Ontario, Canada. She is of Mexican-Irish descent. She was 17 when&nbsp;\u2013 after picking up the guitar that hung on the wall of the family home&nbsp;\u2013 she wrote \"Faded Dress\", which she has said was \"the first in a long line of heartbreak songs\". It was about her first boyfriend dumping her the day before the prom. \"I wrote about the dress hanging in the closet, that never got worn. It was sad, but I thought it would be better the next year. But nobody asked me.\"<ref name=\"guardian 2014\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2014/jan/27/country-musician-lindi-ortega|title=Country musician Lindi Ortega: 'I'm a kickass thing'|last=Simpson|first=Dave|date=2014-01-27|newspaper=The Guardian|language=en-GB|issn=0261-3077|access-date=2016-09-12}}</ref>\n\nOrtega spent years trawling around record labels as the Toronto scene dubbed her \"Indie Lindi\". In 2008, she signed to major label Interscope, releasing one EP before they directed their resources into something more conventionally radio-friendly. Ortega remembers \"singing my heart out for suits with BlackBerries. Your emotions are all over the place&nbsp;\u2013 and they're staring at the ceiling.\"<ref name=\"guardian 2014\"/>\n\nAfter a decade of making ends meet by working in pizza places and fleamarkets, in 2011, she signed to Last Gang.<ref name=\"guardian 2014\"/>\n\nIn 2017, Ortega married Daniel Huscroft.<ref name=\"marrying tweet\">{{cite web |url=https://twitter.com/lindiortega/status/912416176386473984 |title=Tweet by Lindi Ortega |last=Ortega |first=Lindi |work=Twitter |date=2017-09-25 |accessdate=2023-01-03 |quote=So.. I'm actually getting married on Friday. He's got 4 days to hatch an escape plan! }}</ref><ref name=\"creston valley advance\">{{cite news |last=Coulter |first=Barry |url=https://www.crestonvalleyadvance.ca/community/making-new-music/ |title=Making new music |work=Creston Valley Advance |location=Creston, BC, Canada |publisher=Creston Valley Advance and Black Press Group Ltd. |date=2020-05-01 |accessdate=2023-01-03 |quote=...Lindi Ortega says she was feeling burnt out when she and her husband, Daniel Huscroft, moved to Creston last year. }}</ref> They divorced in July 2023.<ref>{{Cite tweet|number=1681734186233909248|user=lindiortega|title=\"Happily Divorced since July 2023\"|author=Lindi Ortega|date=July 19, 2023|access-date=July 19, 2023}}</ref>\n\nIn 2018, Ortega revealed that she has suffered from [[body dysmorphic disorder]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.lennyletter.com/story/lindi-ortega-body-dysmorphic-disorder|title=How Being on Stage Helped Me Cope With Body-Dysmorphic Disorder|first=Lindi|last=Ortega|website=Lennyletter.com|accessdate=May 17, 2018}}</ref>\n\n==Charity work==\nA self-described bird lover, Ortega organised and was the featured performer at a benefit concert for the World Parrot Refuge in [[Coombs, British Columbia]] on March 3, 2010.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.thestar.com/living/article/771597--music-for-the-birds |title=Music for the birds |last=Turnbull |first=Barbara |newspaper=[[The Toronto Star]] |date=February 26, 2010|accessdate=June 28, 2010}}</ref> The concert was held at [[The Supermarket]] in Toronto and featured a collection of local musicians that included Sara Kamin, Mandippal Jandu, [[The Framework]], [[Emma-Lee]], The DoneFors, and Dylan Murray.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://worldparrotrefuge.org/wpr.php/lindi-ortega |title=Lindi Ortega's Benefit Concert for the WPR |publisher=worldparrotrefuge.org |date=February 2, 2010 |accessdate=June 28, 2010}}</ref>\n\n==Albums==\n===''The Taste of Forbidden Fruit''===\nOrtega's debut album, ''The Taste of Forbidden Fruit'', was released in 2001. In her review of the album, Coreen Wolanski of ''[[Exclaim!]]'' described Ortega's voice as \"the closest thing to vocal perfection\"  she had heard in a long time.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=http://exclaim.ca/musicreviews/generalreview.aspx?csid2=852&fid1=11174&csid1=40 |archive-url=https://archive.today/20120707202111/http://exclaim.ca/musicreviews/generalreview.aspx?csid2=852&fid1=11174&csid1=40 |url-status=dead |archive-date=2012-07-07 |title=Lindi The Taste of Forbidden Fruit |last=Wolanski |first=Coreen |magazine=[[Exclaim!]] |date=April 2002 |accessdate=June 28, 2010 }}</ref> [[CBC Radio 3]] described the album as follows:\n\n{{blockquote|Lindi seasons her musical scores like a deranged chef whipping up a culinary creation. A dash of country, a pinch of folk, a sprinkle of rock, and a smidgeon of jazz! Last but not least, to add a little spice, how about some vaudeville cabaret? No, this is not a textbook recipe, but rather a mystical scribbling from an ancient scroll. Lindi is enigmatic and enchanting with a voice that can be cheeky and brassy or haunting and ghostly. Her music derives from the metaphysical in a sphere that warps time and defies orthodoxy. This madness is a pure passion that has never met the technicalities of music theory.<ref>{{cite web\n |url=http://radio3.cbc.ca/#/bands/Lindi \n |title=Lindi \u2013 CBC Radio 3: Free music, videos, podcasts & concerts \n |publisher=[[CBC Radio 3]] \n |accessdate=June 28, 2010 \n |url-status=dead  |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110301032334/http://radio3.cbc.ca/ \n |archivedate=March 1, 2011 \n}}</ref>}}\n\nThe song ''Nothing at All'' from this album was used in the online campaign for the [[Dove Campaign for Real Beauty]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4ytjTNX9cg0 |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/varchive/youtube/20211221/4ytjTNX9cg0 |archive-date=2021-12-21 |url-status=live|title=YouTube \u2013 a Dove film \u2013 Girl's self-esteem|website=[[YouTube]] }}{{cbignore}}</ref>\n\n===''Fall from Grace''===\nIn late 2005 Ortega began advertising her new album as coming in the autumn of 2006<ref name=\"Oxyfication 2005\"/> having declared, \"People kept pushing and prodding and finally I saw the light\".<ref name=\"DurhamRegion\">{{cite web|url=http://www.newsdurhamregion.com/article/41564 |title=Pickering musician returns to her music\n |last=MacNeil |first=Jason |date=June 2, 2006 |accessdate=June 28, 2010}}</ref> ''Fall From Grace'' was released on February 6, 2007.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mymusic.ca/product.asp?muzenbr=100339557 |title=Lindi, \"Fall From Grace *\" \u2013 mymusic CD, Album details |publisher=mymusic.ca |accessdate=June 28, 2010 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110706190003/http://www.mymusic.ca/product.asp?muzenbr=100339557 |archivedate=July 6, 2011 }}</ref> In reviewing the album Oxyfication.com described ''Fall From Grace'' as \"the quintessential album of the trials, tribulations, and triumphs of life as an indie singer.\"<ref name=\"Oxyfication 2007\"/>\n\n===EPs===\nIn 2007 Ortega collaborated with [[Juno Award]] winning producer [[Ron Lopata]] on \"I Need\", a song for the compilation album ''Year of the Monkey&nbsp;\u2013 68''. Lopata has since produced Ortega's two EPs and occasionally tours with her as her keyboardist. Ortega's eponymous EP was initially sold at concerts and on March 5, 2008 was made available online from independent music retailer killthe8.com.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lindiortega.ca/news/?p=33 |title=Lindi Ortega \u2014 New EP now available online! |accessdate=June 28, 2010}}</ref> When the initial run sold out the EP was discontinued. After being signed to [[Cherrytree Records]] / [[Interscope Records]] in August 2008 Ortega released her second EP, ''[[The Drifter E.P.]]'', to critical success. Ortega then began an extensive touring schedule which included touring with [[Noah & the Whale]] in the autumn of 2008,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.brooklynvegan.com/archives/2008/09/noah_the_whale_1.html |title=Noah & the Whale & Lindi Ortega @ Union Pool, NYC \u2013 pics |last=Reinford |first=Kyle Dean |publisher=brooklynvegan.com |date= September 17, 2008 |accessdate=June 28, 2010}}</ref> performing at the 2009 [[South by Southwest|SXSW]] festival in Austin, TX in March,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://sxsw2009.sched.org/venue/The+PureVolume.com+House/E+2nd+St+%26+Trinity+St,+Austin,+TX+78701|title=South by Southwest Music Festival|accessdate=June 28, 2010}}</ref> and opening for [[Kevin Costner#Country music|Kevin Costner & The Modern West's]] tour in July.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://popdirt.com/highlights-from-lindi-ortegas-iowa-concerts/75231/ |title=Highlights From Lindi Ortega's Iowa Concerts |publisher=PopDirt.com |accessdate=September 7, 2009}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ozanamguild.org/upcoming-events/details/8-kevin-costner-and-modern-west-with-lindi-ortega/ |title=Upcoming Events Kevin Costner and Modern West with Lindi Ortega |publisher=Ozanam Guild.org |accessdate=September 7, 2009 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20110727161320/http://www.ozanamguild.org/upcoming-events/details/8-kevin-costner-and-modern-west-with-lindi-ortega/ |archivedate=July 27, 2011 }}</ref> In September 2009 Ortega performed on a cross-Canada tour as opening act for [[Perfect Symmetry (tour)|Keane's North American tour]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.livenation.com/artist/lindi-ortega-tickets |title=LiveNation.com |accessdate=September 7, 2009 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20081211075642/http://www.livenation.com/artist/lindi-ortega-tickets |archivedate=December 11, 2008 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lindiortega.ca/news/?page_id=26 |title=Past Shows |publisher=Lindi Ortega's Official Site|accessdate=June 28, 2010}}</ref> After the success of labelmate [[Lady Gaga]], Cherrytree decided they would focus on dance / pop acts and Ortega signed with [[Last Gang Records]].\n\n===''Little Red Boots''===\nOrtega announced on her blog that a new full-length album with Juno Award winning producer, Ron Lopata, would be released on June 7, 2011 on Last Gang.<ref name=\"lindiortega.blogspot.com\">{{cite web|url=http://lindiortega.blogspot.com/2010/05/good-things-come-to-those-who-wait.html|title=Good Things Come To Those Who Wait|accessdate=May 21, 2010}}</ref> A release party was held at [[The Dakota Tavern]] in Toronto on June 6, 2011. The album and song, ''[[Little Red Boots]]'', are named after her signature red boots that she got while on tour with Kevin Costner and his rock country band Modern West. The album received critical acclaim and was nominated for two Juno Awards as well as a place on the Polaris Music Prize Long List.\n\n===''Cigarettes & Truckstops''===\nIn December 2011, Ortega moved to Nashville, TN where she began working with producer [[Colin Linden]] to record her album ''[[Cigarettes & Truckstops]]''. The album was released on Last Gang Records on October 2, 2012.  In support of this album, Ortega toured the United States and Canada, opening for Southern California punk legends [[Social Distortion]]. In June 2013, the album was longlisted for the [[2013 Polaris Music Prize]].\n\n===''Tin Star''===\n\nOrtega released her third album for Last Gang, ''Tin Star'', on October 8, 2013.\n\n===''Faded Gloryville''===\n\nOrtega released her fourth full-length album, ''[[Faded Gloryville]]'', on Last Gang Records' imprint Grand Tour Records on August 7, 2015.\n\n=== ''Liberty'' ===\nOrtega released ''[[Liberty (Lindi Ortega album)|Liberty]]'', her fifth full-length album, on Shadowbox Music on March 30, 2018.<ref>{{Citation|title=First Play: Lindi Ortega, Liberty|url=https://www.cbcmusic.ca/first-plays/720/first-play-lindi-ortega-liberty|accessdate=2018-05-15}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Micky_&_the_Motorcars","to":"Micky & the Motorcars"}],"pages":{"24964885":{"pageid":24964885,"ns":0,"title":"Micky & the Motorcars","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=June 2021}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Micky & the Motorcars\n| image             = Micky and the Motorcars blacksheep 2017 7933.jpg\n| image_upright     = 1.2\n| caption           = Micky & the Motorcars at the 2017 Blacksheep Festival\n| origin            = [[Challis, Idaho]], United States\n| genre             = [[Alternative country]], [[Americana (music)|Americana]], [[Texas country]], [[roots rock]], [[country rock]]\n| years_active      = 2002\u2013present\n| label             = Smith Music Group, [[Thirty Tigers]]\n| associated_acts   = [[Cross Canadian Ragweed]]<br/>[[Reckless Kelly (band)|Reckless Kelly]]<br/>[[Mike McClure]]<br />[[Jason Boland & the Stragglers]]\n| current_members   = Micky Braun<br/>Gary Braun<br/>Bobby Paugh<br/>Pablo Trujillo<br/>Andrew Carrell\n| past_members      = {{unbulleted list|Mark McCoy (2001\u20132011)| Travis Hardy (2001\u20132003)| Ken Smith (2001\u20132002)|Joseph Deeb (2002\u20132007)| Kris Farrow (2007-2011)| Shane Vannerson (2004\u20132013)| Dustin Schaefer (2011\u20132016) | Joe Fladger (2011-2021)}}\n| website           = {{URL|https://mickyandthemotorcars.com/}}\n| background        = group_or_band\n}}\n'''Micky & the Motorcars''' is a [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]] band formed in [[Stanley, Idaho]], now based in [[Austin, Texas]]. They have released nine albums, including two live albums.\n\n==Background==\n[[File:Micky and the Motorcars blacksheep 2017 7872.jpg|thumb|Micky Braun 2017]]\n\nThe two founding members, Micky and Gary Braun, are the sons of [[outlaw country]] and western swing musician Muzzie Braun of [[Stanley, Idaho]], and the brothers of Cody Braun and Willy Braun of the [[Texas]]-based [[roots rock]] band [[Reckless Kelly (band)|Reckless Kelly]]. Both were part of Muzzie Braun & the Little Braun Brothers band, but formed their own band after Cody and Willy left to form Reckless Kelly.<ref name=\"allmusic bio\">{{cite web |url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/micky-the-motorcars-mn0000123988/biography |title=Micky & the Motorcars |first= Steve|last= Leggett |work=AllMusic}}</ref> \n\nThe band originated in Idaho. The other founding members were childhood friends Travis Hardy on [[Drum|drums]] and Mark McCoy on [[Bass guitar|bass]]. They moved to [[Austin, Texas|Austin]], Texas, where Joseph Deeb joined the band as their lead guitarist.<ref name=\"allmusic bio\" /> The band has undergone a number of personnel changes since its founding. Mark McCoy left the band in 2011 and died in 2012 in a rafting accident.<ref name=\"the boot\">{{cite web |url=https://theboot.com/micky-and-the-motorcars-hold-this-town-together/ |title=Micky and the Motorcars, 'Hold This Town Together' |work=The Boot|date= October 7, 2019 |first= Angela |last=Stefano}}</ref> \n\nThe band currently consists of Micky Braun ([[acoustic guitar]], [[Lead vocalist|lead vocals]]), Gary Braun (lead & [[harmony vocals]], guitars, [[mandolin]], [[harmonica]]), Pablo Trujillo ([[lead guitar]], [[Pedal steel guitar|pedal steel]]), Andrew Carrell (bass), and Bobby Paugh (drums & percussion).\n\nThe band is also tied to the Texas music movement and, to a lesser extent, the [[Oklahoma]]-based Red Dirt music scene. Every year, the band, in conjunction with their brothers and fellow musicians in Reckless Kelly, host the Braun Brothers Reunion in Idaho to celebrate the music and different artists from the genre.\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"William_Clark_Green","to":"William Clark Green"}],"pages":{"46572653":{"pageid":46572653,"ns":0,"title":"William Clark Green","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=December 2023}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = William Clark Green\n| image           =\n| image_size      =\n| landscape       =\n| alt             =\n| caption         =\n| birth_name      = William Clark Green\n| birth_date      = {{Birth date and age|mf=yes|1986|05|19}}\n| occupation      = Singer, songwriter\n| origin          = [[Flint, Texas]]\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]]\n| years_active    = 2008-present<ref name=\"cmt\">{{cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/william-clark-green/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150405233903/http://www.cmt.com/artists/william-clark-green/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=April 5, 2015 |title=William Clark Green |work=CMT }}</ref>\n| label           = Bill Grease Records LLC\n| associated_acts =\n| website         = [http://www.williamclarkgreen.com/ http://www.williamclarkgreen.com/]\n}}\n\n'''William Clark Green''' (born May 19, 1986) is an American [[country music]] singer and songwriter from [[Flint, Texas]]. He has released six studio albums and two live albums, the most successful of which is ''Ringling Road'' from 2015.\n\n==Early life==\nGreen is from Flint, Texas. He attended [[A&M Consolidated High School]] in [[College Station, Texas]], graduating in 2004 before he went to [[Texas Tech University]] in [[Lubbock, Texas]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://maroonweekly.com/texas-country-star-william-clark-green/ |title=Texas Country Star William Clark Green |first= Jordyn |last=Smith |date= December 9, 2015 |work=Maroon Weekly }}</ref> It took six years for him to graduate as he concentrated on his music career.<ref name=\"cmt\"/>  \n\n==Career==\nGreen recorded his debut album in 2008 while attending Texas Tech in Lubbock. On September 24, 2008, the album Dangerous Man was released. In 2010, he released Misunderstood, his second album, as a follow-up.\n\n===2012: ''Rose Queen''===\nIn 2012, Green recorded his third album, ''Rose Queen'', at Sixteen Ton Studio in [[Nashville, Tennessee]]. The album was released on April 30, 2013. This became his breakthrough album. The first single from the album was \"It\u2019s About Time,\" which became his first Top Ten song on Texas Radio.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.reverbnation.com/williamclarkgreen |title=William Clark Green: Artist Bio |work=Reverbnation }}</ref> He had a No. 1 regional hit with the song \"She Likes the Beatles,\"<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.dallasnews.com/lifestyles/arts/columnists/mario-tarradell/20130718-spotlight-on-texas-artists-william-clark-green-grows-into-his-songwriting-maturity-on-rose-queen.ece |title=Spotlight on Texas Artists: William Clark Green grows into his songwriting maturity on \u2018Rose Queen\u2019 |author=Mario Tarradell |work=Dallas News |date=18 July 2013}}</ref> and the album yielded three top ten singles on the Texas country charts.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://countryperspective.com/2015/04/27/album-review-william-clark-greens-ringling-road/ |title=Album Review \u2013 William Clark Green\u2019s \u2018Ringling Road\u2019 |date=April 27, 2015 |author=Derek Hudgin |work=Country Perspective }}</ref>  According to Green, the album was inspired by the town of [[Tyler, Texas]] which has a local tradition called the [[Texas Rose Festival]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.williamclarkgreen.com/WCG%20CW%20On%20The%20Edge.pdf |title=On the Edge: Willam Clark Green |publisher=Country Weekly }}</ref>\n\n===2015: ''Ringling Road''===\nOn April 21, 2015, Green released his fourth album, ''Ringling Road''.<ref name=\"rollingstone\">{{cite web |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/premieres/hear-william-clark-greens-cleverly-twisted-ringling-road-20150417 | title=Hear William Clark Green's Cleverly Twisted 'Ringling Road'|author= Chris Parton |date= April 17, 2015 |work=Rolling Stone }}</ref>  The album debuted on ''Billboard 200'' at No. 133 and the Top Country Albums chart at No. 18, with 4,600 copies sold in the US.<ref name=\"sales\">{{cite news |url=http://roughstock.com/news/2015/04/34665-country-album-chart-report-for-april-29-2015/ |title=Country Album Chart Report For April 29, 2015 |author= Matt Bjorke |date= April 29, 2015 |work=Roughstock }} Sales figure given [https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1ioGGYQZAR9S3KGRifUYU0peTSyuHChJRE6s9C0J2sfg/edit#gid=0 here]</ref>  The first single from the album was \"Sympathy\" which topped the Texas Music Chart.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://lubbockonline.com/go/music/2014-11-14/greens-ringling-road-inspired-towns |title=Green's 'Ringling Road' inspired by towns|date=November 14, 2014 |author=Eric Woods |work=Lubbockonline }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.wacotrib.com/entertainment/accesswaco/music/texas-country-s-william-clark-green-rolls-into-waco-toward/article_7a72da5c-ee76-5fc2-b70d-d067dd96f66e.html |title=Texas country\u2019s William Clark Green rolls into Waco, toward new album release |author=Carl Hoover |work=WacoTrib.com |date=April 2, 2015 }}</ref>  The second single was \"Sticks and Stones\".  According to Green, the album was inspired by the town of [[Eastland, Texas]].<ref name=\"rollingstone\"/>\n\nGreen contributed a song to ''Dreamer: A Tribute to Kent Finlay'', an album released in early 2016 on Austin-based Eight 30 Records, titled \"Still Think About You.\" This work is a co-write with Finlay.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/dreamer-a-tribute-to-kent-finlay-mw0002916063 |title=Various Artists: Dreamer: A Tribute to Kent Finlay |work=AllMusic }}</ref>\n\nA live album, ''Live At Gruene Hall'', was released on September 23, 2016.<ref name=\"gruene hall\"/> It sold 1,100 copies in its debut week.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://roughstock.com/news/2016/10/40922-top-10-country-albums-sales-chart-october-3-2016 |title=Top 10 Country Albums Sales Chart: October 3, 2016 |first= Matt |last=Bjorke |date= October 5, 2016 |work=Roughstock }}</ref>\n\n===2018&ndash;present: ''Hebert Island'' and ''Baker Hotel''===\nA fifth album, ''Hebert Island'', was released on August 10, 2018.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://sixshootercountry.com/2018/08/06/william-clark-green-interview-hebert-island/ |title=William Clark Green: The Texan opens about \u2018Hebert Island\u2019, how he wouldn\u2019t change being a songwriter for anything and much more in this revealing interview! |date= August 6, 2018|first=Mark |last=Wiggins|work=Six Shooter Country }}</ref>\n\nIn November 2019, he released his second live album, ''Live At Cheatham Street Warehouse'', recorded at the [[Cheatham Street Warehouse|Cheatham Street venue]] in [[San Marcos, Texas]].<ref name=cheatham>{{cite news |url=https://kokefm.com/2019/11/08/william-clark-green-releases-live-album-and-video/ |title=William Clark Green Releases Live Album and Video |date=November 8, 2019 |work=KOKE FM}}</ref>\n\nIn 2022, Green released his sixth studio album, ''Baker Hotel''.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://txmusic.com/william-clark-green-baker-hotel/ |title=William Clark Green: 'Baker Hotel'|first= Mike Ethan |last= Messick |date=March 23, 2022 |work=Texas Music}}</ref>\n\n== Personal life ==\nHe currently lives in [[Eastland, Texas]].\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" \n|-\n! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Departed_(band)","to":"The Departed (band)"}],"pages":{"37528954":{"pageid":37528954,"ns":0,"title":"The Departed (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American rock band}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = The Departed\n| image             = CodyCanadaApr09.jpg\n| caption           = \n| image_size        = <!-- Only use for images smaller than 220 pixels -->\n| alias             = Cody Canada and the Departed, Jeremy Plato and the Departed\n| origin            = [[Yukon, Oklahoma]], [[United States|USA]]\n| genre             = [[Alternative Rock]], [[Southern Rock]], [[Alternative Country]], [[Americana (music)|Americana]], [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]]\n| label             = Underground Sound\n| years_active      = 2011-present\n| associated_acts   = [[Cross Canadian Ragweed]],<br/>[[ZZ Top]]<br/>[[Jason Boland & the Stragglers]]<br/>[[Wade Bowen]]<br/>[[Stoney LaRue]]<br/>[[Mike McClure Band]]<br/>[[Jonathan Tyler and the Northern Lights]]\n| current_members   = [[Cody Canada]]-Lead Vocals,<br/>Jeremy Plato-Bass Guitar,<br>[[Eric Hansen (drummer)|Eric Hansen]]-Drums\n| past_members      = Dave Bowen, Seth James, Steve Littleton, Chris Doege, Ross Smith\n| website           = [http://www.thedepartedmusic.com/ thedepartedmusic.com]\n}}\n'''The Departed''' (also known as '''Cody Canada and the Departed''') is an American [[Rock music|rock]] band. The band was formed in 2011 by [[Cody Canada]], the former lead vocalist and guitarist for [[Cross Canadian Ragweed]] after that band broke up in 2010. The band currently consists of Canada (guitars and lead vocals), Jeremy Plato (bass guitar and vocals), and [[Eric Hansen (drummer)|Eric Hansen]] (drums).\n\n==Formation==\nAfter Oklahoma based southern rock band [[Cross Canadian Ragweed]] broke up in 2010, [[Cody Canada]] decided to start the Departed that was billed by Texas and Oklahoma music scene observers as a \"Super Group.\" Canada remained on lead vocals and lead guitar and former Ragweed bass guitar player Jeremy Plato joined Canada. Canada recruited friend and Texas based blues rock singer and songwriter Seth James to be co-lead on guitar and vocals, well known red dirt keyboardist Steve Littleton, and fellow [[Yukon, Oklahoma]] native Dave Bowen on drums. Naming themselves \"The Departed\" as all had left previous bands to join together, the group at first billed themselves as \"Cody Canada and The Departed\" namely for fan recognition according to the band members in a 2011 interview.\n\n==''This Is Indian Land''==\nThe band released its first album in June 2011 titled ''This Is Indian Land'' through its own record label, Underground Sound. The record was a tribute album to Oklahoma music and songwriters. The band's cover version of the Red Dirt Rangers song \"Staring Down the Sun\" was the only released single from the album. Two other songs, \"The Ballad of Rosalie\" and \"Skyline Radio\" both charted on the Texas and Oklahoma music charts.\n\n==''Advent\u016bs''==\nOn August 24, 2012, now billed as simply The Departed, the band announced on its website and in social media that it would release its first original album, ''Advent\u016bs'' (Latin for \"arrival\") on November 13, 2012, on Underground Sound. Bowen had left the group and was replaced by Chris Doege on the drums. The band moved to an [[alternative rock]] and grunge sound with driving electric guitars and the power vocals of James and Canada. Three singles were released: \"Worth The Fight\", \"Prayer For the Lonely\" and \"Flagpole\".\n\n==''HippieLovePunk'' & Line-Up Changes==\nIn September 2013, Seth James announced that he intended to leave the band. The parting was amicable; as James said. \"After three years of great times and great music, I have decided to take a step down as a band member of the Departed. It has been an unbelievable ride and I am so grateful for the support and love along the way. My last show will be November 23 at Gruene Hall. I look forward to supporting these guys alongside you as they continue down the road.\"<ref>{{cite news |url=http://newsok.com/cody-canada-announces-the-departed-lineup-changes-new-solo-acoustic-live-album-due-this-fall/article/3883601 |title=Cody Canada announces The Departed lineup changes, new solo acoustic live album due this fall |author= Brandy McDonnell |date= September 16, 2013 |work=NewsOK }}</ref> The band continued performing as a four-piece group.\n\nIn 2014, the band finished a new album, ''HippieLovePunk''.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/5-minutes-in-texas-with-cody-canada-20140721 |title=5 Minutes in Texas With Cody Canada|author= Jim Casey |date=July 21, 2014 |magazine= Rolling Stone }}</ref> It was released on January 13, 2015, and debuted at No. 9 on the Top [[Alternative Country]] Albums chart, with 4,700 copies sold in the US in its first week. The sound was, for the most part, still like the alt-rock sound of ''Advent\u016bs''.<ref>{{cite news |url= http://roughstock.com/news/2015/01/32254-country-album-chart-report-january-21-2015/|title=Country Album Chart Report For January 21, 2015 |author= Matt Bjorke |date=January 21, 2015 |work=Roughstock }}</ref> Cody Canada and The Departed, as the band was once again known, debuted a new line-up at The MusicFest in Steamboat Springs, Colorado, on January 8, 2015. [[East Texas]] native Ross Smith replaced Littleton on keyboards and took up rhythm guitars, while [[Eric Hansen (drummer)|Eric Hansen]] became the drummer in place of Doege. In late November 2015, the band produced a music video for the song \"All Nighter\" on ''HippieLovePunk'' at John T. Floore's Country Store in [[Helotes, Texas]]. The song and the video were dedicated to the former bass guitar player for [[Micky and the Motorcars]] Mark McCoy, who had died in [[Idaho]] in 2012 while on vacation. The songs \"Inbetweener\" and \"Easy\" were released as singles.\n\n==''Jeremy Plato And The Departed: In Retrospect''==\nIn early 2016, the band announced on social media that it would be releasing an album consisting of cover versions of classic country songs. This project was named ''Jeremy Plato And The Departed: In Retrospect'', honoring 1960s era country music with songs by [[Johnny Paycheck]], Stonewall Jackson and [[Charlie Walker (musician)|Charlie Walker]], among others. The bass guitarist, Plato, took the lead vocals and had Canada, Smith and Hansen as his backing on the project. [[Reckless Kelly (band)|Reckless Kelly's]] Cody Braun and Cody Angel of Jason Boland and the Stragglers contributed their instrumentation to the project, as well as the folk singer Jamie Lin Wilson, who sang backing vocals and also appeared on a popular duet with Plato.\n\n==''3''==\nIn early 2017, Ross Smith left the band and The Departed became a 3 piece set with Canada, Plato, and Hansen. On April 20, 2018 the band released the single \"Lipstick\" from their new album ''3'', that was released on June 29, 2018, by the Underground Sound Label. [[Mike McClure]], who had produced several of Cross Canadian Ragweed's albums, came back to produce the album. The name of the album comes from the number of those who were left in the band. It was also their 3rd album of original content as '''In Retrospect''', and '''Indian Land''' had both been cover albums.\n\n==Current==\nDue to the band's current lineup, several popular Cross Canadian Ragweed songs have made their way back into the Departed's nightly set list in addition to the new material the band has written. Canada said in a 2018 Rolling Stone interview that he was \"truly happy with the way the band is now and I feel this is the band I have always wanted, and really deserved.\"\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Stoney_LaRue","to":"Stoney LaRue"}],"pages":{"16821333":{"pageid":16821333,"ns":0,"title":"Stoney LaRue","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American musician (born 1977)}}\n{{Infobox person\n| image           = Stoney LaRue (1).jpg\n| caption         = LaRue in 2014\n| birth_name      = Stoney Larue Phillips\n| birth_place     = [[Taft, Texas]], US\n| occupation      = Musician\n| years_active    = 2002\u2013present\n| website         = {{URL|www.stoneylarue.com}}\n| module          = {{Infobox musical artist|embed=yes\n| genre           = {{hlist|[[Red dirt (music)|Red dirt]]|[[Texas country]]}}\n| label           = Smith Music Group\n| past_member_of  = Stoney LaRue and the Organic Boogie Band\n}}\n}}\n\n'''Stoney LaRue''' (born '''Stoney Larue Phillips'''; 1977) is an American [[Texas country]]/[[Red dirt (music)|Red dirt]] artist.\n\n==Life and career==\nBorn in [[Taft, Texas]], LaRue was raised in Yanush/Buffalo Valley, Oklahoma, where he still visits regularly and began playing country music at a young age.\n\nLaRue moved to [[Stillwater, Oklahoma]], and began to play in the various bars around the college town, as well as his brother, Bo Phillips. He befriended [[Jason Boland & the Stragglers|Jason Boland]] and [[Cody Canada]] and the three moved into the infamous \"Yellow House\" where they would have late night jam sessions and entertain other various musicians around the town, like [[Mike McClure]] and [[Brandon Jenkins (singer/songwriter)|Brandon Jenkins]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Galleywinter Interview with Cody Canada |url=http://www.galleywinter.com/main/News/article/sid=402.html}}</ref> LaRue was heavily influenced by Woody Guthrie, Bob Childers, Mike Hosty and the \"Red Dirt\" music scene.<ref>from an interview on [http://americanamusicshow.com/episode228 episode 228 of the Americana Music Show], published January 12, 2015</ref> \n \nIn 2002, LaRue led The Organic Boogie Band and released ''Downtown'', recorded in private sessions at Cain's Ballroom in [[Tulsa]]. LaRue's 2005 follow-up, ''The Red Dirt Album'', reached the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' sales charts in its debut week. The next year, Stoney released his first live record ''Live at Billy Bob's Texas''.\n\nLaRue sang backing vocals on [[Miranda Lambert]]'s 2013 single \"[[All Kinds of Kinds]].\"<ref name=\"taste\">{{cite web|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/miranda-lambert-all-kinds-of-kinds/|title=Miranda Lambert, 'All Kinds of Kinds'&nbsp;\u2013 Song Review|author=Billy Dukes|date=June 10, 2013|publisher=Taste of Country|access-date=July 7, 2013}}</ref>\n\n== Legal issues ==\nOn the morning of July 20, 2015, LaRue was arrested and charged with domestic abuse after an altercation involving his then girlfriend Amanda Winsworth. Winsworth claimed in court documents that she was getting ready for work when LaRue began physically assaulting her and ultimately pushed her down a flight of stairs in their home. LaRue was released from jail on $4,000 bond ({{Inflation|US|4000|2015|fmt=eq|r=-2}}{{Inflation/fn|US}}) later that day. The next morning, Winsworth rescinded part of her account of the assault on Twitter stating that the incident had been blown out of proportion by the media.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Schwab |first=Kyle |title=Girlfriend says in court documents that musician LaRue punched her |url=https://www.oklahoman.com/story/entertainment/music/2015/07/22/girlfriend-says-in-court-documents-that-musician-larue-punched-her/60733862007/ |access-date=2022-11-18 |website=The Oklahoman |language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Whitaker |first=Sterling|title=Stoney LaRue Arrested, Charged With Domestic Abuse |url=https://tasteofcountry.com/stony-larue-arrested-domestic-abuse/ |access-date=2022-11-18 |website=Taste of Country |language=en}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Jack_Ingram","to":"Jack Ingram"}],"pages":{"2850182":{"pageid":2850182,"ns":0,"title":"Jack Ingram","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American country music singer (born 1970)}}\n{{Other people}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=September 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Jack Ingram\n| image           = Jack Ingram (14248722558) (cropped).jpg\n| caption         = Ingram performing in 2014\n| background      = solo_singer\n| birth_name      = Jack Owen Ingram\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|1970|11|15}}\n| origin          = [[The Woodlands, Texas]], U.S.\n| instrument      = Vocals, guitar\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]]\n| occupation      = Singer-songwriter\n| years_active    = 1992\u2013present\n| label           = Rhythmic, [[Rising Tide Records|Rising Tide]], Lucky Dog, [[Sony Music Nashville|Columbia Nashville]], [[Big Machine Records|Big Machine]], Blaster\n| website         = {{URL|jackingram.net}}\n}}\n\n'''Jack Owen Ingram''' (born November 15, 1970) is an American [[country music]] artist formerly signed to [[Big Machine Records]], an [[independent record label]]. He has released eleven studio albums, one [[extended play]], six live albums, and 19 [[single (music)|singles]]. Although active since 1992, Ingram did not reach the U.S. Country Top 40 until the release of his single \"[[Wherever You Are (Jack Ingram song)|Wherever You Are]]\" late-2005. A number one hit on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' country charts, that song was also his first release for Big Machine and that label's first Number One hit. Ingram has sent six other songs into the country Top 40 with \"[[Love You (song)|Love You]]\", \"[[Lips of an Angel]]\" (a [[cover version]] of a song by [[Hinder]]), \"[[Measure of a Man (Jack Ingram song)|Measure of a Man]]\", \"[[Maybe She'll Get Lonely]]\", \"[[That's a Man]]\", and \"[[Barefoot and Crazy]]\".\n\n==Biography==\nIngram was born in [[Houston|Houston, Texas]]. He started writing songs and performing while studying [[psychology]] at [[Southern Methodist University]] in [[Dallas]], where he was member of [[Alpha Tau Omega]].\n\n===Musical career===\nJack Ingram began his music career singing at a privately owned bar near the TCU campus of Fort Worth, Texas, which was owned by his friend [[John Clay Wolfe]].\nLater, during the early 1990s, Jack toured the state of Texas opening for [[Mark Chesnutt]] and other acts.<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web|url={{AllMusic|class=artist|id=p89255|pure_url=yes}}|title=Jack Ingram biography|last=Erlewine|first=Stephen Thomas|work=[[AllMusic]]|access-date=May 28, 2009}}</ref> His first release was his self-titled album in 1995 via the Rhythmic label, followed by 1995's ''Lonesome Questions''. [[Warner Records|Warner Bros. Records]] eventually signed him and released a live album entitled ''Live at Adair's'', and re-issued his first two indie albums.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/>\n\nIn 1997 he had his first time on the 22nd season of [[Austin City Limits]]. That same year, he released ''[[Livin' or Dyin']]'' via [[Rising Tide Records]], which produced his first chart single in the No.&nbsp;51-peaking \"Flutter\". Two years later came ''Hey You'' via Lucky Dog, a division of [[Epic Records]], which accounted for a No.&nbsp;64 country single in \"How Many Days\". In 2000, he collaborated with [[Charlie Robison]] and [[Bruce Robison]] for the live album ''Unleashed Live''.\n\n''[[Electric (Jack Ingram album)|Electric]]'', his second album for Lucky Dog, was also his first album to enter [[Top Country Albums]], despite not producing a chart single. This album was supplemented a year later by an [[extended play|EP]] entitled ''Electric: Extra Volts'' before he left Lucky Dog. Two more live albums followed before he signed to [[Sony Music Nashville|Columbia Nashville]] for the release of ''Young Man'' in 2004, which accounted for no singles. Another live album, ''Acoustic Motel'', was issued in 2005.\n\nOn Sunday, February 3, 2013, [[H-E-B]] premiered their 'Texas Myths' Super Bowl commercial featuring Jack Ingram.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RLcSPOZoBPw|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130206002258/http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RLcSPOZoBPw|url-status=dead|archive-date=2013-02-06|title=H-E-B 2013 Game Day Commercial: Texas Myths - YouTube|website = [[YouTube]]|date=February 6, 2013}}</ref>\n\n===2005\u20132011: Big Machine Records===\nIn 2005, Ingram signed to the independent record label [[Big Machine Records]]. Under the Big Machine banner, Ingram released a predominantly live album entitled ''[[Live: Wherever You Are]]''. His first single release on that record label, \"[[Wherever You Are (Jack Ingram song)|Wherever You Are]]\", became Ingram's first top 40, and later his first and only Number One single on the U.S. ''Billboard'' [[Hot Country Songs]] charts, as well as the first Number One for the Big Machine label. \"[[Love You (song)|Love You]]\", the only other studio track on ''Live: Wherever You Are'', was also released as a single, peaking at No.&nbsp;12 on the charts. This song was also recorded by [[Trent Summar & the New Row Mob]] (whose frontman, Trent Summar, co-wrote it) on their 2005 album ''Horseshoes & Hand Grenades''.\n\nIn late 2006, Ingram released a cover of [[Hinder]]'s song \"[[Lips of an Angel]]\". Ingram's cover peaked at No.&nbsp;16 on the country charts \"Lips of an Angel\" was the lead-off single to ''This Is It'', his second album for Big Machine. This album also produced the No.&nbsp;18 \"[[Measure of a Man (Jack Ingram song)|Measure of a Man]]\" (a [[Radney Foster]] co-write) and the No.&nbsp;24 \"[[Maybe She'll Get Lonely]]\".\n\nIn 2008, Ingram appeared at the Argyle Education Foundation Black Diamond Affair.\n\nHe won the [[Academy of Country Music]] award for top new male vocalist on May 19, 2008. Ingram also filled in for radio host [[Bob Kingsley]] on the countdown show \"[[Bob Kingsley's Country Top 40]]\" for the week of September 20\u201321, 2008.\n\nAccording to [[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]], Ingram's ''Big Dreams & High Hopes'' album has \"more guts\" and [[Ellis Paul]]'s \"The World Ain't Slowing Down\" may be the song that takes Ingram to the \"next level\".<ref>Shelburne, Craig. [https://web.archive.org/web/20080930213604/http://blog.cmt.com/2008-09-29/jack-ingrams-new-music-will-have-more-guts/ Jack Ingram\u2019s New Music Will Have \u201cMore Guts\u201d.] CMT Blog, September 29, 2008. Retrieved October 29, 2008.</ref> Ingram says \"It'll be fun for me to expose people to a fantastic song from an artist who's had a 20-year career of being a very successful folk artist.\"<ref>Mansfield, Brian. [https://www.usatoday.com/printedition/life/20081226/jackingram26_st.art.htm Ingram has 'Big Dreams' for album.] ''USA Today'', December 26, 2008.  Retrieved January 6, 2009.</ref> The song was cut from the album. Its lead-off single \"[[That's a Man]]\" charted in the Top 20, followed by \"[[Barefoot and Crazy]],\" which became his second Top 10 hit. The album's next three singles all failed to enter the Top 40: \"Seeing Stars\" (a duet with [[Patty Griffin]]), \"Free\" and a re-recording of \"Barbie Doll\" with guest vocals from [[Dierks Bentley]].\n\nOn August 26, 2009, Ingram set a [[Guinness World Records|Guinness record]] for the most radio interviews in one day, when he was interviewed 215 times.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.roughstock.com/blog/jack-ingram-breaks-guinness-book-world-record-|title=Jack Ingram breaks Guinness book world record|last=Bjorke|first=Matt|date=August 2, 2008|work=Roughstock|access-date=August 27, 2009|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110613191231/http://www.roughstock.com/blog/jack-ingram-breaks-guinness-book-world-record-|archive-date=June 13, 2011}}</ref>\n\n[[File:Jack Ingram.JPG|200px|thumbnail|right|Singing the [[The Star-Spangled Banner|National Anthem]] in Denver at [[Empower Field at Mile High|Sports Authority Field at Mile High]] on October 28, 2012.]]\nIngram and Big Machine amicably parted ways in late 2011.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.radio-info.com/programming/country/country-star-jack-ingrams-surprising-side-job-imaging-voice-for-radio |title=Country Star Jack Ingram's Surprising Side Job: Imaging Voice For Radio|access-date=April 22, 2012 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120426111256/http://www.radio-info.com/programming/country/country-star-jack-ingrams-surprising-side-job-imaging-voice-for-radio |archive-date=April 26, 2012 }}</ref>\n\nAs a sideline, Ingram does [[Radio sweeper|voice imaging]] for a number of country stations, including KRYS-FM Corpus Christi; [[WSIX-FM]] [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]]; [[WMIL-FM]] Milwaukee; [[KWJJ-FM]] [[Portland, Oregon|Portland, Ore.]]; and [[KSCS]] [[Dallas]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.radio-info.com/programming/country/country-star-jack-ingrams-surprising-side-job-imaging-voice-for-radio|title=Country Star Jack Ingram's Surprising Side Job: Imaging Voice For Radio|last=Stark|first=Phyllis|date=April 1, 2012|work=Radio-Info.com|access-date=April 22, 2012|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120426111256/http://www.radio-info.com/programming/country/country-star-jack-ingrams-surprising-side-job-imaging-voice-for-radio|archive-date=April 26, 2012}}</ref>\n\n===Fundraising===\nIn 2013, Jack teamed up with actor [[Matthew McConaughey]] and University of Texas at Austin football coach [[Mack Brown]] to create a fundraiser for their favorite children's charities.  Dubbed Mack, Jack & McConaughey, the affair was held April 11\u201312 at Austin's ACL Live at the [[Block 21|Moody Theater]] and featured a gala, golf tournament, fashion show and two nights of music.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/news/mack-jack-mcconaughey-benefit-austin|title=Mack, Jack & McConaughey Benefit In Austin|date=December 2, 2014|website=Grammy.com}}</ref> Mack, Jack & McConaughey returned in 2014.<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://mackjackmcconaughey.org/schedule-of-events/ |title=Event Opportunities &#124; MJ&M 2014 |access-date=April 23, 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140520160204/http://mackjackmcconaughey.org/schedule-of-events/ |archive-date=May 20, 2014 |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Corey_Kent","to":"Corey Kent"}],"pages":{"71437833":{"pageid":71437833,"ns":0,"title":"Corey Kent","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n| background        = person\n| name              = \n| image             = \n| alt               = \n| birth_name        = Corey Kent White\n| alias             = \n| birth_date        = {{Birth date and age|1994|06|21}}\n| birth_place       = [[Bixby, Oklahoma]], U.S.\n| origin            = [[Frisco, Texas]], U.S.\n| genre             = {{flatlist|\n* [[Country music|Country]]\n* [[country rock]]\n}}\n| occupation        = Singer\n| instrument        = {{flatlist|\n* Vocals\n* guitar\n}}\n| years_active      = 2015\u2013present\n| label             = [[RCA Records Nashville|RCA Nashville]]\n}}\n\n'''Corey Kent White''' (born June 21, 1994) is an American [[country music]] singer from [[Frisco, Texas]] signed to [[RCA Records Nashville|RCA Nashville]].\n\n== Biography ==\nCorey Kent White was born in [[Bixby, Oklahoma]]. Kent grew up listening to [[country music]], taking influence from artists such as fellow Oklahoma native [[Garth Brooks]]. Learning the road life early, Kent was just 11 when he joined a touring Western Swing group, traveling the country at the front of a \u201cworking class\u201d band brothers for five years before they finally dissolved.<ref>{{Cite web |title=In Focus: Corey Kent {{!}} Holler |url=https://holler.country/feature/in-focus-corey-kent |access-date=2023-06-23 |website=holler.country |language=en}}</ref> Still in high school and unsure of what came next, he nearly quit entirely \u2013 but after a chance encounter of being pulled out of the audience and joining Willie Nelson on stage, he was inspired to start writing songs, a new path emerged. At age 17, he moved to Tennessee, hit the pavement and scored a publishing deal. And then the bottom dropped out.  He lost his publishing deal, decided to move back to Texas and then epidemic happened<ref>{{Cite web |last=O'Connell |first=Madeleine |date=2023-06-02 |title=Corey Kent's Major Label Debut, 'Blacktop,' Signals A New Sense Of Appreciation For His Life And Career |url=https://countrynow.com/corey-kents-major-label-debut-blacktop-signals-a-new-sense-of-appreciation-for-his-life-and-career/ |access-date=2023-06-23 |website=Country Now |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nAs the world started opening up, Corey began touring in Texas and Oklahoma<ref>{{Cite web |title=Country Star Corey Kent Coming in Concert to Sarasota, has hit, Wild as Her {{!}} 92.1 CTQ |url=https://ctqcountry.iheart.com/featured/maverick-mornings/content/2023-02-17-country-star-corey-kent-coming-in-concert-to-sarasota-has-hit-wild-as-her/ |access-date=2023-06-23 |website=Maverick |language=en}}</ref> playing in night clubs and opening for bands like [[Randy Rogers Band|Randy Rogers]], [[Parker McCollum]], [[Kolby Cooper]] and [[Cody Johnson]]. Corey then emerged on to the ''Billboard'' charts in 2022 with \"[[Wild as Her]]\". Due to popularity on streaming services, the song charted in late 2022. The song is a follow-up to Kent's second studio album, ''21''.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1842984/corey-kent-talks-chart-topping-single-wild-as-her-and-how-willie-nelson-took-a-chance-on-him/ | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220528191617/http://www.cmt.com/news/1842984/corey-kent-talks-chart-topping-single-wild-as-her-and-how-willie-nelson-took-a-chance-on-him/ | url-status=dead | archive-date=May 28, 2022 | title=Corey Kent Talks Chart-Topping Single \"Wild As Her\" And How Willie Nelson Took A Chance On Him | publisher=[[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]] | date=March 24, 2022 | accessdate=August 2, 2022}}</ref> Because of this song's initial charting success, ''Billboard'' reported that many Nashville labels were in a [[bidding war]] to sign Kent.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.billboard.com/pro/corey-kent-wild-as-her-label-deal-inside-track/ | title=Inside Track: 'Wild as Her' Singer Corey Kent at Center of Nashville Bidding War | publisher=Billboard | date=April 26, 2022 | accessdate=August 2, 2022 | author=Jessica Nicholson}}</ref> [[RCA Records Nashville]] signed Kent in August 2022 and began promoting \"Wild as Her\" to country radio.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://countrynow.com/corey-kent-reflects-on-life-changing-success-of-wild-as-her-its-pretty-crazy/ | title=Corey Kent Reflects On Life-Changing Success Of 'Wild As Her:' 'It's Pretty Crazy' | publisher=Country Now | date=August 8, 2022 | accessdate=August 16, 2022}}</ref> \"Wild as Her\" amassed over 300 million streams in its first year, reached [https://musicrow.com/2023/05/corey-kent-lands-first-chart-topper-with-wild-as-her/ platinum] status in March 2023 and reached the [https://musicrow.com/2023/05/corey-kent-lands-first-chart-topper-with-wild-as-her/ top spot at Country Radio] in May of the same year.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Hollabaugh |first=Lorie |date=2023-05-15 |title=Corey Kent Lands First Chart-Topper With 'Wild As Her' |url=https://musicrow.com/2023/05/corey-kent-lands-first-chart-topper-with-wild-as-her/ |access-date=2023-06-23 |website=MusicRow.com |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nKent's major label debut and third studio album, ''[[Blacktop (album)|Blacktop]]'', was released on June 2, 2023 via RCA Nashville. \"Something's Gonna Kill Me\" was released on July 10, 2023 as the second single.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.allaccess.com/country/future-releases | title=Future Releases for Country Radio Stations &#124; New Music Artist Free Song }}</ref>\n\n== Discography ==\n=== Albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" border=\"1\"\n|+ List of albums, with selected chart positions, showing other This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Bruce_Robison","to":"Bruce Robison"}],"pages":{"10471206":{"pageid":10471206,"ns":0,"title":"Bruce Robison","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n\n{{Use mdy dates|date=August 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Bruce Robison\n| image           = Bruce Robison (1).jpg\n| caption         = Robison in 2009\n| birth_name      = Bruce Ben Robison\n| birth_date      = {{Birth date and age|1966|6|11}}\n| origin          = [[Bandera, Texas]]\n| instrument      = Vocals, guitar, harmonica\n| genre           = [[Folk music|Folk]], [[Country music|country]]\n| label           = Vireo, Lucky Dog, Premium\n| spouse = {{Marriage|[[Kelly Willis]]|1996|2022|end=div}}\n| website         = {{url|brucerobison.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Bruce Ben Robison''' (born June 11, 1966) is an American, [[Austin, Texas|Austin]]-based [[Texas country music]] singer-songwriter.  Bruce and his brother, fellow singer-songwriter [[Charlie Robison]], grew up in [[Bandera, Texas]], near [[San Antonio]].  His self-titled debut album was released in 1995.<ref>{{cite web|author=William Ruhlmann |url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/bruce-robison-mw0000083869 |title=Bruce Robison \u2013 Bruce Robison &#124; Songs, Reviews, Credits, Awards |publisher=AllMusic |access-date=July 14, 2014}}</ref>\n\nRobison has written several songs which have become hits when covered by well-known singers, including: \"[[Travelin' Soldier]],\" (recorded in 2003 by the [[Dixie Chicks]], reached No. 1 on the Country charts); \"[[Angry All the Time]],\" (recorded by [[Tim McGraw]] and [[Faith Hill]] in 2001, also reached No. 1 on the country charts); and \"[[Wrapped (George Strait song)|Wrapped]]\" (recorded in 2006 by [[George Strait]], reached No. 2 in 2007). Bruce runs The Next Waltz, a record label by artists for artists.\n\n==Personal life==\nSister, Robyn Ludwick, and late brother [[Charlie Robison]] are accomplished singer-songwriters in their own right.\n\nIn 1992, he met singer-songwriter [[Kelly Willis]] and they married in 1996. Together they had a son, Deral Otis, in January 2001. Willis became pregnant again and gave birth to twins Abigail Esme and Benjamin James<ref>[http://www.commotionpr.com/images/BruceKelly_twins.jpg]  {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070930095738/http://www.commotionpr.com/images/BruceKelly_twins.jpg |date=September 30, 2007 }}</ref> on March 24, 2003.<ref>{{cite }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://dir.salon.com/story/mwt/feature/2003/08/01/rockermoms/index.html |title=Mothers who rock - Salon.com |publisher=Dir.salon.com |date=August 1, 2003 |access-date=July 14, 2014 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110606191622/http://dir.salon.com/story/mwt/feature/2003/08/01/rockermoms/index.html |archive-date=June 6, 2011 Bowen"}],"pages":{"24497807":{"pageid":24497807,"ns":0,"title":"Wade Bowen","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = Wade Bowen\n| image            = \n| caption          = \n| birth_name       = Paul Wade Bowen\n| image_size       = \n| background       = solo_singer\n| birth_date       = {{birth year and age|1977}}\n| origin           = [[Waco, Texas]], U.S.\n| genre            = [[Country music|Country]], [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]], [[Texas Country]]\n| years_active     = 2000\u2013present\n| label            = [[BNA Records|BNA]], [[Columbia Records|Columbia]]\n| associated_acts  = [[Cross Canadian Ragweed]]<br />[[Randy Rogers Band]]<br/>[[Brandon Rhyder]]\n| website          = https://wadebowen.com\n| current_members  = \n}}\n\n'''Paul Wade Bowen''' (born 1977) is an American [[Texas Country]]/[[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]] singer from [[Waco, Texas]], United States.\n\nBowen was a member of the band West 84 with friend Matt Miller until 2001 when the group became known as Wade Bowen and West 84.<ref name=\"am\">{{cite news |title=Wade Bowen Biography |url={{AllMusic|class=artist|id=p326461|pure_url=yes}}}}, [[AllMusic]]</ref> He released his first album in 2002, ''Try Not To Listen'', which became a regional hit in Texas.<ref>{{cite news |title=Biography |url={{AllMusic|class=artist|id=p326461|pure_url=yes}}}}, [[AllMusic]]</ref> He released his first live album in 2003, recorded live at The Blue Light in [[Lubbock, Texas]], followed by studio albums ''Lost Hotel'' in 2006 and ''[[If We Ever Make It Home]]'' in 2008.<ref>{{cite news |title=Wade Bowen: If We Ever Make It Home Review |url=http://www.slantmagazine.com/music/music_review.asp?ID=1542|website=Slantmagazine.com}}</ref> On November 21, 2009, Bowen recorded his second live album at [[Billy Bob's Texas]] in [[Fort Worth, Texas|Fort Worth]]. The album was released on April 27, 2010, as a CD/DVD combo.<ref>{{cite news |title=WADE BOWEN GEARS UP FOR \"LIVE AT BILLY BOB'S\" ALBUM AND DVD ON NOV. 21, 2009 |url=https://app.e2ma.net/app/view:CampaignPublic/id:7018.2550101837/rid:2848afec78311ce4e9bfd8c3c5d361a5|website=App.e2ma.net}}</ref>\n\nBowen released his fourth studio album, ''The Given'', in 2010.<ref name=\"am\"/>  It was his first on a major label, [[Sony Music|Sony]] imprint [[BNA Records]], though he returned to releasing music independently after BNA closed.<ref name=\"am\"/>  He released a self-titled studio album in 2014, followed by a duets album in 2015 with singer Randy Rogers of the [[Randy Rogers Band]], titled ''[[Hold My Beer Vol. 1]]''.<ref name=\"am\"/>  Bowen's next album was '' Then Sings My Soul: Songs for My Mother'', a solo [[gospel music|gospel]] influenced studio release.<ref name=\"am\"/> He has released 3 more albums: Watch This, with Randy Rogers, Solid Ground, released in 2018, and a follow-up to Hold My Beer Vol. 1, Hold My Beer Vol. 2 with Randy Rogers.\n\nDuring the [[COVID-19 pandemic|Covid-19 Pandemic]] of 2020, Wade started a web series of live shows called Wade's World, where he hosted other prominent Texas musicians to play and tell stories about their songs every Friday night. Guests included [[Bruce Robison]], [[Cody Canada]], [[Jack Ingram]], and others.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Hennessey|first=Katie|title=Texas Americana Artist Wade Bowen Hosts Quaranstream Concert Series on Friday Nights|url=https://www.sacurrent.com/sa-sound/archives/2020/05/13/texas-americana-artist-wade-bowen-hosts-quaranstream-concert-series-on-friday-nights|access-date=2021-01-20|website=San Antonio Current|language=en}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nBowen is the brother-in-law of [[Cross Canadian Ragweed]] frontman [[Cody Canada]]<ref>{{cite news |title=Galleywinter Interview with Cody Canada |url=http://www.galleywinter.com/main/News/article/sid=402.html|website=Galleywinter.com}}</ref> and is a graduate of [[Texas Tech University]], where he is a member of the Epsilon Nu chapter of the [[Sigma Chi]] fraternity.<ref>{{cite news |title=Wade Bowen |website=CMT.com |url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/wade_bowen/artist.jhtml|archive-url=https://archive.today/20130121040709/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/wade_bowen/artist.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=January 21, 2013}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Danielle_Peck","to":"Danielle Peck"}],"pages":{"6792824":{"pageid":6792824,"ns":0,"title":"Danielle Peck","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n\n{{Use mdy dates|date=December 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Danielle Peck\n| image           = Danielle Peck stage (cropped).jpg\n| caption         = Danielle Peck performing for the troops at [[Naval Submarine Base New London]] May 31, 2007, for the [[Spirit of America (company)|Spirit of America]] tour\n| image_size      =\n| birth_name      = Danielle Marie Peck\n| birth_date      = {{Birth date and age|1978|9|14}}\n| origin          = [[Jacksonville, North Carolina|Jacksonville]], North Carolina, United States\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]]\n| occupation      = Singer-songwriter\n| years_active    = 2005\u2013present\n| label           = [[Dreamworks Records|Dreamworks Nashville]], [[Big Machine Records|Big Machine]]\n| associated_acts = [[Sherri\u00e9 Austin]]\n| website         = {{URL|www.daniellepeck.com}}\n}}\n'''Danielle Marie Peck''' (born September 14, 1978) is an American [[country music]] artist. Signed to the independent [[Big Machine Records]] label in 2005, Peck released her self-titled debut album, which produced the Top 30 country hits \"I Don't\", \"[[Findin' a Good Man]]\", and \"Isn't That Everything\". A fourth single, \"Bad for Me\", charted in mid-2007. Peck is now heard as a host on \"Y2 Kountry\" a country music radio station on [[Sirius XM]] radio.\n\n==Biography==\n===Early life===\n[[Image:Danielle Peck autographs.jpg|thumb|left|150px|Danielle Peck signs autographs for sailors during the [[Spirit of America (company)|Spirit of America]] tour, May 31, 2007]] Peck was born in [[Jacksonville, North Carolina|Jacksonville]], North Carolina, but was raised in [[Coshocton, Ohio|Coshocton]], Ohio. She is the daughter of a United States [[Marine (military)|Marine]]. Her parents both came from musical backgrounds. Her mother's side of the family traveled and sang in churches. Her fathers' parents and grandparents were steeped in country music, playing dances in the area.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.gactv.com/gac/ar_az_danielle_peck/article/0,,GAC_26129_4702985,00.html |archive-url=https://archive.today/20120903223858/http://www.gactv.com/gac/ar_az_danielle_peck/article/0,,GAC_26129_4702985,00.html |url-status=dead |archive-date=September 3, 2012 |title=Danielle Peck > Biography |publisher=[[Great American Country]] |accessdate=April 19, 2011 }}</ref>\n\nThe first song she ever sang was [[Johnny Cash]]'s \"[[Folsom Prison Blues]],\" which she continues to perform in her live shows to this day. She wrote her first song before the age of 10. She also sang in her church, as solo and as part of a choir. At age 16, she joined a band called ''The Neon Moon Band'', which performed around the local area.\n\nAfter graduating from [[River View High School (Warsaw, Ohio)|River View High School]] in 1997, Peck formed her own band that performed at festivals and other events. She then moved to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]], Tennessee, finding work as a [[waitress]] while pursuing a career in country music. While in Nashville, she met Clay Myers, a publisher who signed her to a deal as a songwriter with Barbara Orbison's Still Working Music. Peck soon started writing for her staff members.\n\n===Musical career===\nSoon, Peck signed a recording contract with [[DreamWorks Records]], with executive [[Scott Borchetta]]. She was working on her debut album when DreamWorks folded and Borchetta founded his own record company entitled [[Big Machine Records]], which would go on to be the record company for artists like [[Taylor Swift]] and [[Tim McGraw]].\n\nIn 2005, she released her debut single, \"I Don't\" (co-written with Clay Mills and Burton Collins). The song peaked at number 28 on the U.S. ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] chart. Peck then released her [[Danielle Peck (album)|eponymous debut album]] in June 2006. The album peaked at number 23 on the ''Billboard'' [[Top Country Albums]] chart and produced two more Top 30 singles in \"[[Findin' a Good Man]]\" (her highest-charting single to date) and \"Isn't That Everything\". Also in 2006, Peck took part in a duet with fellow country singer [[Jack Ingram]] on his 2006 album ''[[Live: Wherever You Are]]'', titled \"Never Knocked Me Down,\" which was an audio excerpt from the [[Country Music Television|CMT]] program ''Outlaws 2005''.\n\nPeck released her fourth single in early 2007. Titled \"Bad For Me,\" the single (which was co-written by Australian country singer [[Sherri\u00e9 Austin]]) was intended to be the lead-off to an upcoming second album. \"Bad For Me\" failed to reach the Hot Country Songs Top 40 (number 46), however, and the second album's release date was delayed until late 2008. That album, titled ''Can't Behave'', was released on December 23 of that year, though it was only available through digital retailers. The title track to ''Can't Behave'' was then released as a single in January 2009. The single, however, failed to chart altogether, and Peck parted ways with Big Machine shortly afterward.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1606224/country-rosters-remain-stable-despite-sales-downturn.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090305134112/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1606224/country-rosters-remain-stable-despite-sales-downturn.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=March 5, 2009|title=Country Rosters Remain Stable Despite Sales Downturn|publisher=[[Country Music Television]]|accessdate=April 19, 2011}}</ref>\n\n===2007 ALCS controversy===\nIn 2006, Peck briefly dated [[Boston Red Sox]] pitcher [[Josh Beckett]]. On October 18, 2007, she was a last-minute choice to sing the national anthem before Game 5 of the [[American League Championship Series]] between the Red Sox and the [[Cleveland Indians]]. While the Indians organization stated that she was chosen because she was an Ohio native and Indians fan, it was believed that she was brought in to distract Beckett, who was starting the game for the Red Sox.<ref>[http://www.cleveland.com/tribe/plaindealer/index.ssf?/base/sports/119270858859540.xml&coll=2 Head games? Tonight's anthem singer is Beckett's ex \u2013 Cleveland.com<!-- Bot generated title -->] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080329053021/http://www.cleveland.com/tribe/plaindealer/index.ssf?%2Fbase%2Fsports%2F119270858859540.xml&coll=2 |date=March 29, 2008 }}</ref> Beckett went on to a decisive victory, and when asked about Peck's presence, he replied: \"I don't get paid to make those fucking decisions<!--Wikipedia does not censor its articles, per talk page discussion.-->...she's a friend of mine. It doesn't bother me at all. Thanks for flying one of my friends to the game, so she could watch it for free.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://sports.yahoo.com/mlb/recap?gid=271018105 |title=Yahoo |website=Sports.yahoo.com |date= |accessdate=April 4, 2020}}</ref> Peck has never publicly commented on the incident.\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! On June 12, 2014, Peck married tour production manager Josh Smith in Ballina, Ireland.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://daniellepeck.com/news/danielle-peck-eloped |title=News |website=Daniellepeck.com |date= |accessdate=April 4, 2020 |archive-date=February 16, 2016 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160216175250/http://daniellepeck.com/news/danielle-peck-eloped |url-status=dead }}</ref> The |website=Theboot.com |date= August 19, 2015|accessdate=April 4, 2020}}</ref>\nPeck and Smith separated in March 2016, according to her official page.<ref>{{cite web|url=
