This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Court_Yard_Hounds","to":"Court Yard Hounds"}],"pages":{"25821052":{"pageid":25821052,"ns":0,"title":"Court Yard Hounds","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country and folk music duo}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=May 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Court Yard Hounds\n| image           = Maguire and Robeson 2010.jpg\n| caption         = Maguire, left, and Robison, right, performing at Antone's, [[SXSW]], Austin, Texas, March 17, 2010\n| image_size      = 275px\n| landscape       = Yes\n| origin          = [[San Antonio|San Antonio, Texas]], U.S.\n| genre           = {{Hlist|[[Americana (music)|Americana]]|[[Country music|country]]|[[Folk music|folk]]}}\n| years_active    = 2009\u20142013\n| label           = [[Columbia Records|Columbia]]\n| spinoff_of      = [[The Chicks]]\n| past_members    = \n* [[Martie Maguire]]\n* [[Emily Robison]]\n| website         = {{URL|courtyardhounds.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Court Yard Hounds''' were an American [[country music]] and [[Folk music|folk]] duo, founded by sisters [[Martie Maguire]] and [[Emily Robison]]. They, along with [[Natalie Maines]], make up [[The Chicks]], formerly the Dixie Chicks. The sisters decided to record a side project under a different name. Court Yard Hounds, featuring Robison for the first time as lead vocalist, released a debut album for [[Columbia Records]], the same label for which the Dixie Chicks has recorded, on May 4, 2010. The album debuted at No. 7 on the Billboard 200 chart, initially selling 61,000 copies. It has sold approximately 825,000 copies in the United States.<ref>[http://www.theboot.com/2010/05/12/zac-brown-band-pass-the-jar-charts/ Zac Brown Band Pull Double-Duty on Country Chart] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120227045047/http://www.theboot.com/2010/05/12/zac-brown-band-pass-the-jar-charts/ |date=February 27, 2012 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.roughstock.com/blog/lady-antebellum-zac-brown-band-miranda-lead-charts-this-wek |title=Lady Antebellum, Zac Brown Band & Miranda Lead Charts This Week &#124; New Country Music, Listen to Songs & Video |publisher=Roughstock.com |date=May 12, 2010 |access-date=February 10, 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131224084940/http://www.roughstock.com/blog/lady-antebellum-zac-brown-band-miranda-lead-charts-this-wek |archive-date=December 24, 2013 }}</ref>\n\n==Career==\n===Dixie Chicks===\n{{Main|Dixie Chicks}}\nEmily and Martie Erwin, now Emily Robison and Martie Maguire, founded the [[Dixie Chicks]] in 1989 with Robin Lynn Macy (lead vocals) and [[Laura Lynch (musician)|Laura Lynch]]. They released two independent albums before Macy left, and their third album was released with Lynch on lead vocals.  In 1995, Lynch left and was replaced by [[Natalie Maines]].  The group was then signed to [[Monument Records]] and released two hit albums, before departing from Monument in 2000 and founding their own label, Open Wide Records, in association with [[Columbia Records]]. They then released their third album [[Home (Dixie Chicks album)|Home]] to critical acclaim. During a London concert ten days before the [[2003 invasion of Iraq]], lead vocalist Maines stated, \" Just so you know, we're on the good side with y'all, we don't want this war, this violence, and we're ashamed that the President of the United States is from Texas\" (the trio's home state). The statement offended their core fan base who thought it rude and unpatriotic, and the ensuing controversy cost the group half of their concert audience attendance in the United States and led to accusations of the three women being un-American, as well as hate mail, death threats, and the public destruction of their albums in protest.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.today.com/popculture/dixie-chicks-shut-sing-toronto-wbna14822593 |title=Dixie Chicks 'Shut Up and Sing' in Toronto |date=September 13, 2006 | publisher=Today.com |access-date=October 8, 2006}}</ref>  The group followed a small hiatus with a live album and a documentary highlighting the maelstrom  created by Maines' comment entitled ''[[Dixie Chicks: Shut Up and Sing]]''. The Dixie Chicks released ''[[Taking the Long Way]]'' in 2006 which has since sold over 3 million copies and ultimately won five [[Grammy Awards]]. The Dixie Chicks were on hiatus from 2008 until in 2016 they reformed for a world tour.\n\n===Formation of Court Yard Hounds===\n[[File:Martie Maguire-Emily Robison.jpg|thumb|275px|right|L to R:Maguire and Robison, playing in concert as the [[Dixie Chicks]] in 2003]]\nCourt Yard Hounds was formed in 2009 when Maguire and Robison wanted to return to the studio however Maines was still reluctant to do so.\n\nThe duo's project was announced in January 2010 and the album features Emily on lead vocals.<ref name=cmt>{{cite web|author=Edward Morris |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1629456/two-members-of-dixie-chicks-releasing-album-without-natalie-maines.jhtml |title=News : Two Members of Dixie Chicks Releasing Album Without Natalie Maines |publisher=CMT |date=January 11, 2010 |access-date=February 19, 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140115031625/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1629456/two-members-of-dixie-chicks-releasing-album-without-natalie-maines.jhtml |archive-date=January 15, 2014 }}</ref> Robison said that the album is \"very personal\" and she would also be joined by singer-songwriter [[Jakob Dylan]] on a track called \"See You in the Spring\".<ref name=rs>{{cite magazine|author=David Browne |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/rockdaily/index.php/2010/01/15/dixie-chicks-plan-album-tour-with-court-yard-hounds-side-project/ |title=Pair of Dixie Chicks Plan Album, Tour as New Band Court Yard Hounds : Rolling Stone : Rock and Roll Daily |magazine=Rolling Stone |access-date=February 19, 2010}}{{dead link|date=August 2021|bot=medic}}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref>  The band signed to Columbia Records and released their self-titled debut album on May 4, 2010.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.courtyardhounds.com |title=The Official Court Yard Hounds Site |publisher=Court Yard Hounds |date=January 15, 2010 |access-date=February 19, 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140517075148/http://www.courtyardhounds.com/ |archive-date=May 17, 2014 }}</ref>  Their first public appearance as Court Yard Hounds was on March 18, 2010 at the [[Americana Music Association]]'s [[SXSW]] showcase in [[Austin, Texas]].<ref name=rs/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theboot.com/2010/01/19/court-yard-hounds/ |title=Dixie Chicks Sisters Return as Court Yard Hounds |publisher=The Boot |date=January 15, 2010 |access-date=February 19, 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120712221544/http://www.theboot.com/2010/01/19/court-yard-hounds |archive-date=July 12, 2012 }}</ref> With Robison on lead vocals she is backed up by her sister Martie, with other band members consisting of Natalie Maines' father, [[Lloyd Maines]], on guitar, and other members from the Dixie Chicks' backing band; the debut album was also recorded in Maguire's home studio.\n\nAccording to Maguire and Robison, the Dixie Chicks have not parted ways.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1629856/two-dixie-chicks-rename-themselves-as-court-yard-hounds.jhtml|title=Two Dixie Chicks Rename Themselves as Court Yard Hounds|date=January 15, 2010|work=CMT|access-date=February 19, 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140115031407/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1629856/two-dixie-chicks-rename-themselves-as-court-yard-hounds.jhtml|archive-date=January 15, 2014}}</ref> And still continue to make appearances including touring with the [[Eagles (band)|Eagles]] and [[Keith Urban]] in 2010 and appearing at selected events, such as the [[Calgary Stampede]], in 2013.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/rockdaily/index.php/2010/03/17/dixie-chicks-team-with-eagles-for-first-tour-in-four-years/|archive-url=https://archive.today/20120911181123/http://www.rollingstone.com/rockdaily/index.php/2010/03/17/dixie-chicks-team-with-eagles-for-first-tour-in-four-years/|url-status=dead|archive-date=September 11, 2012|title=Dixie Chicks Team With Eagles for First Tour in Four Years|date=March 17, 2010|magazine=Rolling Stone |access-date=April 3, 2010}}</ref>\n\nCourt Yard Hounds' second studio album, ''Amelita'', was released on July 16, 2013. \"Sunshine,\" the album's lead single, was released on June 10, 2013.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.musicrow.com/calendars-2/single-releases/ |title=Single Releases : MusicRow \u2013 Nashville's Music Industry Publication \u2013 News, Songs From Music City |publisher=Musicrow.com |date= December 29, 2008|access-date=July 15, 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140212165034/http://www.musicrow.com/calendars-2/single-releases/|archive-date=February 12, 2014}}</ref>\nIn 2015, the Dixie Chicks announced a tour of Europe for the following year, later also announcing a tour in North America, their first tour in years.\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Brandon_Jenkins_(musician)","to":"Brandon Jenkins (musician)"}],"pages":{"52679526":{"pageid":52679526,"ns":0,"title":"Brandon Jenkins (musician)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=July 2019}}\n\n{{Infobox person\n| name  = Brandon Jenkins\n| image  =\n| alt = \n| caption = \n| image_size= \n| birth_date = {{birth date|1969|6|7}}\n| birth_place = [[Tulsa, Oklahoma]], U.S.\n| death_date = {{death date and age|2018|3|2|1969|6|7}}\n| death_place = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| alma_mater = [[Oklahoma State University]]\n| occupation = {{flatlist|\n* Singer\n* songwriter\n* philanthropist \n}}\n| years_active = 1994\u20132018\n| spouse = Michele Jenkins\n| module = {{Infobox musical artist\n| embed           = yes  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| genre           = [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]]<br/>[[Texas Country]]\n| label           = Rainy Records<br />Red Dirt Legend Recordings<br />Remorseless Records<br />Explosive Records<br />[[Thirty Tigers]]<br />Smith Entertainment<br />E1 Music\n| associated_acts = [[Cross Canadian Ragweed]]<br />[[Jason Boland & The Stragglers]]<br/>[[Stoney LaRue]]<br/>[[Casey Donahew|Casey Donahew Band]]<br/>[[Josh Abbott Band]]\n| website         = {{URL|brandonjenkins.com}}\n}}\n}}\n'''Brandon Dean Jenkins''' (June 7, 1969 \u2013 March 2, 2018) was an American singer-songwriter and philanthropist. He was part of the [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt]] music genre.<ref name=RedDirtNation-TheFlag-2016>{{cite news|last1=Little|first1=Tonya|title=Brandon Jenkins: Austin to Nashville|url=http://www.reddirtnation.com/View-Article/AID/3158|work=Red Dirt Nation|date=March 21, 2016|access-date=29 December 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161228033707/http://www.reddirtnation.com/View-Article/AID/3158|archive-date=2016-12-28|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref name=NoDep-BlueBandana-2015>{{cite news|last1=Wenger Watson|first1=Julie|title=Brandon Jenkins Takes Red Dirt Digital with Blue Bandana|url=http://nodepression.com/interview/brandon-jenkins-takes-red-dirt-digital-blue-bandana|work=[[No Depression (magazine)|No Depression]]|date=October 26, 2015|access-date=December 27, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161228033414/http://nodepression.com/interview/brandon-jenkins-takes-red-dirt-digital-blue-bandana|archive-date=December 28, 2016|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref name=Oklahoman-2018>{{cite news|last1=McDonnell|first1=Brandy|title=Red dirt musician Brandon Jenkins dies following heart operation|url=http://newsok.com/red-dirt-musician-brandon-jenkins-dies-following-heart-operation/article/5585527|work=newsok.com|date=March 2, 2018}}</ref>\n\nJenkins performed in the Texas and Oklahoma regions, and he toured Europe on several occasions.<ref name=RedDirtNation-TheFlag-2016 /><ref name=TulsaWorld-Europe-2001>{{cite news|last1=Wooley|first1=John|title=Jenkins conquers Europe; Goodbye to Andy O|url=http://www.tulsaworld.com/archives/jenkins-conquers-europe-goodbye-to-andy-o/article_37cbfbed-9e74-54ff-aebe-6c1c37026c45.html|work=[[Tulsa World]]|date=September 6, 2001}}</ref> He often played 150 shows per year and shared the stage with [[Sunny Sweeney]], [[Zane Williams]], [[Cory Morrow]], [[Deana Carter]], [[Pat Green]], [[Willie Nelson]], [[The Mavericks]], and [[Kevin Welch]].<ref name=LubbockAJ-RedDirtLabel-2010 /><ref name=AllMusic-Bio>{{cite web|last1=MacNeil|first1=Jason|title=Brandon Jenkins: Biography & History|url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/brandon-jenkins-mn0000511685/biography|publisher=[[AllMusic]]}}</ref>\n\nOne of Jenkins' notable songs, \"Refinery Blues,\" was a biographical ballad about growing up near the Sand Springs Line, an area where oil refineries abound near the [[Arkansas River]] tributary of the [[Mississippi River]].<ref name=AltOklahoma-WoodyGuthrieRedDirtMusicians-2007 />\n\nJenkins was also a philanthropist as a supporter of the Red Dirt Relief Fund, a non-profit organization that supports musicians from the Red Dirt family of artists who face financial hardship.<ref name=RedDirtReliefFund-Stand-2014/>\n\n== Early life ==\nJenkins was born in [[Tulsa, Oklahoma]], to parents Wilma Jenkins (n\u00e9e Linthicum) and Dean Jenkins, a popular Tulsa radio disc jockey on stations [[KTBZ (AM)|KELi]] (where he was known as Dean Kelly) and [[KMOD-FM]].<ref name=Oklahoman-BrothersDirt-2009>{{cite news|last1=McDonnell|first1=Brandy|title=CD Review: Brandon Jenkins \"Brothers of the Dirt\"|url=http://newsok.com/cd-review-brandon-jenkins-brothers-of-the-dirt/article/3411096|work=[[The Oklahoman]]|date=October 23, 2009}}</ref><ref name=TuslaRadioMemories-DeanJenkins>{{cite web|title=Tulsa Radio: KTOW AM and FM|url=http://tulsatvmemories.com/ktow.html|website=Tulsa Radio Memories}}</ref>\n\nIn 1987, Jenkins graduated from [[Central High School (Tulsa, Oklahoma)|Central High School]] in Tulsa, where he was in the jazz band, sang in the choir, and taught himself guitar.<ref name=TulsaWorld-Faded-WesternSoul-1996>{{cite news|last1=Braudrick|first1=Nicole L.|title=Western Soul: Brandon Jenkins Reinvents His Style|url=http://www.tulsaworld.com/archives/western-soul-brandon-jenkins-reinvents-his-style/article_719221c7-43c9-5fe6-b490-00ed78fb33a1.html|work=[[Tulsa World]]|date=May 1, 1996}}</ref> In the 1980s, He attended [[Oklahoma State University]] in [[Stillwater, Oklahoma|Stillwater]].<ref name=Oklahoman-BrothersDirtFeature-2009>{{cite news|last1=McDonnell|first1=Brandy|title=Brandon Jenkins at home with 'Brothers of the Dirt'|url=http://newsok.com/brandon-jenkins-at-home-with-brothers-of-the-dirt/article/3403122|work=[[The Oklahoman]]|date=September 23, 2009}}</ref> During his time at OSU, Jenkins made life-long friends with many of his long-term musical collaborators in the [[Red Dirt (music)|Red Dirt Music]] community, including [[Cody Canada]], [[Mike McClure]], [[Stoney LaRue]], and Bleu Edmondson.<ref name=OKGazette-ProjectEleven-2012>{{cite news|last1=Boydston|first1=Joshua|title=Branded|url=http://okgazette.com/2012/02/21/branded/|work=[[Oklahoma Gazette]]|date=February 21, 2012}}</ref>\n\nJenkins' uncle was the [[Grammy Award]]-winning bass player, sound engineer, and producer, Gordon Shryock, who was known for his work with [[J. J. Cale]] and [[Leon Russell]], as well as [[Andrae Crouch]], [[Elvis Presley]], [[Natalie Cole]], and [[Dwight Yoakam]].<ref name=Oklahoman-BlueBandana-BlueDoor-2015>{{cite news|last1=McDonnell|first1=Brandy|title=Oklahoma native Brandon Jenkins brings red dirt to home state for tonight's Blue Door show|url=http://newsok.com/article/5467579|work=[[The Oklahoman]]|date=December 18, 2015}}</ref><ref name=TulsaWorld-ShryockHome-1989>{{cite news|last1=Wooley|first1=John|title=Gordon Shryock: Grammy Winner Is Home to Stay|url=http://www.tulsaworld.com/archives/gordon-shryock-grammy-winner-is-home-to-stay/article_29d137df-01ec-581b-8eda-9299d8f42143.html|work=[[Tulsa World]]|date=February 26, 1989}}</ref>\n\n== Career ==\nIn the early 1990s, Jenkins got his start recording for the Alabama-based record label, Rainy Records.<ref name=AltOklahoma-WoodyGuthrieRedDirtMusicians-2007>{{cite book|last1=Conner|first1=Thomas|editor1-last=Joyce|editor1-first=Davis D.|title=Alternative Oklahoma: Contrarian Views of the Sooner State|url=https://archive.org/details/alternativeoklah00joyc|url-access=limited|date=2007|publisher=University of Oklahoma Press|location=Norman|isbn=978-0-806-13819-0|pages=[https://archive.org/details/alternativeoklah00joyc/page/n109 89]\u201390, 100, 104\u2013105|chapter=Chapter 6: Getting Along: Woody Guthrie and Red Dirt Musicians|oclc=71222981}}</ref>\n\nIn 2003, Jenkins moved from Oklahoma to [[Austin, Texas]], where he lived until 2015.<ref name=Oklahoman-BrothersDirtFeature-2009 /><ref name=BMI-RepertoireProfile>{{cite web|title=Songwriter/Composer: Jenkins, Brandon Dean|url=http://repertoire.bmi.com/writer.asp?page=1&blnWriter=True&blnPublisher=True&blnArtist=True&fromrow=1&torow=25&affiliation=BMI&cae=186810450&keyID=605623&keyname=JENKINS+BRANDON+DEAN&querytype=WriterID|website=[[Broadcast Music, Inc.|BMI]]}}{{Dead link|date=October 2019 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref>\n\nIn 2005, Jenkins released ''Down in Flames'' and got a 3-year record deal for his Western Soul Records imprint to have his work distributed by [[RED Distribution|Sony/RED]]. The record came out on the [[Thirty Tigers]] label.<ref name=AngryCountry-DownInFlames-RED-2005>{{cite news|title=Brandon Jenkins Signs Sony/RED Deal|url=http://magazine.angrycountry.com/article.php?story=20050215143804604&query=brandon+jenkins|work=Angry Country Magazine|date=February 15, 2005|format=Press release|access-date=December 30, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161230092823/http://magazine.angrycountry.com/article.php?story=20050215143804604&query=brandon+jenkins|archive-date=December 30, 2016|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn 2008, Jenkins released ''Faster Than a Stone,'' which featured Travis Fite and Stoney LaRue.<ref name=RoughStock-FasterThanAStone-2008>{{cite news|last1=Sudhalter|first1=Michael|title=Brandon Jenkins \u2013 Faster Than A Stone|url=http://www.roughstock.com/news/2008/11/21326-brandon-jenkins-faster-than-a-stone|work=RoughStock|date=November 22, 2008}}</ref><ref name=TulsaWorld-FasterThanStone-2008>{{cite news|last1=Brown|first1=Mark|title=Q&A with Brandon Jenkins: Austin transplant Brandon Jenkins channels Tulsa|url=http://www.tulsaworld.com/archives/austin-transplant-brandon-jenkins-channels-tulsa/article_949b92f2-3219-5a2a-bc0e-9961780c0eb7.html|work=[[Tulsa World]]|date=November 26, 2008}}</ref>\n\nJenkins' 2009 album ''Brothers of the Dirt'' was a collaboration with many Red Dirt and Texas country scene artists: [[Cody Canada]] ([[Cross Canadian Ragweed]]), [[Stoney LaRue]], [[Jason Boland & The Stragglers|Jason Boland]], and [[Randy Rogers]].<ref name=AustinChron-BrothersDirt-Review-2009>{{cite news|last1=Moser|first1=Margaret|title=Brandon Jenkins|url=http://www.austinchronicle.com/music/2009-11-27/921312/|work=[[The Austin Chronicle]]|date=November 27, 2009}}</ref> The record was his first release on the independent label E1 Entertainment/Red Dirt Music Co.<ref name=LubbockAJ-RedDirtLabel-2010>{{cite news|last1=Woods|first1=Eric|title=Red Dirt rebel Brandon Jenkins still churning out chart-toppers|url=http://lubbockonline.com/entertainment/2010-08-27/red-dirt-rebel-brandon-jenkins-still-churning-out-chart-toppers|work=[[Lubbock Avalanche-Journal]]|date=August 27, 2010}}</ref> The song, \"Out of Babylon,\" sung by Jenkins and Canada, was a tribute to [[9/11]], while the song, \"Innocent Man,\" is a LaRue and Rogers contribution inspired by the [[John Grisham]] novel about [[Ron Williamson]], ''[[The Innocent Man: Murder and Injustice in a Small Town]].''<ref name=Oklahoman-BrothersDirt-2009 /> The song, \"Blood for Oil,\" was a protest song that focuses on [[George W. Bush]]'s involvement with [[Iraq War]].<ref name=Oklahoman-BrothersDirtFeature-2009 />\n\nIn 2011, Jenkins released a record he called ''Project Eleven,'' which was a digital only 11-track record released on the 10th anniversary of [[September 11 attacks|9/11]], with a single released on September 11, 2011.<ref name=OKGazette-ProjectEleven-2012 />\n\nIn 2015, Jenkins released the record, ''Blue Bandana,'' which was recorded over a period of two days in David Percefull's Yellow Dog Studios with a full band capturing a live sound in one day and the engineering and mastering done over the next day.<ref name=Oklahoman-BlueBandana-BlueDoor-2015 /> The record was released in a digital only format, with a limited number of physical versions available.<ref name=NoDep-BlueBandana-2015 /><ref name=Oklahoman-BlueBandana-BlueDoor-2015 />\n\nAlso in 2015, Jenkins released ''Brandon Jenkins @ Radio Recorders,'' which he recorded for Pride Hutchison and Dale Lawton's Tulsa-based label, Explosive Records.<ref name=Oklahoman-BlueBandana-BlueDoor-2015 /> The record was made in 2006 in the Southern California record studio called Radio Recorders.<ref name=OKMag-ExplosiveSounds-2015/> Since Jenkins' music was firmly in the Texas country genre, this record was held onto for release, some nine years later.<ref name=OKMag-ExplosiveSounds-2015>{{cite news|last1=Wooley|first1=John|title=Explosive Sounds: Oklahoma native and Texas country artist Brandon Jenkins releases two albums recorded nine years apart|url=http://www.okmag.com/blog/2015/11/20/explosive-sounds/|work=Oklahoma Magazine|date=November 20, 2015}}</ref>\n\nJenkins recorded ''The Flag,'' in 2016 which again with long-time collaborator, Dave Percefull.<ref name=RedDirtNation-TheFlag-2016 /> This was recorded in [[Wimberley, Texas|Wimberley]], Texas, in the [[Texas Hill Country]], and features Dony Wynn, Bukka Allen (son of [[Terry Allen (artist)|Terry Allen]]) on accordion, and Kim Deschamps on lap steel and dobro.<ref name=RedDirtNation-TheFlag-2016 /> In 2016, Jenkins moved from Austin to [[Nashville, Tennessee]], where his career would be based from until his death in 2018.<ref name=RedDirtNation-TheFlag-2016 />\n\n=== Songwriting ===\nJenkins' song \"My Feet Don't Touch The Ground\" was featured on [[Pete Anderson]]'s 2003 ''A Country West of Nashville'' album. The song garnered him an Emerging Artists in Music Award.<ref name=\"mtv\">{{Cite web |url=http://www.mtv.com/artists/brandon-jenkins-1/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161228032824/http://www.mtv.com/artists/brandon-jenkins-1/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=December 28, 2016 |title=Brandon Jenkins |publisher=MTV |access-date=December 29, 2016}}</ref> The song was placed 8th on the list of \"The 50 Best Red Dirt Texas Country Songs\" of the ''[[Dallas Observer]],'' and helped his career significantly.<ref name=DallasObserver-50BestRedDirt-2015>{{cite news|last1=McCarthy|first1=Amy|last2=Dearmore|first2=Kelly|title=The 50 Best Red Dirt Texas Country Songs|url=http://www.dallasobserver.com/music/the-50-best-red-dirt-texas-country-songs-7055741|work=[[Dallas Observer]]|date=February 16, 2015}}</ref>\n\nFellow Red Dirt artists Bleu Edmondson (\"Finger on the Trigger\") and [[Stoney LaRue]] (\"Feet Don't Touch The Ground\") recorded and performed songs written by Jenkins.<ref name=AltOklahoma-WoodyGuthrieRedDirtMusicians-2007 /> The song, \"Feet Don't Touch The Ground,\" was praised by [[KKCN]] as being one of the top 5 recorded songs by [[Stoney LaRue]],<ref name=KKCN-StoneyLaRue-Top5Songs-2012>{{cite news|last1=Stubbs|first1=Tommy|title=Top 5 Songs Ever Released By Stoney LaRue|url=http://103kkcn.com/top-5-songs-ever-released-by-stoney-larue/|publisher=[[KKCN]]|date=July 24, 2012}}</ref><ref name=RoadGoesOnForever-Music-2010>{{cite book|last1=Hessman|first1=Jake|title=The Road Goes on Forever|date=2010|publisher=iUniverse|location=Bloomington, IN|isbn=978-1-4502-3906-6|pages=272\u2013273|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=eL33O_fpfLwC&q=brandon+jenkins|chapter=The Music}}</ref> and features on his album ''Live at Billy Bob's Texas''. His song \"Down in Flames,\" co-written by [[Stoney LaRue]], appeared on ''[[The Red Dirt Album]]''.<ref name=AltOklahoma-WoodyGuthrieRedDirtMusicians-2007 />\n\nOne of Jenkins' notable songs, \"Refinery Blues,\" was a biographical ballad about growing up near the Sand Springs Line, an area where oil refineries about the [[Arkansas River]] tributary of the [[Mississippi River]].<ref name=AltOklahoma-WoodyGuthrieRedDirtMusicians-2007 /> The song describes the devastating effect the refineries and their pollutants had on generations of families in the area.<ref name=AltOklahoma-WoodyGuthrieRedDirtMusicians-2007 />\n\nIn addition to writing hits for several of his fellow \"brothers of the dirt,\" Jenkins had songs at the top of the Texas Music Radio Charts.<ref name=TxMusicChart-2007>{{cite web|title=Texas Music for the Country \u2013 Chart: August 13, 2007|url=http://www.texasmusicchart.com/Pages/Chart.htm|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070814011905/http://www.texasmusicchart.com/Pages/Chart.htm|archive-date=August 14, 2007|date=August 14, 2007}}</ref>\n\n== Influences ==\nJenkins cited the influence of the \"[[Tulsa Sound]]\" of [[J. J. Cale]] and [[Leon Russell]] on his songs and said that the songwriting gives him the most satisfaction.<ref name=Oklahoman-BlueBandana-BlueDoor-2015 /><ref name=FACM-Unmended-Interview-2002>{{cite news|last1=Dufour|first1=Florent|title=Interview: Brandon Jenkins|url=http://facm.free.fr/interjenkins.htm|work=French Association of Country Music (FACM)|year=2002|language=fr}}</ref>\n\nJenkins also cited the life and music of [[Woody Guthrie]] as being an important part of his approach to music and focusing on people and their lives in the Oklahoma region.<ref name=AltOklahoma-WoodyGuthrieRedDirtMusicians-2007 />\n\n== Personal life ==\nJenkins went by the nickname of Red Dirt Legend.<ref name=RedDirtNation-TheFlag-2016 /><ref name=LoneStarMag-BlueBandana-Review-2015>{{cite news|last1=Poet|first1=J.|title=Brandon Jenkins: \"Blue Bandana\"|url=http://lonestarmusicmagazine.com/brandon-jenkins-blue-bandana/|work=Lone Star Music Magazine|date=December 24, 2015}}</ref> He was married to Michele Angelique Jenkins until his death in 2018.<ref name=\"Obit\"/>\n\nJenkins was a supporter of the Red Dirt Relief Fund, a non-profit organization that supports musicians from the Red Dirt family of artists who face financial hardship.<ref name=RedDirtReliefFund-Stand-2014>{{cite news|title=\"Stand\" Song Project benefits RDRF|url=http://www.reddirtrelieffund.org/blog/stand/|work=Red Dirt Relief Fund|date=April 1, 2014|format=Press release}}</ref><ref name=Oklahoman-RedDirtReliefFund-2014>{{cite news|last1=McDonnell|first1=Brandy|title=Red Dirt Rangers and all-star lineup of Oklahoma musicians recording song for Red Dirt Relief Fund|url=http://newsok.com/red-dirt-rangers-and-all-star-lineup-of-oklahoma-musicians-recording-song-for-red-dirt-relief-fund/article/3946875|work=[[The Oklahoman]]|date=March 25, 2014}}</ref>\n\nOn February 21, 2018, Jenkins was hospitalized in Nashville and underwent surgery to replace his [[aorta]] and [[aortic valve]].<ref name=\"OKN\">{{cite web|url=http://newsok.com/red-dirt-musician-brandon-jenkins-dies-following-heart-operation/article/5585527|title=Red dirt musician Brandon Jenkins dies following heart operation|publisher=NewsOK|date=March 2, 2018|accessdate=March 2, 2018}}</ref> After the procedure, he experienced surgical complications and remained hospitalized until his death on March 2, 2018, at the age of 48.<ref name=\"Obit\">{{cite web|url=http://www.tulsaworld.com/scene/music/red-dirt-music-artist-brandon-jenkins-dies/article_56755311-848a-5d8d-a7b5-0a74bc8e473f.html|title=Red dirt music artist Brandon Jenkins dies|publisher=Tulsa World|date=March 2, 2018|accessdate=March 2, 2018}}</ref><ref name=\"OKN\"/>\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" (born 1974)}}\n{{Use American English|date=October 2020}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=February 2021}}\n{{Infobox musical artist \n| name            = Natalie Maines\n| image           = Natalie Maines in Austin, Texas.jpg\n| caption         = Maines in [[Austin, Texas|Austin]], Texas, 2006\n| landscape       = Yes\n| background      = solo_singer\n| birth_name      = Natalie Louise Maines\n| alias [[Columbia Records|Columbia]]\n}}\n|current_member_of = [[The Chicks]]\n| website          = {{URL|nataliemainesmusic.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Natalie Louise Maines'''<ref name=\"Dickerson\">{{cite book| last=Dickerson| first=James L.| year=2000| title=Dixie Chicks: Down-Home and Backstage| publisher=Taylor Trade Publishing| location=Dallas, Texas| isbn=978-0-87833-189-5 | url-access=registration| url=https://archive.org/details/dixiechicksdownh00dick}}</ref> (born October 14, 1974)<ref>{{cite news|title=Monitor|newspaper=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|publisher=[[Time Inc.]]|date=October 12\u201319, 2012|issue=1228/1229|page=23}}</ref><ref name=\"allmusicbio\">{{cite web| url = http://www.allmusic.com/artist/natalie-maines-mn0000372037/biography|title=Natalie Maines Biography |first=Thom|last= Jurek|publisher=[[AllMusic.com]]| access-date= July 4, 2017}}</ref> is an American musician. She is the lead vocalist for the country band [[the Chicks]].\n\nIn 1995, after leaving [[Berklee College of Music]], Maines was recruited by the Dixie Chicks to replace their lead singer, Laura Lynch. With Maines as lead vocalist, the band earned 10 [[Country Music Association Awards]] and 13 [[Grammy Award]]s for their work between 1998 and 2007.\n\nIn 2006, with Maines still acting as lead singer, the Dixie Chicks released ''[[Taking the Long Way]]''. The album subsequently won five [[Grammy Awards]] (including [[Grammy Award for Album of the Year|Album of the Year]]). After dropping the \"Dixie\", the Chicks new album ''[[Gaslighter (album)|Gaslighter]]'' was released on July 17, 2020. As a solo artist, Maines released the album, ''[[Mother (Natalie Maines album)|Mother]]'', on May 7, 2013.\n\n== Early life ==\nMaines was born in [[Lubbock, Texas]], to country musician and producer [[Lloyd Maines]] and Tina May Maines. She attended Nat Williams Elementary School in Lubbock, where her second grade teacher recalls being told by Maines during a math lesson, \"Teacher, I don't need to learn this stuff\u2014I'm gonna be a star.\"<ref name=\"Dickerson\" /> Maines was a cheerleader while attending O. L. Slaton Junior High School,<ref name=\"Dickerson\" />  and graduated in 1992 from [[Lubbock High School]] where she had participated in the school [[choir]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.amc-music.com/musicmaking/play@school/artists.htm |title=Play at School |publisher=American Music Conference |access-date=April 15, 2007 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070928211031/http://www.amc-music.com/musicmaking/play@school/artists.htm |archive-date=September 28, 2007 }}</ref> Maines has described growing up in conservative [[Texas]], saying \"I always rebelled against that. My parents sent me and my sister to public minority schools so I always felt like a hippie and a rebel. ... As a teenager I always loved not thinking in the way I knew the majority of people thought. I always stood up for minorities. ... I've always stood up for homosexuals. I just always had these really strong convictions about doing so.\"<ref name=\"Heysen\">Heysen, Kristen. (October 8, 2006) [http://www.news.com.au/adelaidenow/story/0,22606,20541859-5006343,00.html Not ready to make nice] AdelaideNow. Retrieved April 3, 2007.</ref>\n\nFollowing the completion of high school, Maines attended several colleges. She spent two semesters pursuing an undeclared major at [[West Texas A&M University|West Texas A&M]] where her studies focused heavily on radio, then a year and a half at [[South Plains College]]. One of Maines's instructors at South Plains, and a former member of [[The Maines Brothers Band]], Cary Banks, recalled \"She was mostly into [[rock'n'roll]], [[rhythm and blues]] ... [[alternative rock]].\" When Banks encountered Maines on campus, he said that she usually needed to vent a little steam. \"She would get into a lot of political arguments\" at the predominantly Republican school, and was a fan of Texas Governor [[Ann Richards]]. \"She's always been opinionated and hardheaded like her dad.\"<ref name=\"Dickerson\" />  In December 1994, Maines auditioned for and received a full vocal scholarship to Berklee College of Music. She pursued the diploma program at Berklee but dropped out before the completion of her studies. Even though Maines is from Lubbock, home of [[Texas Tech University]], she attended only one class at the school, a 1995 summer course in \"Introductory Wildlife\".<ref name=\"Dickerson\" />\n\n== Career ==\nMaines's first professional recording was lead vocals on the song \"White Women's Clothes\" on Andy Wilkinson's album \"Charlie Goodnight's Life in Poetry and Song.\" Maines's first commercially released work was [[backing vocalist|background vocals]] on [[Pat Green]]'s debut album, ''Dancehall Dreamer'', produced by her father Lloyd Maines and released in 1995. At the end of 1995, at age 21, Maines joined the all-female [[country music]] band, the then named [[Dixie Chicks]], which had been performing since 1989, but which had been unsuccessful in gaining more than local attention. Maines replaced founding lead singer Laura Lynch.  She plays guitar and bass in concert in the band.<ref>{{cite web |last=Davis |first=Rob |url=http://dixiechicksfaq.homestead.com/files/chicks.htm#_28.__What |title=Dixie Chicks FAQ No.&nbsp;30 |access-date=April 12, 2007}}</ref>\n\nMaines co-wrote four tracks for The Chicks' first three albums, including the ''[[Billboard charts|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs|Hot Country Singles & Tracks]] chart number one hit \"[[Without You (Dixie Chicks song)|Without You]]\" on ''[[Fly (Dixie Chicks album)|Fly]]''. Maines was a primary songwriter on all 14 tracks of the band's 2006 album ''[[Taking the Long Way]]'' which peaked on the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] chart at No.&nbsp;1. ''Taking the Long Way'' has the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] single \"[[Not Ready to Make Nice]]\", (Maines, Strayer, Erwin, Wilson) hitting No.&nbsp;4<ref name=\"Billboard\">{{cite magazine|url={{BillboardURLbyName|artist=dixie chicks|chart=all}} |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070929125545/http://{{billboardurlbyname|artist=dixie/}} |archive-date=September 29, 2007 |title=Dixie Chicks: Singles |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=June 17, 2007 |url-status=dead }}</ref> and for which the band won the songwriting Grammy Award, for [[Grammy Award for Song of the Year|Song of the Year]]. Maines considers the songwriting she did for ''Taking the Long Way'' \"pure therapy\" after the controversy that ensued over a comment Maines made from the stage in London that criticized U.S. President [[George W. Bush]].<ref name=\"Burkeman\">{{cite news |last=Burkeman |first=Oliver |date=March 25, 2006 |url=https://www.theguardian.com/usa/story/0,,1739311,00.html |title=Dixie Chicks turn death threats to song |newspaper=The Guardian |access-date=March 18, 2007}}</ref> \"Everything felt more personal this time\", Maines said about the album, \"there's just more maturity, depth, intelligence. ... [These songs] feel more grown-up.\"<ref>{{cite magazine |last=Cohen |first=Jonathan |date=March 10, 2006 |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/59125/dixie-chicks-get-personal-on-long-way |title=Dixie Chicks Get Personal On 'Long Way' |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=June 1, 2007}}</ref>\n\nMaines collaborates with other musical artists, both as a member of the Chicks and an individual singer. The Chicks first worked with [[Sheryl Crow]] in 1999 while performing for the concert tour [[Lilith Fair]].<ref>{{cite web |last=Rosen |first=Craig |date=December 3, 1999 |url=http://music.yahoo.com/read/news/12032703 |title=Dixie Chicks And Sheryl Crow Prove They're Gutsy Women |publisher=Yahoo!Music |access-date=June 1, 2007}}</ref> Since then, the Chicks have worked with Crow on her ''[[Sheryl Crow and Friends: Live from Central Park]]'' album, a Crow remixed version of \"[[Landslide (Fleetwood Mac song)|Landslide]]\" performed by the Chicks, and the Chicks' song \"Favorite Year\" from ''Taking the Long Way''.  Maines has performed with artists including Pat Green, [[Charlie Robison]], [[Yellowcard]], [[Stevie Nicks]], [[Patty Griffin]], [[Neil Diamond]], [[Eddie Vedder]], [[Pete Yorn]] and [[Ben Harper]].\n\nOn May 7, 2013, Maines released a solo album entitled ''[[Mother (Natalie Maines album)|Mother]]''.<ref name=\"tasteofcountry.com\">{{Cite web|url=https://tasteofcountry.com/dixie-chicks-natalie-maines-pink-floyd-mother-video/|title=Dixie Chicks' Natalie Maines Covers Pink Floyd's 'Mother'|first=Cory|last=Stromblad|website=Taste of Country|date=July 19, 2012 }}</ref><ref name=\"twitter.com\">{{Cite web|url=https://twitter.com/1NatalieMaines/status/281263948551057408|title=@JRig2010 @tray2276 May 7th.|first=Natalie|last=Maines|date=December 18, 2012}}</ref> This was Maines's first album since the Chicks hiatus started in 2007. The album was co-produced by [[Ben Harper]]. The album contains Maines's interpretation of several cover songs, including [[Pink Floyd]]'s [[Mother (Pink Floyd song)|\"Mother\"]], [[Eddie Vedder]]'s \"Without You\", and [[Jeff Buckley]]'s \"Lover, You Should've Come Over\". She also sings about motherhood, [[feminism]], and painful relationships.<ref name=\"tasteofcountry.com\" /><ref name=\"twitter.com\" /><ref>{{cite web|title=Natalie Maines: A Country-Music Rebel Rocks On Her Own|date=May 8, 2013|url=http://wunc.org/post/natalie-maines-country-music-rebel-rocks-her-own|publisher=North Carolina Public Radio|access-date=June 16, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=First Listen: Natalie Maines, 'Mother'|url=https://www.npr.org/2013/04/28/179030765/first-listen-natalie-maines-mother|publisher=NPR Music|access-date=June 16, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|title=Natalie Maines: A Dixie Chick Declares War on Nashville |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/natalie-maines-a-dixie-chick-declares-war-on-nashville-20130530|magazine=Rolling Stone|access-date=June 16, 2013}}</ref>\n\nIn September 2015, Maines was inducted into the [[West Texas Walk of Fame]].  The ceremony took place at [[Lubbock High School]] from where she graduated in 1992.<ref>{{cite web |title=Natalie Maines, Jo Harvey Allen headed for West Texas Walk of Fame |url=https://www.kcbd.com/story/29442793/natalie-maines-jo-harvey-allen-headed-for-west-texas-walk-of-fame/ |website=KCBD.com |date=June 30, 2015 |access-date=28 December 2023}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=WEST TEXAS WALK OF FAME INDUCTEES |url=https://civiclubbock.org/walk-of-fame/list-of-inductees/ |website=Civic Lubbock |access-date=28 December 2023}}</ref>\n\n== Philanthropic works ==\nMaines has participated in various fundraising and awareness events. They include:\n* Legendary Bingo (August 23, 2007): Maines participated in \"Legendary Bingo\", a [[Bingo (US)|US bingo]] game hosted by [[drag queens]] and held weekly in Los Angeles. Proceeds from the event go to special charity interests; when Maines participated in the event, the proceeds benefited the \"Voice for the Animals Foundation\".<ref name=\"bingo\">{{cite web |url=http://omg.yahoo.com/bingos-no-drag-for-dixie-chick-natalie-maines/news/1925 |title=Bingo's No Drag For Dixie Chick Natalie Maines |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070825144911/http://omg.yahoo.com/bingos-no-drag-for-dixie-chick-natalie-maines/news/1925 |archive-date=August 25, 2007 }}</ref>\n* St. Jude Benefit (June 12, 2008): Maines attended \"Scrabble Under The Stars\" in [[Beverly Hills, California|Beverly Hills]], California. The event benefits [[St. Jude Children's Research Hospital]]. Scrabble boards autographed by celebrity attendees, including Maines, were auctioned through June 30, 2008.<ref name=\"scrabble\">{{cite web |url=http://www.clothesoffourback.org/product_info.php?products_id=1390 |title=Clothes Off Our Back Autographed Scrabble Boards |access-date=July 23, 2008 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080707071759/http://www.clothesoffourback.org/product_info.php?products_id=1390 |archive-date=July 7, 2008 }}</ref>\n* [[David Lynch Foundation]]: Maines with the Dixie Chicks was the headline performer at a benefit night honoring [[Rick Rubin]] at the [[Beverly Wilshire Hotel]] in February 2014.<ref>{{cite web|last=Willman |first=Chris |title=Dixie Chicks, Russell Simmons Meditate on Rick Rubin's Greatness at David Lynch Foundation Event |website=[[The Hollywood Reporter]] |url=http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/dixie-chicks-russell-simmons-meditate-684492 |access-date=April 27, 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140304083118/http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/dixie-chicks-russell-simmons-meditate-684492 |archive-date=March 4, 2014 |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\n== Personal life ==\n[[File:Natalie Maines of the Dixie Chicks in Glawgow by deebeeandswivel.jpg|thumb|Maines in Glasgow 2003]]\nIn 1997, Maines married her [[South Plains College]] boyfriend, bassist Michael Tarabay, and the couple moved to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]], Tennessee. Within two years they filed for divorce, citing irreconcilable differences.<ref name=\"Dickerson\" />\n\nMaines met actor [[Adrian Pasdar]] in May 1999 at the wedding of bandmate [[Emily Erwin]] to Charlie Robison. Maines and Pasdar married on June 24, 2000, at [[A Little White Wedding Chapel]] in [[Las Vegas]].<ref>[http://www.nyrock.com/worldbeat/06_2000/062600.asp \"Dixie Chick Natalie Maines Weds Adrian Pasdar in Early Morning Vegas Ceremony\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101218221613/http://www.nyrock.com/worldbeat/06_2000/062600.asp |date=December 18, 2010}}, NY Rock, June 26, 2000</ref><ref>[https://web.archive.org/web/20121023215957/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1472621/natalie-maines-gets-hitched.jhtml \"Natalie Maines Gets Hitched\"], [[Country Music Television|CMT]], June 26, 2000</ref><ref name=\"Why\">Hatton, Spencer (November 26, 2006). \"Why rent a castle when you've got the King?\", ''[[Yakima Herald-Republic]]'', p. B1.</ref> They have two sons.<ref>Dixie Chicks. [https://web.archive.org/web/20080225075202/http://www.frontpagepublicity.com/dxc/content/personalfacts.html Dixie Chicks: Taking the Long Way: Dates & Facts] Dixie Chicks Official website. Retrieved April 19, 2007.</ref> During her marriage, Maines referred to herself as Natalie Pasdar.<ref name=\"Kopple\">Kopple, Barbara; Peck, Cecilia. (2006) [[Dixie Chicks: Shut Up and Sing]] Documentary.</ref>  Maines filed for divorce in July 2017; it was finalized in December 2019.<ref>[https://www.eonline.com/news/864775/dixie-chicks-singer-natalie-maines-files-for-divorce-from-adrian-pasdar-after-17-years-of-marriage \"Dixie Chicks Singer Natalie Maines Settles Divorce From Adrian Pasdar\" E! News, Retrieved August 26, 2022]</ref>  The events leading to her divorce inspired multiple songs on the 2020 album ''[[Gaslighter (album)|Gaslighter]]''.<ref>[https://www.allure.com/story/dixie-chicks-april-2020-cover-interview/amp \"The Dixie Chicks on the Price of Being Genuine\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220612003826/https://www.allure.com/story/dixie-chicks-april-2020-cover-interview/amp | date=June 12, 2022}}</ref>\n\nMaines practices [[Transcendental Meditation technique|transcendental meditation]].<ref>{{cite web|last=Willman |first=Chris |title=Dixie Chicks, Russell Simmons Meditate on Rick Rubin's Greatness at David Lynch Foundation Event |website=[[The Hollywood Reporter]] |url=http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/dixie-chicks-russell-simmons-meditate-684492 |access-date=April 27, 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140304083118/http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/dixie-chicks-russell-simmons-meditate-684492 |archive-date=March 4, 2014 |quote=Maines is a TM-er, it turns out. Eighteen years ago, she told the crowd, she and fiddler Martie Maguire went to learn TM together |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\n== Controversies ==\n\n=== Iraq War criticism and aftermath ===\n{{Main|Dixie Chicks comments on George W. Bush}}\nOn March 10, 2003, nine days before the invasion of Iraq, the Dixie Chicks performed at the [[Shepherd's Bush Empire]] theater in London, England, UK. It was the first concert of their [[Top of the World Tour]] in support of their sixth album, ''[[Home (Dixie Chicks album)|Home]].''<ref name=\":7\">{{Cite magazine|last=Dansby|first=Andrew|date=March 17, 2003|title=Fans Turn on Dixie Chicks|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/fans-turn-on-dixie-chicks-251772/|access-date=June 14, 2020|magazine=Rolling Stone|language=en-US}}</ref> Introducing their song \"[[Travelin' Soldier]]\", Maines told the audience the band they did not support the upcoming [[2003 Invasion of Iraq|Allied invasion of Iraq]] and were \"ashamed\" that [[President George W. Bush]] was from Texas.<ref name=\"Guardian32\">Campbell, Duncan (2003). [https://www.theguardian.com/international/story/0,3604,943170,00.html {{\"'}}Dixie sluts' fight on with naked defiance\"] ''Guardian Unlimited''. Retrieved April 13, 2006.</ref><ref name=\"Guardian\">{{cite news|last=Clarke|first=Betty|date=March 12, 2003|title=\"The Dixie Chicks\" concert review|newspaper=The Guardian|url=http://arts.guardian.co.uk/reviews/story/0,,912236,00.html|access-date=January 22, 2007}}</ref>\n\nMany American country music listeners supported the war, and Maines's remark triggered a backlash in the United States.<ref name=\"Guardian32\" /> The Dixie Chicks were [[Blacklisting|blacklisted]] by thousands of country radio stations,<ref name=\":2\">{{cite magazine|last=Sachs|first=Andrea|date=May 21, 2006|title=Chicks In the Line of Fire \u2013 Printout \u2013 TIME|url=http://www.time.com/time/magazine/printout/0,8816,1196419,00.html|magazine=Time.com|archive-url=https://archive.today/20121206045558/http://www.time.com/time/magazine/printout/0,8816,1196419,00.html|archive-date=December 6, 2012|access-date=December 26, 2010|url-status=dead}}</ref> and the band members received death threats.<ref>{{cite news|date=April 24, 2003|title=Dixie Chicks 'get death threats'|work=BBC News|url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/2972043.stm|url-status=live|access-date=March 2, 2009|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090829151806/http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/2972043.stm|archive-date=August 29, 2009}}</ref> Maines issued an apology, saying her remark had been disrespectful; in 2006 she rescinded the apology, saying she felt Bush deserved no respect.<ref name=\":2\" /> The backlash damaged sales of their music and sales of their next album and tour.<ref name=\"auto\">{{Cite web|title=Dixie Chicks: Home|url=https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/dixie-chicks-home/|access-date=June 14, 2020|website=Pitchfork|language=en}}</ref>[[File:Natalie-Maines by Ron Baker 2006.jpg|thumb|Maines performing with the Dixie Chicks during their \"[[Accidents & Accusations Tour]]\" December 4, 2006]]\nAt the first US concert after Maines's comment, she said from the stage, \"They told me that you may not come, but I knew you'd come because we have the greatest fans in the whole wide world.\"<ref name=\"DemocracyNow\">Goodman, Amy. (February 15, 2007) [http://www.democracynow.org/article.pl?sid=07/02/15/1528222 \"Shut Up And Sing: Dixie Chicks' Big Grammy Win Caps Comeback From Backlash Over Anti-War Stance\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20071114015029/http://www.democracynow.org/article.pl?sid=07%2F02%2F15%2F1528222 |date=November 14, 2007 }} ''Democracy Now!''. Retrieved February 24, 2007.</ref><ref name=\"Mattingly\">Mattingly, David. (May 2, 2003) [http://www.cnn.com/2003/SHOWBIZ/Music/05/02/dixie.chicks.tour/index.html Fans turn out, cheer Dixie Chicks as U.S. tour opens] CNN. Retrieved March 20, 2007.</ref> Despite fan turnout at concerts, the Dixie Chicks began receiving death threats as circulation of the comment increased. Subsequently, security was heightened at all concert venues and metal detectors were installed where possible.<ref name=\"Burkeman\" /><ref>BBC. (April 24, 2003) [http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/2972043.stm Dixie Chicks 'get death threats']. Retrieved March 18, 2007.</ref> A death threat directed at Maines was received prior to the Dixie Chicks' concert of July 6, 2003, in [[Dallas, Texas]]. Maines described the threat as \"scary because ... it wasn't just somebody wanting to write a hate letter. ... It was somebody who obviously thought they had a plan.\" Security was heightened for the trip to and from the concert venue as well as at the arena.<ref>Associated Press. (May 11, 2006) [http://www.today.com/id/12745436 Dixie Chicks recall death threat] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200613142519/http://www.today.com/id/12745436 |date=June 13, 2020 }} Today.com. Retrieved March 18, 2007.</ref>\n\nOn May 21, 2006, while promoting the release of the album ''[[Taking the Long Way]]'', Maines recanted her 2003 apology to President Bush, saying, \"I don't feel that way anymore. I don't feel he is owed any respect whatsoever. ... If people are going to ask me to apologize based on who I am ... I don't know what to do about that. I can't change who I am.\"<ref name=\"Tryangiel\">Tryangiel, Josh. (May 21, 2006) [https://archive.today/20121206045558/http://www.time.com/time/magazine/printout/0,8816,1196419,00.html Chicks In the Line of Fire]. Retrieved March 18, 2007.</ref>\n\nMaines says she is not looking for more battles but that \"The Incident,\" as it is referred to by the Dixie Chicks, reminded her of how she \"felt in high school: to be angry, to be sure that you're right and that the things you do matter. You don't realize that you're not feeling those feelings until you do. And then you realize how much more interesting life is.\"<ref name=\"Tryangiel\" />\n\nTwo 2006 documentaries, ''[[Protesting the Dixie Chicks]]'' and ''[[Dixie Chicks: Shut Up and Sing|Shut Up And Sing]]'', deal with the controversy surrounding Maines's comment and the ensuing fallout. In an interview with ''[[The Daily Telegraph]]'' on June 15, 2006, regarding the fallout from her comment, Maines again stirred up controversy by stating:<blockquote>The entire country may disagree with me, but I don't understand the necessity for patriotism; Why do you have to be a patriot? About what? This land is our land? Why? You can like where you live and like your life, but as for loving the whole country ... I don't see why people care about patriotism.<ref>Sweeting, Adam. (15 June 2006) [https://web.archive.org/web/20060622082458/http://www.telegraph.co.uk/arts/main.jhtml?xml=/arts/2006/06/15/bmdixie15.xml How the Chicks survived their scrap with Bush] ''[[The Daily Telegraph]]''. Retrieved 18 March 2007.</ref></blockquote>\n\nIn 2007, the Dixie Chicks won three Grammys for \"[[Not Ready to Make Nice]]\" and two Grammys for ''Taking the Long Way'', receiving all five Grammys for which they were nominated. This was seen by some as vindication for the Dixie Chicks, who were shunned by country radio programmers after Maines's remarks about President Bush. As the Dixie Chicks accepted the album of the year award, Maines said, \"I think people are using their freedom of speech with all these awards. We get the message.\"<ref name=\"Moody\">Moody, Nekesa Mumbi. (February 12, 2007) [http://www.heraldtribune.com/apps/pbcs.dll/article?AID=/20070212/FEATURES/70212001/1015/FEATURES10 Dixie Chicks lead Grammys with 5 awards] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110605040204/http://www.heraldtribune.com/apps/pbcs.dll/article?AID=%2F20070212%2FFEATURES%2F70212001%2F1015%2FFEATURES10 |date=June 5, 2011 }} Associated Press. Retrieved March 18, 2007.</ref>\n\n=== Feud with Toby Keith ===\nMaines had a public feud with fellow country music superstar [[Toby Keith]] over the 2002 chart-topping country hit \"[[Courtesy of the Red, White and Blue]]\", as well as a comment Maines made about U.S. President George W. Bush during a March 2003 Dixie Chicks concert in London.\n\nMaines publicly criticized Keith's song \"Courtesy of the Red, White and Blue\" by saying, \"I hate it. It's ignorant, and it makes country music sound ignorant. It targets an entire culture\u2014and not just the bad people who did bad things. You've got to have some tact. Anybody can write, 'We'll put a boot in your ass.'\"<ref>''LA Daily News''. (August 8, 2002) [http://www.top40-charts.com/news.php?nid=3488 Natalie Maines (Dixie Chick member) Bashes Toby Keith's Patriotic Anthem]. Retrieved March 17, 2007.</ref> Keith responded by belittling Maines's songwriting skills with, \"I'll bury her. She has never written anything that has been a hit\"<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.buzzle.com/editorials/6-5-2003-41299.asp | archive-url=https://wayback.archive-it.org/all/20090316001744/http://www.buzzle.com/editorials/6-5-2003-41299.asp | url-status=usurped | archive-date=2009-03-16 | title=Dixie Chicks vs. Toby Keith }}</ref> and, \"That's what I do\u2014I write songs.\"<ref>CMT.com. (December 6, 2002) [https://web.archive.org/web/20040417102749/http://www.cmt.com/artists/news/1459027/12062002/keith_toby.jhtml Toby Keith Reacts to Maines's Comments in Upcoming CMT.com Interview]. Retrieved March 17, 2007.</ref>\n\nAfter Maines commented at a March 2003 Dixie Chicks concert at the Shepherd's Bush Empire theatre in London that the Dixie Chicks didn't want the [[Iraq War]] and were \"ashamed\" President Bush \"was from Texas\", Keith's 2003 \"[[Shock'n Y'all]]\" tour began displaying a backdrop showing a doctored photo of Maines with Iraqi dictator [[Saddam Hussein]].<ref name=\"BBCfreshrow\">BBC News. (June 3, 2003) [http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/2958450.stm Fresh Dixie Chicks row erupts]. Retrieved March 17, 2007.</ref> Shortly thereafter, on May 21, 2003, Maines wore a T-shirt with the letters \"F.U.T.K.\" written on the front while performing for the [[Academy of Country Music|Academy of Country Music Awards]] broadcast.<ref name=\"BBCfreshrow\" /> The Dixie Chicks website stated that the letters stood for \"Freedom, United, Together in Kindness\".<ref>Wolf, Buck. (April 26, 2005) [https://abcnews.go.com/Entertainment/WolfFiles/story?id=720819 Hilton vs. Richie: When Celebs Duke It Out \u2013 7. Dixie Chicks vs. Toby Keith] ABC News. Retrieved March 20, 2007.</ref> Many in the country music industry saw it as a veiled insult directed at Keith.<ref name=\"BBCfreshrow\" /> The audience at the award show also booed the Dixie Chicks numerous times, the loudest being when their nomination for the Entertainer of the Year award was read out, Toby Keith subsequently won the award. <ref name=\"BBC Awards\">BBC News. (May 22 2003)[http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/3049209.stm Dixie Chicks booed at music awards]. Retrieved September 19 2024.</ref>\n\nIn the 2006 documentary ''[[Dixie Chicks: Shut Up and Sing]]'', backstage footage prior to her appearance wearing the F.U.T.K. shirt recorded the conversation between Maines and Simon Renshaw and confirmed that the original intent of the shirt was in response to Keith's criticism of her: the letters stood for \"Fuck You Toby Keith\".<ref name=\"Kopple\" /> As of January 2007, Keith continued to refuse to say Maines's name and argues that the doctored photos displayed during his concerts were intended to express his feeling that Maines's criticism was tyrannical and a dictator-like attempt to squelch Keith's free speech.<ref>Guzman, Rafer. (January 28, 2007)\n[http://www.newsday.com/entertainment/music/ny-ettoby0128,0,6077773.story?coll=ny-music-headlines Toby Keith, angry American]. Retrieved March 18, 2007.  {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070516110755/http://www.newsday.com/entertainment/music/ny-ettoby0128%2C0%2C6077773.story?coll=ny-music-headlines |date=May 16, 2007 }}</ref>\n\n=== West Memphis Three lawsuit ===\nMaines and other members of The Dixie Chicks participated in a rally in Little Rock, Arkansas, in late 2007, in support of the [[West Memphis Three]], three imprisoned men convicted of the 1993 murder of three young boys in [[West Memphis, Arkansas]].  On August 19, 2011, Maines joined with [[Pearl Jam]] frontman [[Eddie Vedder]] in Jonesboro, Arkansas, supporting the release of the West Memphis Three.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.yahoo.com/entertainment/west-memphis-three-natalie-maines-eddie-vedder-arrive-131002608.html |title=West Memphis Three: Natalie Maines, Eddie Vedder Arrive at Court (Report) |date=August 19, 2011 |publisher=The Hollywood Reporter |access-date= September 22, 2020}}</ref>\n\n== Discography ==\n\n=== The Chicks ===\n{{Main|The Chicks discography}}\n\n=== Solo ===\n\n==== Studio albums ====\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Troy_Cartwright","to":"Troy Cartwright"}],"pages":{"52309298":{"pageid":52309298,"ns":0,"title":"Troy Cartwright","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American country music singer-songwriter (born 1990)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=July 2019}}\n{{BLP sources|date=January 2017}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Troy Cartwright\n| image           = Troy Cartwright.jpg\n| image_size      =\n| caption         =\n| origin          = [[Dallas]], Texas\n| genre           = Singer-songwriter, [[Country music|Country]], [[Texas country music]], [[Americana (music)]]\n| years_active    = 2013\u2013present<ref>{{cite web|title=About Troy Cartwright|url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/troy-cartwright/biography/|publisher=Country Music Television|accessdate=November 17, 2016}}{{dead link|date=July 2024|bot=medic}}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref>\n| label           = Warner Music Nashville\n| associated_acts = [[Rob Baird]]\n| website         = {{URL|www.troycartwright.com/}}\n}}\n'''Troy Cartwright''' (born April 3, 1990) is an American [[country music]] singer-songwriter. The [[Dallas]], Texas native currently resides in [[Nashville, Tennessee]].\n\n== Life and career ==\n=== Early life ===\nCartwright grew up in Dallas, Texas where he was given a guitar for his twelfth birthday and started penning his own songs shortly thereafter. By the time he hit high school, he was regularly playing in bars and local venues in town. A summer program at [[New York University]] exposed Cartwright to the world outside of Dallas and inspired him to head even further from home to attend the [[Berklee College of Music]] in [[Boston]], Massachusetts where he studied music business and songwriting. During college, he worked odd jobs in the music industry, including a stint as a wedding singer. Upon graduating in 2012, Cartwright moved back to Texas to pursue his own music career.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.berklee.edu/berklee-today/fall-2014/alumnotes|title=Alumnotes {{!}} Berklee College of Music|website=www.berklee.edu|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref>\n\n=== 2013\u20132015 ===\nSoon after returning to Dallas, Texas, he recorded an EP, ''Bull Run'', earning him recognition at the 2013 [[B. W. Stevenson]] Songwriting Competition.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://sceneintown.com/?p=13015|title=Cartwright takes B.W. Stevenson 2013 songwriter title|date=April 25, 2013|newspaper=Scene in Town|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref> The following year, he was the recipient of the 2014 Rising Star Texas Music Award.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.texasmusicawards.org/results/|title=TMA Results|website=texasmusicawards.org|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref> A performance with [[John Fullbright]] led Cartwright to [[Oklahoma]], where he collaborated with producer [[Wes Sharon]] on his 2015 self-titled full-length debut.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.dallasobserver.com/music/troy-cartwright-is-flying-high-on-a-texas-country-journey-7701872|title=Troy Cartwright Is Flying High on a Texas Country Journey|last=Dearmore|first=Kelly|date=October 20, 2015|newspaper=Dallas Observer|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref>\n\n=== 2016\u2013present ===\nRadio play coupled with extensive touring caught the ear of fellow Texas songwriter [[Rob Baird]], who offered to co-produce Cartwright's latest release, an EP titled 'Don't Fade', with Brian Douglas Phillips at Phillip's Austin-based Rattle Trap Studio, which released October 7, 2016.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.texasmusicpickers.com/troy-cartwright-set-impress-dont-fade-ep/|title=Troy Cartwright Set to Impress with \"Don't Fade\" EP {{!}} Texas Music Pickers|website=www.texasmusicpickers.com|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref> The new project played a part in helping him land an agency deal with [[William Morris Endeavor]] (WME).<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.musicrow.com/2016/08/industry-ink-apa-nashville-pennington-entertainment-wme-bud-light/|title=Industry Ink: APA Nashville, Pennington Entertainment, WME, Bud Light|date=August 12, 2016|newspaper=MusicRow \u2013 Nashville's Music Industry Publication \u2013 News, Songs From Music City|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref> 'Don't Fade' also garnered Cartwright debuts on numerous [[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] [[Billboard charts|music charts]] \u2013 No. 60 on the US Country Chart, No. 53 on the US Heatseekers Chart, and No. 8 on the Heatseekers South Central Chart.\n\nIn early 2017, Rolling Stone named Cartwright one of \"10 New Country Artists You Need to Know.\" Shortly thereafter, Cartwright moved to Nashville full-time to be closer to the songwriter community. Later that year, he signed a worldwide publishing deal with Warner/Chappell Music, the music publishing arm of Warner Music Group, and signed with Red Light Management. By June 2018, Warner Music Nashville announced that it had signed Cartwright to its label as a country music recording artist and songwriter. Later that year, Cartwright began working with Grammy Award-winning producer David Garcia on his next project.\n\nIn Summer of 2019, Cartwright released his first music through Warner Music Nashville with Love Like We Used To and Hung Up On You. SiriusXM The Highway selected Love Like We Used To as its \"YouTube Country Spotlight\" and added the song to its \"On The Horizon\" programming. In Fall of 2019, My First Beer was released, and Cartwright's latest release, Cake For Breakfast, was featured on Billboard's \"First Country,\" as one of the best new country songs of the week. Cartwright is currently releasing music and playing live shows across the country.\n\nCartwright has shared the stage and toured with several notable acts including [[Nitty Gritty Dirt Band]], [[Green River Ordinance (band)]], [[Turnpike Troubadours]], [[Randy Rogers Band]], [[William Clark Green]], [[Rob Baird]], [[Stoney LaRue]], [[Wade Bowen]], [[Sean McConnell]], [[Cody Jinks]] and more.\n\n== Discography ==\n{{BLP unreferenced section|date=January 2017}}\n\n=== Studio albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\" border=\"1\"\n|-\n! A Timeline of the Band\u2019s Rise, Hiatus and Return |url=https://countrynow.com/who-are-the-turnpike-troubadours-a-timeline-of-the-bands-rise-hiatus-and-return/ |access-date=2024-02-12 |website=Country Now |language=en-US}}</ref> They started their own imprint, Bossier City Records, in 2007 and have released six studio albums. Their self-titled 2015 album peaked at number 17 on the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]].\n\n==Career==\nThe band was formed in 2005 by [[Evan Felker]] and R.C. Edwards. Their debut album, ''Bossier City,'' was recorded a month after the formation of the band, in order to have a recording to sell at live shows. Felker later said the musical arrangements were \"not a good representation\" of what the band later became.<ref name=\"wofford\">{{cite news |last1=Wofford |first1=Jerry |title=Evan Felker of Turnpike Troubadours talks on the band's success ahead of its Cain's show |url=http://www.tulsaworld.com/blogs/scene/offbeat/evan-felker-of-turnpike-troubadours-talks-on-the-band-s/article_7e39eb72-2257-5186-8c9e-1fa7fc3dbe3b.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200220095042/https://www.tulsaworld.com/blogs/scene/offbeat/evan-felker-of-turnpike-troubadours-talks-on-the-band-s/article_7e39eb72-2257-5186-8c9e-1fa7fc3dbe3b.html |archive-date=20 February 2020 |accessdate=3 May 2018 |work=Tulsa World |language=en}}</ref> \n\nTheir sophomore album, ''Diamonds & Gasoline,'' followed in 2010.<ref name=\"Diamonds & Gasoline\">{{cite web | url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/diamonds-and-gasoline-mw0002023125 | title=''Diamonds & Gasoline'' | publisher=AllMusic | accessdate=April 10, 2022 | archive-date=April 9, 2022 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220409224351/https://www.allmusic.com/album/diamonds-and-gasoline-mw0002023125 | url-status=live }}</ref>  \n\nThe songs \"Easton and Main\" and \"Bossier City\" were re-recorded for their 2015 self-titled album.<ref name=\"wofford\" /> \n\nIn October 2017, the album ''[[A Long Way from Your Heart]]'' was released, peaking at number three on the [[Top Country Albums|''Billboard'' Top Country Albums]] chart.\n\nFollowing a string of poor performances in late 2018, stemming from Felker's insobriety, the band was forced to cancel 12 shows slated to be held in the weeks to follow, returning on November 30th to play at [[Moody Theater|ACL Live]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=Freeman |first=Jon |date=2018-10-30 |title=Turnpike Troubadours Cancel Concerts for 'Situation That Needs Our Complete Attention' |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/turnpike-troubadours-tour-cancelled-749742/ |access-date=2024-02-13 |website=Rolling Stone |language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Trigger |date=2018-12-01 |title=Turnpike Troubadours Make Return to the Stage in Austin - Saving Country Music |url=https://www.savingcountrymusic.com/turnpike-troubadours-make-return-to-the-stage-in-austin/ |access-date=2024-02-13 |website=www.savingcountrymusic.com |language=en-US}}</ref> Felker's personal battles continued the following year, spurring the band to cancel all remaining tour dates. It left the band's future undecided but noting a possible return to the stage once \"everyone is of strong mind, body and spirit and can deliver what our fans deserve.\"<ref>{{Cite web |last=Freeman |first=Jon |date=2019-05-31 |title=Turnpike Troubadours Cancel Tour Dates, Announce Hiatus |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/turnpike-troubadours-cancel-tour-hiatus-evan-felker-843072/ |access-date=2024-02-13 |website=Rolling Stone |language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Crutchmer |first=Josh |date=2023-05-03 |title=Turnpike Troubadours Talk Anticipated New Comeback Album and Real Reason Behind the Breakup |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nIn November 2021, the band's Instagram was cleaned of all previous posts and their website displayed only the band's logo and a message that read \"Coming Soon\".<ref>{{cite web |last1=Liebig |first1=Lorie |title=Turnpike Troubadours Reunite, Announce 2022 Show |url=https://theboot.com/turnpike-troubadours-reunite-announce-2022-show/ |publisher=The Boot |access-date=26 February 2023 |date=November 30, 2021}}</ref> In January 2022, the band announced their long-awaited reunion and return to live performances, holding their first shows on April 8\u20139, 2022 at [[Cain's Ballroom]].<ref>{{Cite web |date=2022-01-12 |title=Turnpike Troubadours will play Cain\u2019s Ballroom in Tulsa |url=https://www.fox23.com/news/turnpike-troubadours-will-play-cain-s-ballroom-in-tulsa/article_7f37a129-746e-59fd-9a8e-dccbc8d94608.html |access-date=2024-02-13 |website=www.fox23.com |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Crutchmer |first=Josh |date=2022-04-09 |title=Turnpike Troubadours Reunited to Play Their First Show in 3 Years -- Grown Men Cried |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/turnpike-troubadours-reunion-concert-review-1335286/ |access-date=2024-02-13 |website=Rolling Stone |language=en-US}}</ref> One month later, another two-night run of shows were held May 14\u201315 at [[Red Rocks Amphitheatre]].<ref>{{Cite magazine|last1=Crutchmer|first1=Josh|date=2021-11-30|title=Exclusive: Turnpike Troubadours Talk Unexpected Hiatus, Newfound Sobriety, and Surprise Reunion|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/turnpike-troubadours-reunion-evan-felker-interview-1264002/|access-date=2021-12-01|magazine=Rolling \n\nOn August 25, 2023 the band released their album ''A Cat in the Rain'' after releasing three earlier singles: \"Mean Old Sun,\" \"Chipping Mill,\" and \"Brought Me.\"<ref>{{Cite web |last=Winograd |first=Jeremy |date=2023-08-20 |title=Turnpike Troubadours \u2018A Cat in the Rain\u2019 Review |url=https://www.slantmagazine.com/music/turnpike-troubadours-a-cat-in-the-rain-album-review/ |access-date=2024-02-13 |website=Slant Magazine |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n== Musical style, composition, and influences ==\nCritically, the Turnpike Troubadours' musical style has been labeled as primarily [[country music]] and its respective subgenres, such as [[Red dirt (music)|red dirt]],<ref name=\"freeman\">{{cite web |last1=Freeman |first1=Jon |title=Turnpike Troubadours' Triumphant Return |url=https://www.spin.com/2023/08/turnpike-troubadours-interview-shooter-jennings/ |website=[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]] |access-date=November 12, 2023 |date=August 24, 2023}}</ref><ref name=\"wickstrom\">{{cite web |last1=Wickstrom |first1=Matt |title=CONCERT REVIEW: Turnpike Troubadours' Red Dirt Reunion Rocks Nashville's Ryman Auditorium |url=https://theboot.com/turnpike-troubadours-ryman-auditorium-review/ |website=The Boot |access-date=November 12, 2023 |date=August 2, 2022}}</ref><ref name=\"vonderhaar\">{{cite news |last1=Vonder Haar |first1=Pete |title=The Turnpike Troubadours Bring Red Dirt Country Back To Houston |url=https://www.houstonpress.com/music/review-turnpike-troubadours-at-white-oak-music-hall-13334577 |access-date=November 12, 2023 |date=May 8, 2022}}</ref> [[honky-tonk music|honky-tonk]],<ref name=\"wolgamott\">{{cite news |last1=Wolgamott |first1=L. Kent |title=Avett Brothers and Turnpike Troubadours combine for strong arena show in Lincoln |url=https://journalstar.com/life-entertainment/local/avett-brothers-turnpike-troubadours-lincoln-concert/article_90d975c6-430d-11ee-a7f1-af11a4381597.html |access-date=November 12, 2023 |work=[[Lincoln Journal Star]] |date=August 25, 2023}}</ref> [[Americana (music)|Americana]],<ref name=\"crutchmer\">{{cite web |last1=Crutchmer |first1=Josh |title=Jason Isbell Says Evan Felker's Comeback Spurred Him to Join Turnpike Troubadours' Arena Shows |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/turnpike-troubadours-jason-isbell-tour-dates-1234848752/ |website=[[Rolling Stone (magazine)|Rolling Stone]] |access-date=November 12, 2023 |date=October 9, 2023}}</ref> [[neotraditional country]],<ref name=\"cmac\">{{cite news |last1=C. Mac |first1=Sam |title=A guide to all the artists playing the Houston Rodeo this year |url=https://www.chron.com/culture/houston-rodeo/article/houston-rodeo-guide-17800433.php |access-date=November 12, 2023 |work=[[Houston Chronicle]] |date=February 28, 2023}}</ref> and [[country rock]].<ref name=\"stewart\"/> Mark Deming of [[AllMusic]] referred to the Turnpike Troubadours as a \"country-leaning [[roots rock]] band,\" with elements of political [[folk music]], honky-tonk, [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]], [[Cajun music]], and [[Rock music|rock]].<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web|url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/mn0002038565|title=Turnpike Troubadours Biography|last=Leggett|first=Steve|work=[[Allmusic]]|accessdate=July 12, 2012|archive-date=March 3, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150303152432/http://www.allmusic.com/artist/mn0002038565|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nIn an interview with the ''[[Chicago Tribune]]'', band co-founder and bassist RC Edwards identified the band's musical style as honky-tonk.<ref name=\"stewart\">{{cite news |last1=Stewart |first1=Allison |title=Turnpike Troubadours are giving that road thing a go again |url=https://www.houstonpress.com/music/review-turnpike-troubadours-at-white-oak-music-hall-13334577 |access-date=November 12, 2023 |date=January 17, 2019}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Reckless_Kelly_(band)","to":"Reckless Kelly (band)"}],"pages":{"13473822":{"pageid":13473822,"ns":0,"title":"Reckless Kelly (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{copyvio-revdel|url=https://recklesskelly.com/pages/about|start1=1236662505|end1=1247714206}}\n{{Short description|American band}}\n{{Multiple issues|\n{{More footnotes needed|date=May 2010}}\n{{More citations needed|date=September 2011}}}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Reckless Kelly\n| image               =Reckless Kelly (1).jpg\n| caption             =Willy Braun and Chris Schelske at the Reckless Kelly Celebrity Softball Jam\n| image_size          =\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Stanley, Idaho]], U.S.\n| genre               = {{Flatlist|\n* [[Country rock]]\n}}\n| years_active        = 1997-present.\n| label               =\n| associated_acts     =\n| website             = [http://www.recklesskelly.com/ www.recklesskelly.com]\n| current_members     = Willy Braun<br />Cody Braun<br />Ryan Engleman<br />Jay Nazz<br />Joe Miller\n| past_members        = David Abeyta<br />Casey Pollock<br />Adam Odor<br />Jimmy \"JAM\" McFeeley<br />Chris Schelske\n}}\n\n'''Reckless Kelly''' is an American [[country rock]] band formed in [[Stanley, Idaho]]. The band relocated to [[Austin, Texas]] in October 1996.\n\n==History==\nLed by brothers Willy (vocals/guitar) and Cody Braun (vocals/fiddle/mandolin/harmonica), the alternative country-rock outfit Reckless Kelly formed in Stanley, Idaho in February 1996 before moving to Austin, Texas. The Brauns had previously toured with their father in Muzzie Braun & the Boys, a Western swing band, and were joined in their own group by the lead guitarist Casey Pollock, the bass guitarist Chris Schelske and the drummer Jay Nazz.\n\nWith their younger brothers Micky and Gary, Cody and Willy were raised in [[central Idaho]] near the [[Sawtooth Range (Idaho)|Sawtooth Mountains]], between [[Clayton, Idaho|Clayton]] and [[Challis, Idaho|Challis]] in [[Custer County, Idaho|Custer County]], and were homeschooled by their mother. Originally they were \"Muzzie Braun & the Little Braun Brothers\", as Muzzie and his brothers Gary and Billy were the \"Braun Brothers\" from [[Twin Falls, Idaho|Twin Falls]] in the 1970s and early 1980s, sons of the musician Eustaceus \"Mustie\" Braun.<ref name=bbhra>{{cite news |url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=eJVfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JDEMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3614%2C1990319 |work=Lewiston Morning Tribune |location=(Idaho)|last=McCarthy |first=John |title=Braun Brothers hit the road again for tour |date=June 22, 1990 |page=1D}}</ref><ref name=lntobitmmb81>{{cite news |url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=tJxfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=tjEMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5698%2C1808942 |work=Lewiston Morning Tribune |location=(Idaho) |agency=(obituary) |title=Mustie and Marian Braun, former Lewiston residents |date=February 20, 1981 |page=5C}}</ref> From [[North Dakota]], Mustie was a neighbor and relative of the bandleader [[Lawrence Welk]], and was a keyboard player during the last days of legalized gambling in Idaho at [[Weiser, Idaho|Weiser]] in the early 1950s. He then moved to the new Club [[U.S. Route 93|93]] in [[Jackpot, Nevada]], on the Idaho border, and moved his family to Twin Falls, about fifty miles (80&nbsp;km) north.<ref name=tmbfipt>{{cite news |url=http://www.idahopress.com/cavalcade/the-musical-braun-family/article_8d62e3c2-5703-11e0-9cb7-001cc4c03286.html |work=Idaho Press-Tribune |location=(Nampa)|last=Lea|first=Dan|title=The musical Braun family|date=April 2, 2011 |accessdate=March 20, 2017}}</ref> In February 1981, Mustie and wife Marian (''[[n\u00e9e]]'' Beckman) were involved in a [[head-on collision]] north of Jackpot, and both died from their injuries.<ref name=lntobitmmb81/>\n\nIn 1989, Muzzie and his sons appeared on [[Johnny Carson]]'s ''[[The Tonight Show Starring Johnny Carson|Tonight Show]]'' twice.<ref name=bbhra/><ref name=tmbfipt/>\n\nReckless Kelly played locally on the historic Sixth Street in Austin. They turned Lucy's Retired Surfers Bar, a small bar and restaurant, into a noted music venue with their Monday night residency from November 1996 to May 1998. During this period, other music venues in Austin invited them to play, including the Continental Club, the Saxon Pub, [[Stubb's Bar-B-Q|Stubb's Barbecue]], and Antone's Home of the Blues.\n\nReckless Kelly's first album, ''[[Millican (album)|Millican]]'', appeared in fall 1997 and was officially released in 1998. ''[[Acoustic: Live at Stubb's]]'' and ''[[The Day (Reckless Kelly album)|The Day]]'' followed two years later, after which David Abeyta replaced Pollock on lead guitar. ''[[Under the Table and Above the Sun|Under the Table & Above the Sun]]'' in 2003 began the band's relationship with the high-profile Sugar Hill label and won the hearts of the music press and the honky tonkin' legend [[Joe Ely]], who sang the band's praises in interviews. ''[[Wicked Twisted Road]]'' was released in 2005, and the next year the live album ''[[Reckless Kelly Was Here]]'' captured the band's stage presence. ''[[Bulletproof (Reckless Kelly album)|Bulletproof]]'' was released in summer 2008 on a new label, [[Yep Roc Records]], and includes tracks critical of and reflecting on recent sociopolitical unfoldings, such as the [[Iraq War]] and [[Hurricane Katrina]]. In 2010, Reckless released an album of songs by one of their musical heroes, Pinto Bennett. ''[[Somewhere in Time (Reckless Kelly album)|Somewhere in Time]]'', in the band's own words, highlighted their love of \"straight-up honky tonk\". The band regularly returns to Austin to play before capacity crowds at venues like Nutty Brown Cafe & Amphitheatre.\n\nYounger brothers Micky and Gary Braun front their own band, [[Micky & The Motorcars]]. Both bands play at the annual Braun Brothers Reunion in Challis, Idaho, in August.\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:18em;\"| Title\n!
