This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Chicks","to":"The Chicks"}],"pages":{"11040148":{"pageid":11040148,"ns":0,"title":"The Chicks","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country band}}\n{{About|the American country band||}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=July 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name              = The Chicks\n| image             = Dixie Chicks in Austin, Texas.jpg\n| caption           = The Dixie Chicks in 2006. Left to right: [[Emily Strayer]], [[Natalie Maines]], and [[Martie Maguire]]\n| alt               = Country band the Chicks performing onstage\n| background        = group_or_band\n| alias             = Dixie Chicks (1989\u20132020)\n| origin            = [[Dallas|Dallas, Texas]], U.S.\n| genre             = {{flatlist|\n* [[Country music|Country]]<ref name=\"Ankeny\"/>\n* [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]]<ref name=\"Ankeny\"/>\n* [[country pop]]<ref name=\"Ankeny\"/>\n}}\n| years_active      = 1989\u2013present\n| label             = {{flatlist|\n* Crystal Clear Sound\n* [[Monument Records|Monument Nashville]]\n* [[Columbia Records|Columbia Nashville]]\n}}\n| spinoffs          = [[Court Yard Hounds]]\n| website           = {{URL|thechicks.com}}\n| current_members   = * [[Emily Strayer]]\n* [[Martie Maguire]]\n* [[Natalie Maines]]\n| past_members      = * Robin Lynn Macy\n* Laura Lynch\n}}\n\n'''The Chicks''' (formerly the '''Dixie Chicks''') are an American [[country band]] from [[Dallas]], Texas. The band consists of [[Natalie Maines]] (lead vocals, guitar, bass guitar) and sisters [[Martie Maguire]] (vocals, fiddle, [[mandolin]], guitar) and [[Emily Strayer]] (vocals, guitar, banjo, [[Dobro]]). Maguire and Strayer, both n\u00e9e Erwin, founded the band in 1989, with bassist Laura Lynch and vocalist and guitarist Robin Lynn Macy. They performed [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]] and [[country music]], [[busking]] and touring the bluegrass festival circuits and small venues for six years without attracting a [[major label]]. In 1992, Lynch replaced Macy as the lead vocalist.\n\nAfter releasing three independent albums, the Dixie Chicks signed to [[Monument Records|Monument Records Nashville]] in 1997, by which point Maines had joined. They achieved success with their albums ''[[Wide Open Spaces (album)|Wide Open Spaces]]'' (1998) and ''[[Fly (Dixie Chicks album)|Fly]]'' (1999). After Monument closed its Nashville branch, the Dixie Chicks moved to [[Columbia Records]] for ''[[Home (Dixie Chicks album)|Home]]'' (2002). These albums achieved [[multi-platinum]] sales in the United States, Canada, and Australia, along with several charting singles on the American ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] charts. Their successful US singles were \"[[There's Your Trouble]]\", \"[[Wide Open Spaces (song)|Wide Open Spaces]]\", \"[[You Were Mine]]\", \"[[Cowboy Take Me Away]]\", \"[[Without You (Dixie Chicks song)|Without You]]\", and a cover of [[Bruce Robison]]'s \"[[Travelin' Soldier]]\". The Dixie Chicks also reached number one on the [[Adult Contemporary (chart)|Adult Contemporary]] chart with their 2002 cover of [[Fleetwood Mac]]'s \"[[Landslide (Fleetwood Mac song)|Landslide]]\".\n\nDays before the [[2003 invasion of Iraq]], Maines [[Dixie Chicks comments on George W. Bush|told a London audience that the Dixie Chicks did not endorse the war]] and were ashamed of US President [[George W. Bush]] being from Texas. The remarks triggered boycotts in the US and a backlash from fans. After a hiatus, the Dixie Chicks recorded ''[[Taking the Long Way]]'' in 2006, an album informed by the backlash. \"[[Not Ready to Make Nice]]\" became their biggest crossover single, reaching number four on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]]. After a second hiatus, Maguire and Strayer recorded as a duo called [[Court Yard Hounds]]. The Dixie Chicks reunited to tour in the 2010s. In 2020, they removed \"[[Dixie]]\" from their name due to negative connotations, and released their first album in 14 years, ''[[Gaslighter (album)|Gaslighter]].''\n\nThe Chicks have won 13 [[Grammy Award]]s, including five in 2007 for ''Taking the Long Way,'' which received the [[Grammy Award for Album of the Year]], and its single \"[[Not Ready to Make Nice]]\", which received the [[Grammy Award for Record of the Year]] and the [[Grammy Award for Song of the Year]]. In addition, the band has received ten [[Country Music Association]] awards and eight [[Academy of Country Music]] awards. By July 2020, with 33 million certified albums sold<ref name=\"RIAA1\">{{cite web|title=Gold & Platinum \u2013 Top Selling Artists|url=http://riaa.com/goldandplatinumdata.php?table=tblTopArt|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130409064003/http://www.riaa.com/goldandplatinumdata.php?table=tblTopArt|archive-date=April 9, 2013|access-date=July 19, 2010|publisher=[[Recording Industry Association of America|RIAA]]}}</ref> and sales of 27.9&nbsp;million albums in the US, the Chicks had become the best-selling all-woman band and best-selling country group since [[Nielsen SoundScan]] began recording sales in 1991.<ref>{{cite magazine|title=Natalie Maines Announces 'Mother' Solo Album|url=https://www.billboard.com/music/music-news/natalie-maines-announces-mother-solo-album-1538577/|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=February 25, 2022|archive-date=February 25, 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220225204139/https://www.billboard.com/music/music-news/natalie-maines-announces-mother-solo-album-1538577/|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|title=Chart Moves: Dixie Chicks' Natalie Maines Makes Solo Debut, She & Him Bows on Cassette|url=https://billboard.com/biz/articles/news/1562724/chart-moves-dixie-chicks-natalie-maines-makes-solo-debut-she-him-bows-on|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130609085841/http://www.billboard.com/biz/articles/news/1562724/chart-moves-dixie-chicks-natalie-maines-makes-solo-debut-she-him-bows-on|archive-date=June 9, 2013|access-date=May 17, 2013|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|title=How The Music Industry Finally Caught Up to The Chicks|url=https://www.billboard.com/the-chicks-gaslighter-interview/|last=Newman|first=Melinda|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=February 25, 2022|archive-date=February 25, 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220225204133/https://www.billboard.com/the-chicks-gaslighter-interview/|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n==History==\n\n===1989\u20131995: Original bluegrass group===\n[[File:IMAG2591-dallas-downtown.jpg|thumb|right|250px|The Chicks formed in [[Dallas]], Texas (seen here in 2016).]]\nThe Chicks were founded as the Dixie Chicks in 1989 in [[Dallas]], Texas, an area with country music roots. The original lineup consisted of El Paso native Laura Lynch on [[upright bass]], Californian Robin Lynn Macy on guitar, and the multi-instrumentalist sisters [[Martie Maguire|Martie]] and [[Emily Strayer|Emily Erwin]], respectively born in Pennsylvania and Massachusetts and raised in Dallas. The Erwin sisters, who were later married and both changed their names twice (Martie to Martie Seidel, then Martie Maguire; Emily to Emily Robison, then Emily Strayer). The band name was taken from the album ''[[Dixie Chicken]]'' by [[Lowell George]] of [[Little Feat]].<ref name=\"Tarnow\">Tarnow, Noah, \"Dixie Chicks\", ''Rolling Stone''; 12/01/98 Issue 801, pg.37</ref> They initially played predominantly [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]] and a mix of [[country music|country standards]]. All four women played and sang, though Maguire and Strayer provided most of the instrumentation while Lynch and Macy shared lead vocal duties. Maguire primarily played [[fiddle]], [[mandolin]], and viola, while Strayer's specialties included five-stringed [[banjo]] and [[resonator guitar]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.countrythangdaily.com/martie-maguire-facts/|title=10 Facts You Probably Didn't Know About Martie Maguire|last=Lambert|first=Arden|date=September 16, 2022|publisher=Country Thang Daily|accessdate=July 17, 2024|archive-date=July 17, 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240717060343/https://www.countrythangdaily.com/martie-maguire-facts/|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=\"margolis gaslighter\">{{cite web|url=https://americansongwriter.com/gaslighter-the-chicks-album-review/|title=The Chicks' 'Gaslighter' an Emotional Chronicle of Divorce-driven Heartache|last=Margolis|first=Lynne|publisher=American Songwriter|date=July 17, 2020|accessdate=July 17, 2024|archive-date=July 18, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200718143003/https://americansongwriter.com/gaslighter-the-chicks-album-review/|url-status=live}}</ref> In 1987, Maguire had won second place, and in 1989, third place in the national fiddle championships held at the [[Walnut Valley Festival]] in [[Winfield, Kansas]].<ref name=\"Walnut Valley Association\">{{cite web |url=http://www.wvfest.com/ |title=Walnut Valley Association 1987 and 1989 National fiddle championships in archive |access-date=March 2, 2008 |publisher=Wvfest.com |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080216052745/http://wvfest.com/ |archive-date=February 16, 2008 }}</ref>\n\nIn 1990, Penny Cook, the daughter of then-Texas senator [[John Tower]], gave the Dixie Chicks $10,000 to record an album. Later that year, the Dixie Chicks released their debut studio album ''[[Thank Heavens for Dale Evans]]'' on a local independent label called Crystal Clear Sound. The album was named after actress and singer-songwriter [[Dale Evans]].<ref>Dickerson, James L. ''Go, Girl, Go! The Women's Revolution in Music'', Schrimer Trade Books, 2005, p. 173</ref> The group paid $5,000 for the 14-track album.<ref name=\"BROOKS\">{{Cite web |title=All-Inclusive Dixie Chicks Timeline |url=https://rbrooks.tripod.com/timeline.html |access-date=2024-06-18 |website=rbrooks.tripod.com}}</ref> Macy co-wrote two of the album's 14 tracks, with Maguire also serving as co-writer for the title track.\n\nA Christmas single was released at the end of the year \u2013 a 45 RPM [[Gramophone record|vinyl record]] titled ''Home on the Radar Range'' with \"Christmas Swing\" on one side and the song on the flip side named \"The Flip Side\". The record titles were significant; during that period of time, the bandmates dressed up as \"[[cowgirls]]\", and publicity photos reflected this image. They also appeared at the [[Grand Ole Opry]]<ref name=\"Dixie Chicks Fans\">{{cite web |url=http://www.dixiechicksfans.net/martie_maguire.html |title=Dixie Chicks Fans Net |publisher=Dixiechicksfans.net |access-date=December 26, 2010 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://archive.today/20031224102456/http://www.dixiechicksfans.net/martie_maguire.html |archive-date=December 24, 2003 }}</ref> and [[Garrison Keillor]]'s [[radio broadcast|radio show]] ''[[A Prairie Home Companion]]''.<ref name=\"Clark\">Clark, Renee [http://www.dixie-chicks.com/dlife392.shtml \"Can the Dixie Chicks make it in the big time? Local Heroes\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304191833/http://www.dixie-chicks.com/dlife392.shtml |date=March 4, 2016}} ''Dallas Morning News'', March 1, 1992. Retrieved March 23, 2008</ref>\n\nThe Dixie Chicks began building a fan base, winning the prize for \"best band\" at the 1990 [[Telluride Bluegrass Festival]] and opening for established [[country music]] artists, including such names as [[Garth Brooks]], [[Reba McEntire]], and [[George Strait]].<ref name=\"BROOKS\"/>\n\nIn 1992, the Dixie Chicks' next Crystal Clear Sound release, ''[[Little Ol' Cowgirl]]'', moved towards a more contemporary country sound, as the band used more [[session musician]]s, and developed a richer sound with larger and more modern arrangements. Macy and Maguire each wrote two of the album's songs, with Lynch co-writing one song with Maguire. Displeased with the change in sound, Macy left in late 1992 to devote herself to a \"purer\" bluegrass sound, remaining active in the Dallas and Austin music scenes.<ref name=\"8 Note\">{{Cite web |title=Dixie Chicks biography - 8notes.com |url=https://www.8notes.com/biographies/dixie_chicks.asp |access-date=2024-06-18 |website=www.8notes.com |archive-date=June 1, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240601171123/https://www.8notes.com/biographies/dixie_chicks.asp |url-status=live }}</ref> During this period, the Texan [[steel guitar]]ist [[Lloyd Maines]] (who had played on both albums) introduced them to his daughter, [[Natalie Maines|Natalie]], an aspiring singer. He thought his daughter would be a good replacement for Macy, and had passed her [[Demo (music)|demo tape]], which had won her a scholarship to the [[Berklee College of Music]], to the Erwin sisters.<ref Name=\"Redbook\">[http://www.accessmylibrary.com/coms2/summary_0286-26096144_ITM \"Dishing With The Dixie Chicks\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090112034011/http://www.accessmylibrary.com/coms2/summary_0286-26096144_ITM |date=January 12, 2009 }} ''Redbook'' March 1, 2002. Retrieved March 23, 2008.</ref> Her distinctive voice was a match for Maguire's [[soprano]] and Strayer's [[alto]] [[harmonies]].{{Citation needed|date=December 2023}} Reviewing their show [[the Birchmere]], Virginia in 1992, Eric Brace of ''[[The Washington Post]]'' wrote that \"record label executives will be kicking themselves soon enough ... These Chicks have what it takes to make the big time, yet no major label has taken the plunge to sign them.\"<ref name=\"Brace\">Brace, Eric (March 30, 1992). [http://www.highbeam.com/doc/1P2-998203.html \"Dixie Chicks\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121105222734/http://www.highbeam.com/doc/1P2-998203.html|date=November 5, 2012}}. ''[[The Washington Post]]''. Retrieved March 28, 2008</ref>\n\nLynch became lead singer on the Dixie Chicks' third Crystal Clear Sound album, ''[[Shouldn't a Told You That]]'' (1993). They were still unable to attract support from a major [[record label]] and struggled to expand their fan base beyond Texas and Nashville. Their manager, Simon Renshaw, approached the executive [[Scott Siman]], best known for his work with [[Tim McGraw]], and he signed them to a developmental deal with [[Sony Music Entertainment]]'s Nashville division. The deal was finalized with Sony over mid-1995,<ref name=\"dm112395\">{{cite news | url=http://www.dallasobserver.com/1995-11-23/music/red-hot/1 | title=Red hot | author=Willonsky, Robert | newspaper=[[Dallas Observer]] | date=November 23, 1995 | url-status=live | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110617075922/http://www.dallasobserver.com/1995-11-23/music/red-hot/1/ | archive-date=June 17, 2011 | df=mdy-all }}</ref> and Lynch was replaced by Maines.<ref name=\"Dickerson\">Dickerson, James L. (2000) Dixie Chicks: Down-Home and Backstage. Taylor Trade Publishing, Dallas, Texas. {{ISBN|0-87833-189-1}}.</ref> Lynch's departure left the Erwin sisters as the two remaining original members. Also in 1995, Maguire married pharmaceutical representative Ted Seidel.\n\nAccounts of Lynch's departure vary. At the time, the sisters said she had been considering leaving for over a year as she was weary of touring and hoped to spend more time with her daughter.<ref name=\"dm112395\" /> Lynch offered to stay for the first recordings on the new album, but the sisters thought it would send the wrong message to Sony; they all agreed she would leave before the new album.<ref name=\"dm112395\" /> In a 1996 interview, Lynch said, \"It can't really be characterized as a resignation. There are three Dixie Chicks, and I'm only one.\"<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.dixie-chicks.com/cchat96a.shtml|title=Chick Chat, Spring 1996|website=dixie-chicks.com|access-date=May 16, 2016|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://archive.today/20130102173059/http://www.dixie-chicks.com/cchat96a.shtml|archive-date=January 2, 2013}}</ref> In 2003, Lynch said she had no regrets about leaving.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.myplainview.com/article_cbb5324a-0f70-531e-a264-8743e28a6b2d.html|title=Former Dixie Chick: No regrets missing out on band's success|last=Chang|first=Anita|date=May 2, 2003|work=[[Plainview Herald|MyPlainview.com]]|access-date=May 16, 2016}}</ref>\n\n===1995\u20132000: Commercial success with ''Wide Open Spaces'' and ''Fly''===\n[[File:Dixie Chicks 1998.jpg|thumb|250px|The Dixie Chicks in 1998.]]\nWith the addition of Maines, the new lineup had a more contemporary sound, as well as a new look, leaving their cowgirl dresses with their past, giving the band a broader appeal.<ref name=\"Ankeny\"/> Renshaw sent staff producer [[Blake Chancey]], best known for his work with [[Deryl Dodd]], to Austin to work with the band.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2019-06-24 |title=One of Nashville's Leading Record Producers and The Guy Who Signed The Dixie Chicks, Blake Chancey |url=https://www.thinkinanddrinkin.com/podcast/blakechancey |access-date=2024-06-19 |website=Thinkin' & Drinkin' |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nAfter Maines joined the band, the instrumental lineup was essentially the same, though Maines was not an acoustic bassist. Instead, she played [[Acoustic guitar|acoustic]] and electric guitar, and occasionally electric bass guitar or [[Tacoma Guitars#Papoose|Tacoma Papoose]] guitar in concert. She sang lead vocals, with Maguire and Strayer singing backing vocals. Strayer was now contributing to the band's sound, adding guitar, [[accordion]], [[sitar]], and papoose to her mastery of the [[five-string banjo]] and [[dobro]], while Maguire began adding guitar, viola, and [[mandolin]] chops more frequently to her expert fiddle.  The sisters welcomed the change; Maguire said, \"It's very rootsy, but then Natalie comes in with a rock and [[blues]] influence. That gave Emily and [me] a chance to branch out, because we loved those kinds of music but felt limited by our instruments.\"<ref name=\"Malkin\">{{cite web |url=http://chickoholic.tripod.com/DixieChicks/id8.html |title=Malkin, Nina |work=Dixie Chicks Henhouse |publisher=Chickoholic.tripod.com |access-date=May 12, 2011 |url-status=live |archive-url=http://archive.wikiwix.com/cache/20110815214537/http://chickoholic.tripod.com/DixieChicks/id8.html |archive-date=August 15, 2011 }}</ref>\n\nWithin the next year, [[Sony Music Nashville]] came to Austin to see the revamped band and signed them as the first new artist on the newly revived [[Monument Records]] label. Their debut single \"[[I Can Love You Better]]\" was released in October 1997 and reached the Top 10 on ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]], while the new lineup recorded the rest of their debut album. ''[[Wide Open Spaces (album)|Wide Open Spaces]]'' was released on January 23, 1998.<ref name=\"Official Site\">[http://www.sonymusic.com/labels/nashville/DixieChicks/ Official Dixie Chicks Site] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060612163721/http://www.sonymusic.com/labels/nashville/DixieChicks/ |date=June 12, 2006 }}</ref>\n\nOver the space of a year, the next three singles from ''Wide Open Spaces'' reached first place on Hot Country Songs: \"[[There's Your Trouble]]\", \"[[You Were Mine]]\", and the [[Wide Open Spaces (song)|title track]]. The album added a widespread audience to their original following, entering the top five on both country and pop charts<ref name=\"Smith\">Smith, Chris (January 19, 2008), [http://www.canada.com/vancouversun/news/arts/story.html?id=6682cf47-f128-4c57-be62-397f11b61d4a \"100 Albums You Need To Own\"] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121109161559/http://www.canada.com/vancouversun/news/arts/story.html?id=6682cf47-f128-4c57-be62-397f11b61d4a |date=November 9, 2012 }}, ''[[The Vancouver Sun]]''. Retrieved May 12, 2011.</ref> with initial sales of 12 million copies in the country music arena alone, setting a record for the best-selling duo or group album in country music history.<ref name=\"Ankeny\">{{Cite web |title=The Chicks Songs, Albums, Reviews, Bio & More ... |url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/the-chicks-mn0000162487 |access-date=2024-06-19 |website=AllMusic |language=en |archive-date=June 19, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240619090202/https://www.allmusic.com/artist/the-chicks-mn0000162487 |url-status=live }}</ref> As of 2003, the 12 million copies sold in the United States of ''Wide Open Spaces'' made it a RIAA-certified diamond album.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Gold & Platinum |url=https://www.riaa.com/gold-platinum/ |access-date=2024-06-19 |website=RIAA |language=en-US |archive-date=November 19, 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211119235334/https://www.riaa.com/gold-platinum/ |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nIn 1998, the Dixie Chicks sold more CDs than all other country music groups combined.<ref name=\"Elle\">[http://celebrity.elle.com/music_artists/celebrity-biography-Dixie+Chicks \"Dixie Chicks Biography\"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231226084013/https://shop.prevention.com/multi-magazine-search?&utm_source=direct_traffic&utm_medium=search&utm_campaign=multi_hearst_magazines_shop |date=December 26, 2023 }}, ''[[Elle (magazine)|Elle]]''. Retrieved May 30, 2008</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Discover hidden connections {{!}}{{!}} GRAMMYconnect |url=https://www.grammyconnect.com/people/dixie-chicks |website=Discover hidden connections {{!}}{{!}} GRAMMYconnect |access-date=May 8, 2020 }}{{Dead link|date=October 2023 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref> The commercial success of ''Wide Open Spaces'' also led to the first of several industry award nominations for the band. The [[Country Music Association]] awarded them the Horizon Award for new artists in 1998, given to those who have \"demonstrated the most significant creative growth and development in overall chart and sales activity, live performance professionalism and critical media recognition\".<ref name=\"Horizon\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmaworld.com/news_publications/pr_common/press_detail.asp?re=235&year=2003|title=Horizon Award requirements|date=September 12, 2003|publisher=Country Music Association|access-date=December 1, 2015|archive-date=February 4, 2007|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070204233922/http://cmaworld.com/news_publications/pr_common/press_detail.asp?re=235&year=2003}}</ref><ref name=\"CBS News\">{{cite web |url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/dixie-chicks-riding-high/ |title=Dixie Chicks Riding High |publisher=[[CBS News]] |date=October 5, 2000 |access-date=May 12, 2011 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120306181751/http://www.cbsnews.com/stories/2000/10/03/entertainment/main238081.shtml?source=search_story |archive-date=March 6, 2012 }}</ref> At the [[41st Annual Grammy Awards]] in 1998, the group was nominated for Grammy Award for Best New Artist, while ''Wide Open Spaces'' won Best Country Album and \"There's Your Trouble\" won Best Country Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocal. The [[Academy of Country Music]] also awarded the band as Top Vocal Group and Top New Vocal Duet or Group in 1999; they would win the former again in 2000 and 2001.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.acmcountry.com/winners?awardTitle=Dixie+chicks&awardCategory=&awardYear=&actionButton=Submit|title=Search results for Dixie Chicks|publisher=Academy of Country Music|accessdate=June 17, 2024}}</ref>\n\nOn August 31, 1999, the Dixie Chicks released their next Monument album, ''[[Fly (Dixie Chicks album)|Fly]]'', which debuted at No. 1 on the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] charts, selling over 10 million copies and making the Dixie Chicks the only country band and the only female band of any genre to hold the distinction of having two back-to-back [[RIAA certified]] diamond albums.<ref name=\"Official Site\"/> Nine singles were released from ''Fly'', including country No. 1s \"[[Cowboy Take Me Away]]\" and \"[[Without You (Dixie Chicks song)|Without You]]\". Dixie Chicks albums continued to place in the list of the [[List of best-selling albums in the United States|50 best-selling albums in American history]] over a half-decade after they were released.<ref name=\"Willman-book\">Willman, Chris (2005), ''Rednecks & Bluenecks: The Politics of Country Music'', New York: [[The New Press]], pp. 21\u201323, {{ISBN|978-1-59558-017-7}}</ref> ''Fly'' again won Grammy awards and honors from the Country Music Association and the Academy of Country Music, and the Dixie Chicks received a number of honors from other sources for their accomplishments.<ref name=\"CBS News-2\">[https://www.cbsnews.com/news/couples-shine-at-country-awards/ \"Couples Shine At Country Awards\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120306212503/http://www.cbsnews.com/stories/2000/05/02/entertainment/main191065.shtml?source=search_story |date=March 6, 2012 }}, [[CBS News]], May 2, 2000. Retrieved February 25, 2022</ref> The band headlined their first tour, the [[Fly Tour]], with guest artists including [[Joe Ely]] and [[Ricky Skaggs]] appearing at each show,<ref name=\"Frontpage Notes\">{{cite web|url=http://www.frontpagepublicity.com/dxc/content/notesandquotes.html|title=Dixie Chicks Official site|publisher=Frontpage Publicity|access-date=December 1, 2015|archive-date=February 25, 2008|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080225174656/http://www.frontpagepublicity.com/dxc/content/notesandquotes.html}}</ref> and also joined [[Sarah McLachlan]], [[Sheryl Crow]], and other female artists on the all-woman touring [[Lilith Fair]].<ref name=\"Willman-jul99\">{{Cite web |title=The Dixie Chicks bring country music to Lilith Fair |url=https://ew.com/article/1999/07/27/dixie-chicks-bring-country-music-lilith-fair/ |access-date=2024-06-19 |website=EW.com |language=en |archive-date=June 19, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240619090202/https://ew.com/article/1999/07/27/dixie-chicks-bring-country-music-lilith-fair/ |url-status=live }}</ref> That November, Maguire divorced Seidel.\n\nThe source of the Dixie Chicks' commercial success during this time came from various factors: they wrote or co-wrote about half of the songs on ''Wide Open Spaces'' and ''Fly''; their mixture of [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]], mainstream [[country music]], [[blues]], and pop songs appealed to a wide spectrum of record buyers, and where the women had once dressed as \"cowgirls\" with Lynch, their dress was now more contemporary.<ref name=\"Ankeny\"/>\n\n\"Cowboy Take Me Away\" from ''Fly'' became another [[signature song]], written by Maguire to celebrate Emily's marriage with country singer [[Charlie Robison]], which took place three months before the album's release. However, a few of their songs brought controversy within their conservative country music fan base, and two songs caused some radio stations to remove the Dixie Chicks from their playlists: \"[[Sin Wagon]]\", from which the term \"mattress dancing\" takes on a new twist, and \"[[Goodbye Earl]]\", a song that uses [[black comedy]] in telling the story of the unabashed murderer of an abusive husband. (The band later made a video portraying the nefarious deed, with actor [[Dennis Franz]] playing the murdered husband.) In an interview, Maines commented about Sony worrying about the reference to \"mattress dancing\" in \"Sin Wagon\", refusing to discuss it in interviews. She said, \"Our manager jokes, 'You can't say mattress dancing, but they love the song about premeditated first degree murder'! She continues, \" ... so it's funny to us that \"mattress dancing\" is out and murder is in!\"<ref name=\"Willman-sep99\">{{Cite web |title=The Dixie Chicks burn up the Billboard pop charts |url=https://ew.com/article/1999/09/23/dixie-chicks-burn-billboard-pop-charts/ |access-date=2024-06-19 |website=EW.com |language=en}}</ref>\n\n===2001\u20132002: Record label dispute and ''Home''===\nAfter the commercial success of their first two albums, the band became involved in a dispute with their record label, [[Sony]], regarding accounting procedures, alleging that in at least 30 cases Sony had used fraudulent accounting practices, underpaying them at least $4&nbsp;million (\u00a32.7m) in [[royalties]] on their albums over the previous three years.<ref name=\"BBC News\">{{Cite news |date=2001-08-29 |title=Dixie Chicks sue Sony for $4m |url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/1514747.stm |access-date=2024-06-19 |language=en-GB |archive-date=December 22, 2008 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20081222094006/http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/1514747.stm |url-status=live }}</ref> Sony held out, and the trio walked away, with Sony suing the group for failure to complete their contract.<ref name=\"Sony\">{{Cite magazine |last=Staff |first=Billboard |date=2001-07-18 |title=Sony Sues Dixie Chicks For Breach Of Contract |url=https://www.billboard.com/music/music-news/sony-sues-dixie-chicks-for-breach-of-contract-79082/ |access-date=2024-06-19 |magazine=Billboard |language=en-US |archive-date=July 4, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130704191934/http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/79082/sony-sues-dixie-chicks-for-breach-of-contract |url-status=live }}</ref> The Dixie Chicks responded with their own $4.1-million lawsuit against [[Sony Music Entertainment]] on August 27,<ref name=\"Rolling Stone\">{{Cite magazine |last=Dansby |first=Andrew |date=2001-08-28 |title=Dixie Chicks Sue Sony |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/dixie-chicks-sue-sony-236628/ |access-date=2024-06-19 |magazine=Rolling Stone |language=en-US |archive-date=September 6, 2008 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080906162507/http://www.rollingstone.com/artists/dixiechicks/articles/story/5931612/dixie_chicks_sue_sony |url-status=live }}</ref> which added clout to claims made by singers [[Courtney Love]], [[Aimee Mann]], and [[LeAnn Rimes]] against the recording industry.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.aimeemanninprint.com/2001/bg100701.htm|title=Recording Artists Sue, Aiming to Rock Industry Action Expected to Put Big Labels Under Scrutiny|newspaper=[[The Boston Globe]]|publisher=Aimeemanninprint.com|date=October 7, 2001|access-date=December 26, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110707095802/http://www.aimeemanninprint.com/2001/bg100701.htm|archive-date=July 7, 2011}}</ref> After months of negotiation, the Dixie Chicks settled their suit privately, and were awarded their own record label imprint, Open Wide Records, which afforded them more control, a better contract, and an increase in [[royalty payment]]s, with Sony still responsible for marketing and distribution of albums.<ref name=\"Elle\"/><ref name=\"Leggett\">Leggett, Steve. [http://music.msn.com/artist/?artist=16649328&menu=bio \"Martie Maguire: Biography.\"] {{Webarchive|url=https://archive.today/20130104003115/http://music.msn.com/artist/?artist=16649328&menu=bio |date=January 4, 2013}} [[MSN]]. Retrieved March 9, 2008.</ref>\n\nDuring the time that they worked with Sony to reconcile their differences, the Dixie Chicks debuted their quiet, unadorned song \"I Believe in Love\" on the ''[[America: A Tribute to Heroes]]'' [[telethon]] following the [[September 11 attacks]]. The three women found themselves home, in Texas, each happily married, planning families, and writing songs closer to their roots, without the usual pressures of the studio technicians from the major labels. The songs they didn't write were solicited from songwriters who wrote with a less commercial emphasis.<ref name=\"Hermes\">Hermes, Will [https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=1149097 NPR Music All Things Considered] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171011181347/http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=1149097 |date=October 11, 2017}}. [[NPR Music]]. August 28, 2002. Retrieved April 20, 2008.</ref> The result was that ''[[Home (Dixie Chicks album)|Home]]'', independently produced by [[Lloyd Maines]] and the Dixie Chicks, was released August 27, 2002.<ref name=\"Official Site\"/>\n\nUnlike the Dixie Chicks' two previous records, ''Home'' is dominated by up-tempo bluegrass and pensive ballads; and [[Emmylou Harris]] added her vocals to \"Godspeed\". In addition, the text of the opening track and first single, \"[[Long Time Gone]]\", was a pointed criticism of contemporary country music radio, accusing it of ignoring the soul of the genre as exemplified by [[Merle Haggard]], [[Johnny Cash]], and [[Hank Williams]]. \"Long Time Gone\" became the Dixie Chicks' first Top 10 hit on the [[Billboard Hot 100|U.S. pop singles chart]] and peaked at No. 2 on the country chart, becoming a major success.  Approximately six million copies of ''Home'' were sold in the United States.<ref>Grein, Paul. [http://new.music.yahoo.com/blogs/chart_watch/18943/chart-watch-extra-ropin-the-biggest-country-hits/ \"Chart Watch Extra: Ropin' The Biggest Country Hits\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20081229001814/http://new.music.yahoo.com/blogs/chart_watch/18943/chart-watch-extra-ropin-the-biggest-country-hits/ |date=December 29, 2008}}. ''[[Yahoo! Music]]''. November 7, 2008.</ref>\n\n''Home'' also won Grammy awards, and other noteworthy accolades as before, though it fell short of reaching the diamond record status of the first two albums. Natalie Maines said afterward, \"I want to check the record books and see how many fathers and daughters have won Grammys together.\"<ref name=\"Frontpage Publicity\">{{cite news|url=http://www.frontpagepublicity.com/dxc/content/careeroverview.html|title=Dixie Chicks Official site|newspaper=Contact Any Celebrity |publisher=Frontpage Publicity|access-date=December 1, 2015|archive-date=February 26, 2008|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080226165207/http://www.frontpagepublicity.com/dxc/content/careeroverview.html}}</ref>\n\nBy 2002, the Dixie Chicks were featured on three television specials: ''[[An Evening with the Dixie Chicks]]'', which was an [[acoustic music|acoustic]] concert primarily composed of the material from ''Home''; ''[[VH1 Divas|VH1 Divas Las Vegas]]'' alongside [[Cher]], [[C\u00e9line Dion]], [[Shakira]], [[Anastacia]], [[Stevie Nicks]], [[Mary J. Blige]], [[Cyndi Lauper]], [[Whitney Houston]] and host [[Ellen DeGeneres]]; and a [[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]] three-hour television special, the ''40 Greatest Women of Country Music''. Ranked No. 13 out of 40, they were \"selected by hundreds of artists, music historians, music journalists and music industry professionals\u2014looking at every aspect of what a great artist is\".<ref name=\"CMT 40 Greatest\">{{cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/shows/dyn/greatest_series/76608/episode_countdown.jhtml |title=40 Greatest Women of Country Music |publisher=[[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]] |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090414142311/http://www.cmt.com/shows/dyn/greatest_series/76608/episode_countdown.jhtml |archive-date=April 14, 2009 |access-date=June 13, 2008}}</ref>\n\n===2003\u20132005: Comments on George W. Bush and backlash===\n{{Main|Dixie Chicks comments on George W. Bush}}\n\n{{anchor|Boycott|Dixie_Chicks#2003.E2.80.9305:_Political_controversy}}\n\nOn March 10, 2003, the Dixie Chicks performed at the [[Shepherd's Bush Empire]] theater in London, England''.''<ref name=\":7\">{{Cite magazine|last=Dansby|first=Andrew|date=March 17, 2003|title=Fans Turn on Dixie Chicks|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/fans-turn-on-dixie-chicks-251772/|access-date=June 14, 2020|magazine=Rolling Stone|archive-date=June 14, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200614160951/https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/fans-turn-on-dixie-chicks-251772/|url-status=live}}</ref> Maines told the audience the band did not support the imminent [[2003 Invasion of Iraq|Allied invasion of Iraq]] and were ashamed that [[President George W. Bush]] was from Texas.<ref name=\"Guardian33\">Campbell, Duncan (2003). [https://www.theguardian.com/world/2003/apr/25/arts.usa {{\"'}}Dixie sluts' fight on with naked defiance\"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200613142526/https://www.theguardian.com/world/2003/apr/25/arts.usa |date=June 13, 2020 }} ''The Guardian''. Retrieved June 26, 2020.</ref> The remark triggered a backlash in the United States.<ref name=\"Guardian33\" /> The Dixie Chicks were [[Blacklisting|blacklisted]] by thousands of country radio stations,<ref name=\":22\">{{cite magazine|last=Sachs|first=Andrea|date=May 21, 2006|title=Chicks In the Line of Fire \u2013 Printout \u2013 TIME|url=http://www.time.com/time/magazine/printout/0,8816,1196419,00.html|magazine=Time|archive-url=https://archive.today/20121206045558/http://www.time.com/time/magazine/printout/0,8816,1196419,00.html|archive-date=December 6, 2012|access-date=December 26, 2010|url-status=dead}}</ref> and the band members received death threats.<ref>{{cite news|date=April 24, 2003|title=Dixie Chicks 'get death threats'|work=BBC News|url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/2972043.stm|url-status=live|access-date=March 2, 2009|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090829151806/http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/2972043.stm|archive-date=August 29, 2009}}</ref> Their single \"[[Landslide (Fleetwood Mac song)|Landslide]]\", a [[Fleetwood Mac]] cover, fell from number 10 to 43 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] in one week and left the chart a week later.<ref name=\":1\">{{Cite news |last=Smith |first=Grady |date=November 19, 2015 |title=Is country music ready to forgive the Dixie Chicks? |newspaper=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2015/nov/19/the-dixie-chicks-tour-is-country-music-ready-to-forgive |access-date=June 13, 2020 |issn=0261-3077 |archive-date=May 17, 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220517115411/https://www.theguardian.com/music/2015/nov/19/the-dixie-chicks-tour-is-country-music-ready-to-forgive |url-status=live }}</ref> The backlash also damaged sales of their next album and tour.<ref name=\"auto\">{{Cite web |title=Dixie Chicks: Home |url=https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/dixie-chicks-home/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200719113250/https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/dixie-chicks-home/ |archive-date=July 19, 2020 |access-date=June 14, 2020 |website=[[Pitchfork (website)|Pitchfork]]}}</ref> Maines issued an apology, saying her remark had been disrespectful; in 2006 she rescinded the apology, saying she felt Bush deserved no respect.<ref name=\":22\" /> \n\n[[File:DixieChicksMSG062003.jpg|thumb|274px|The Dixie Chicks performing at [[Madison Square Garden]] on June 20, 2003, during the [[Top of the World Tour]]]]\nIn 2005, [[Hurricane Katrina]] and [[Hurricane Rita]] battered the [[Gulf Coast]], with the Dixie Chicks' home state of Texas directly in the wake of the disaster. In September, the Dixie Chicks debuted their song \"[[I Hope (Dixie Chicks song)|I Hope]]\" in the telethon [[Shelter from the Storm: A Concert for the Gulf Coast]]. It was released as a download with proceeds to benefit hurricane relief through [[Habitat For Humanity]] and the [[American Federation of Musicians]] Gulf Coast Relief Fund.<ref>{{cite press release|url=http://www.dixiechicks.com/news_092605.htm|title=New Dixie Chicks recording, \"I Hope\", available as digital download on Tuesday, September 27th|publisher=DixieChicks.com|date=September 26, 2005|access-date=May 18, 2009|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080828035522/http://www.dixiechicks.com/news_092605.htm|archive-date=August 28, 2008}}</ref><ref name=\"Shelter\">[http://www.msnbc.msn.com/id/9147333/ \"Shelter From the Storm\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20051115200756/http://www.msnbc.msn.com/id/9147333/ |date=November 15, 2005 }}, MSNBC. Retrieved March 8, 2008</ref><ref name=\"anythought\">[http://anythingbut.com/archive/2005_09.html {{\"'}}Shelter' Fund Drive Extends Reach\"] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20081201131902/http://anythingbut.com/archive/2005_09.html |date=December 1, 2008}}. Retrieved March 8, 2008</ref>\n\nIn October 2004, the Dixie Chicks joined the [[Vote for Change]] tour, performing at concerts organized by [[MoveOn.org]] in [[swing states]], raising funds for political groups opposing Bush.<ref name=\"rs100404\">{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/politics/politics-news/bruce-dave-r-e-m-swing-243452/|title=Bruce, Dave, R.E.M. Swing|last=Orloff|first=Brian|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=October 4, 2004|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080415172755/http://www.rollingstone.com/news/story/6537312/bruce_dave_rem_swing|archive-date=April 15, 2008|access-date=February 25, 2022}}</ref> In 2005, Maguire, Strayer, and Maines joined 31 other recording artists, including [[Dolly Parton]], [[Christina Aguilera]], [[Yoko Ono]], and [[Mandy Moore]] supporting relationships of all kinds, regardless of sexual orientation or gender identity, on a two-disc release titled ''[[Love Rocks]]'', with their song from the album ''Home'' \"I Believe in Love\".<ref name=\"Centaur Entertainment\">\n[http://www.hrc.org/2337.htm \"HRC, Centaur Entertainment to Release 'Love Rocks' CD Feb. 8\"] {{webarchive |url= https://web.archive.org/web/20080919074000/http://www.hrc.org/2337.htm |date= September 19, 2008}}, Human Rights Campaign, January 28, 2005. Retrieved May 25, 2008.\n</ref>\n\n===2006\u20132007: ''Taking the Long Way'' and ''Shut Up and Sing''===\nOn March 16, 2006, the Dixie Chicks released the single \"[[Not Ready to Make Nice]]\" in advance of their upcoming album. Cowritten with [[Dan Wilson (musician)|Dan Wilson]], it addressed the political controversy that had surrounded the group for the previous three years.<ref>[https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=5424238 \"Dixie Chicks Return, 'Taking the Long Way'\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171011181537/http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=5424238 |date=October 11, 2017 }} \u2013 [[NPR]] Interview on ''[[All Things Considered]]'', May 23, 2006.</ref> Strayer said, \"The stakes were definitely higher on that song. We knew it was special because it was so autobiographical, and we had to get it right. And once we had that song done, it freed us up to do the rest of the album without that burden.\" She said writing the song had become their \"therapy\", since they had to hold in so many stored emotions for so long. Thus, the band considered the album not so much political as very personal.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=5424238|title=Dixie Chicks Return, 'Taking the Long Way'|last=Block|first=Melissa|date=May 23, 2006|work=[[All Things Considered]]|publisher=[[NPR]]|access-date=July 29, 2008|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080517170753/http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=5424238|archive-date=May 17, 2008}}</ref>\n\n''[[Taking the Long Way]]'' was released in stores and online on May 22, 2006. The album was produced by [[Rick Rubin]] who had worked with [[hard rock]] acts such as [[Red Hot Chili Peppers]] and [[System of a Down]], as well as idiosyncratic singers such as [[Johnny Cash]] and [[Neil Diamond]]. The band felt they had nothing to lose by a newer approach, and possibly quite a bit to gain.<ref name=MSN>{{cite web | year=2006 | url=http://music.msn.com/artist/?artist=16097852 | title=Dixie Chicks: 'Taking the Long Way' | publisher=[[MSN]] | access-date=April 13, 2006 | url-status=dead | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060412165122/http://music.msn.com/artist/?artist=16097852 | archive-date=April 12, 2006 | df=mdy-all }}</ref> The three Chicks co-wrote every song on the album, alongside various other songwriters, including [[Neil Finn]] of [[Crowded House]]. The album contains references to the 2003 controversy.<ref name=\"Tryangiel\">{{cite magazine |author=Tryangiel, Josh |date=May 29, 2006 |title=In The Line of Fire |url=http://www.time.com/time/archive/preview/0,10987,1196419,00.html |url-status=dead |magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]] |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060615005747/http://www.time.com/time/archive/preview/0,10987,1196419,00.html |archive-date=June 15, 2006}}</ref> ''Taking the Long Way'' debuted at number one on both the [[Billboard 200|U.S. pop albums chart]] and the [[Top Country Albums|U.S. country albums chart]], selling 526,000 copies in the first week (the year's second-best such total for any country act) and making it a [[gold record]] within its first week. The Dixie Chicks became the first female band in chart history to have three albums debut at No. 1.<ref>{{cite press release\n |title       = Dixie Chicks New Album, Taking The Long Way, Debuts At No.&nbsp;1 On Billboard Top 200\n |date        = May 31, 2006\n|publisher   = [[Columbia Records]]\n |url         = http://biz.yahoo.com/prnews/060531/nyw075.html\n |url-status     = live\n |archive-url  = https://web.archive.org/web/20060615185952/http://biz.yahoo.com/prnews/060531/nyw075.html?.v=52\n |archive-date = June 15, 2006\n|df          = mdy-all\n}}</ref>\n\nNeither \"Not Ready to Make Nice\" or second single \"[[Everybody Knows (Dixie Chicks song)|Everybody Knows]]\" reached top 35 on Hot Country Songs.  In June 2006, Emily Strayer noted the lack of support from other country music performers: \"A lot of artists cashed in on being against what we said or what we stood for because that was promoting their career, which was a horrible thing to do. ... A lot of pandering started going on, and you'd see soldiers and the American flag in every video. It became a sickening display of ultra-patriotism.\"<ref name=Telegraph/>\n\nMaines said, \"The entire country may disagree with me, but I don't understand the necessity for patriotism. Why do you have to be a patriot? About what? This land is our land? Why? You can like where you live and like your life, but as for loving the whole country ... I don't see why people care about patriotism.\"<ref name=Telegraph>{{cite news | date=June 14, 2006 | url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/3653132/How-the-Chicks-survived-their-scrap-with-Bush.html | newspaper=The Daily Telegraph | title=How the Chicks survived their scrap with Bush | author=Sweeting, Adam | location=London| archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20081012151525/http://www.telegraph.co.uk/arts/main.jhtml?xml=%2Farts%2F2006%2F06%2F15%2Fbmdixie15.xml | archive-date=October 12, 2008 | df=mdy-all|access-date=February 25, 2022}}</ref> The two singles were more successful in Europe, peaking at Nos. 13 and 11 respectively and remaining on the European Country Charts for more than 20 weeks each.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.europeancma.com/charts.htm | title=European CMA | url-status=dead | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080820214618/http://www.europeancma.com/charts.htm | archive-date=August 20, 2008 | df=mdy-all }}</ref>\n\nThe [[Accidents & Accusations Tour]] began in July 2006. Ticket sales were strong in Canada and in some Northeastern markets, but notably weak in other areas. A number of shows were canceled or relocated to smaller venues due to poor sales, and in [[Houston]], Texas, tickets never even went on sale when local radio stations refused to accept advertising for the event.<ref>\n{{cite news\n |title       = Radio, promoter each blames other for cut in Chicks tour\n |date        = August 15, 2006\n|newspaper   = [[Houston Chronicle]]\n |url         = http://www.chron.com/disp/story.mpl/ent/4116099.html\n |url-status     = live\n |archive-url  = https://web.archive.org/web/20110629021146/http://www.chron.com/disp/story.mpl/ent/4116099.html\n |archive-date = June 29, 2011\n|df          = mdy-all\n}}</ref>\nIn August, a re-routed tour schedule was scheduled with a greater emphasis on Canadian dates, where ''Taking the Long Way'' had gone five-times-[[platinum record|platinum]]. As part of the tour, the Dixie Chicks became the first major band to hire a designated blogger \"all-access\" to keep up with them in their promotional activities and tour.<ref>{{cite news |title=Chicks Magnet |date=June 19, 2006 |newspaper=The Washington Post |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2006/06/18/AR2006061800986.html |first=J. Freedom |last=du Lac |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170706154232/http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2006/06/18/AR2006061800986.html |archive-date=July 6, 2017 }}</ref> During the tour, the group members generally refrained from any explicit verbal political comments. When the Dixie Chicks performed again at Shepherd's Bush Empire, site of \"The Incident\", Maines joked that she wanted to say something the audience had not heard before, but instead said, \"Just so y'all know, we're ashamed the President of the United States is from Texas,\" to much laughter and applause.<ref name=\"Documentary film Shut Up and Sing\">[[Dixie Chicks: Shut Up and Sing]], at Shepherd's Bush, London</ref>\n\nIn 2006, ''Taking the Long Way'' was the ninth-best-selling album in the United States. At the [[49th Annual Grammy Awards]] in February 2007, the group won all five categories for which they were nominated, including the top awards of [[Grammy Award for Song of the Year|Song of the Year]] and [[Record of the Year]], both for \"Not Ready to Make Nice\", and [[Grammy Award for Album of the Year|Album of the Year]], for ''Taking the Long Way''. Maines interpreted the wins as being a show of public support for their advocacy of free speech.<ref>{{cite news|first=Nekesa Mumbi|last=Moody|agency=Associated Press|quote=I think people are using their freedom of speech with all these awards. We get the message.|url=http://www.heraldtribune.com/apps/pbcs.dll/article?AID=/20070212/FEATURES/70212001/1015/FEATURES10|date=February 12, 2007|title=Dixie Chicks lead Grammys with 5 awards|work=[[Sarasota Herald-Tribune]]|access-date=July 19, 2011|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110605040204/http://www.heraldtribune.com/apps/pbcs.dll/article?AID=%2F20070212%2FFEATURES%2F70212001%2F1015%2FFEATURES10|archive-date=June 5, 2011}}</ref> It had been 14 years since an artist had swept those three awards.<ref>{{cite news | url=https://select.nytimes.com/gst/abstract.html?res=F00B1FF8345B0C708DDDAB0894DF404482 | title=Grammy Sweep by Dixie Chicks Is Seen as a Vindication | newspaper=The New York Times | author=Leeds, Jeff | date=February 13, 2007 | url-status=live | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130523061534/http://select.nytimes.com/gst/abstract.html?res=F00B1FF8345B0C708DDDAB0894DF404482 | archive-date=May 23, 2013 | df=mdy-all }}</ref>\n\nAfter the Grammys, ''Taking the Long Way'' hit No. 8 on the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] and No. 1 on the country album charts and \"Not Ready to Make Nice\" re-entered the charts at No. 4 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]]. The music video for \"Not Ready to Make Nice\" was nominated for the 2007 [[CMT Music Video Awards]] in the categories of Video of the Year and Group Video of the Year.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.cmt.com/shows/events/cmt_music_awards/2007/nominees/ | title=CMT Music Video Award Nominees | publisher=[[Country Music Television|CMT]] | url-status=dead | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070423013211/http://www.cmt.com/shows/events/cmt_music_awards/2007/nominees/ | archive-date=April 23, 2007 | df=mdy-all }}</ref> The group was nominated for the 2007 [[Country Music Association]]'s award for Top Vocal Group, but lost to [[Rascal Flatts]].<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.cmaawards.com/2007/database/ArtistDetail.aspx?artistId=505 | title=Awards Database: Artist Detail: Dixie Chicks | publisher=[[CMA Awards]] | url-status=dead | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070927192819/http://www.cmaawards.com/2007/database/ArtistDetail.aspx?artistId=505 | archive-date=September 27, 2007 | df=mdy-all | access-date=August 31, 2007 }}</ref>\n\nAt the [[2006 Toronto International Film Festival]], Cabin Creek Films, the production company of documentarian [[Barbara Kopple]], premiered ''[[Dixie Chicks: Shut Up and Sing]]''. The documentary follows the Dixie Chicks over the three years since the 2003 London concert remark and covers aspects of their musical and personal lives in addition to the controversy.<ref name=\"hour\">{{cite news | url=http://www.hour.ca/film/film.aspx?iIDArticle=10688 | title=High Notes | author=Melora Koepke | newspaper=[[Hour (magazine)|Hour]] | date=November 2, 2006 | access-date=April 7, 2007 | url-status=dead | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070212204008/http://www.hour.ca/film/film.aspx?iIDArticle=10688 | archive-date=February 12, 2007 | df=mdy-all }}</ref>\n\nAn ad for ''Shut Up and Sing'' was turned down by [[NBC]] on October 27, 2006, because of a policy barring ads dealing with \"public controversy\". Ads were rebuffed by [[the CW]] as well, but local affiliate stations of all five major broadcasters, including NBC and CW, ran promotional spots for the film in New York and Los Angeles, the two cities where it opened that day.<ref name=\"cd-sing\"/> The film's distributor [[Harvey Weinstein]] said, \"It's a sad commentary about the level of fear in our society that a movie about a group of courageous entertainers who were [[blacklisted]] for exercising their right of free speech is now itself being blacklisted by corporate America.\"<ref name=\"cd-sing\">{{cite news | url=http://www.chinadaily.com.cn/entertainment/2006-10/29/content_719231.htm | title=NBC rejects TV ads for Dixie Chicks film | newspaper=[[China Daily]] | date=October 29, 2006 | url-status=live | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20061108100034/http://www.chinadaily.com.cn/entertainment/2006-10/29/content_719231.htm | archive-date=November 8, 2006 | df=mdy-all }}</ref>\n\n===2008\u20132014: Hiatus, Court Yard Hounds and continued touring===\nAt a December 2007 rally in [[Little Rock, Arkansas]], Maines expressed support for the [[West Memphis Three]], three men convicted of a 1993 triple murder who many believe innocent.<ref name=\"dcx-wm3\">{{cite web|url=http://www.dixiechicks.com/06_pressDetail.asp?newsID=669|title=Letter from Natalie Maines: WM3 Call to Action|publisher=Dixiechicks.com|date=November 26, 2007|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120313021526/http://www.dixiechicks.com/06_pressDetail.asp?newsID=669|archive-date=March 13, 2012}}</ref> Maines cited a recent defense filing implicating Terry Hobbs, the stepfather of one of the victims, and posted similar comments in a letter on the Dixie Chicks website.<ref name=\"dcx-wm3\" /> In November 2008, Hobbs sued Maines and the Dixie Chicks for defamation as a result of her statements.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.eonline.com/news/71845/natalie_maines_fellow_dixie_chicks|title=Natalie Maines, Fellow Dixie Chicks Courted for Libel|author=Finn, Natalie|publisher=[[E!]]|date=December 4, 2008|access-date=February 25, 2022|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20081208063646/http://www.eonline.com/uberblog/b71845_natalie_maines_fellow_dixie_chicks.html|archive-date=December 8, 2008}}</ref> On December 2, 2009, a U.S. federal judge dismissed the defamation case on the grounds that Hobbs had not shown the statements were made with [[actual malice]].<ref>{{cite news|url=http://news.ninemsn.com.au/entertainment/980335/lawsuit-against-dixie-chicks-dismissed |title=Lawsuit against Dixie Chicks dismissed |publisher=[[ninemsn]]|agency=Associated Press|date=December 6, 2009|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091209112949/http://news.ninemsn.com.au/entertainment/980335/lawsuit-against-dixie-chicks-dismissed|archive-date=December 9, 2009}}</ref> A proposed April 2008 commercial spot to promote [[Al Gore]]'s \"[[We Campaign]]\" involving both the Dixie Chicks and [[Toby Keith]] was eventually abandoned because of scheduling conflicts.<ref name=\"wapo123108\">{{cite news | url=http://voices.washingtonpost.com/postrock/2008/10/toby_keith_unplugged.html | title=Talk Talk: Toby Keith Unplugged | author=du Lac, J. Freedom | newspaper=The Washington Post | date=December 31, 2008 | access-date=November 23, 2008 | archive-date=January 11, 2012 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120111183755/http://voices.washingtonpost.com/postrock/2008/10/toby_keith_unplugged.html | url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\nIn 2010, Maguire and Strayer released their first album as [[Court Yard Hounds]], with Strayer singing lead vocals.<ref name=cmt>{{cite web|date=January 11, 2010|author=Morris, Edward|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1629456/two-members-of-dixie-chicks-releasing-album-without-natalie-maines/|title=Two Members of Dixie Chicks Releasing Album Without Natalie Maines|publisher=[[Country Music Television|CMT]]|access-date=December 26, 2010|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140115031625/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1629456/two-members-of-dixie-chicks-releasing-album-without-natalie-maines.jhtml|archive-date=January 15, 2014}}</ref><ref name=\"rename\">{{cite web|date=January 15, 2010|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1629856/two-dixie-chicks-rename-themselves-as-court-yard-hounds/|title=Two Dixie Chicks Rename Themselves as Court Yard Hounds|publisher=[[Country Music Television|CMT]]|access-date=February 25, 2022|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140115031407/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1629856/two-dixie-chicks-rename-themselves-as-court-yard-hounds.jhtml|archive-date=January 15, 2014}}</ref> Lloyd Maines said that the Dixie Chicks were \"definitely still an entity\".<ref name=cmt/> Beginning on June 8, 2010, the Dixie Chicks joined [[the Eagles]] on their stadium-based [[Eagles 2010 Summer Tour]],<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.courtyardhounds.com/us/news/dixie-chicks-tour-eagles|title=Dixie Chicks To Tour With The Eagles|publisher=Courtyardhounds.com|date=March 16, 2010|access-date=December 26, 2010|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110708032207/http://www.courtyardhounds.com/us/news/dixie-chicks-tour-eagles|archive-date=July 8, 2011}}</ref> visiting cities such as [[Toronto]], [[Boston]], Chicago, [[Philadelphia]], [[Washington, D.C.|Washington]], [[St. Louis]] and [[Winnipeg]] with a performance at the [[New Meadowlands Stadium]] in [[New Jersey]]. Country singer and guitarist [[Keith Urban]] appeared at selected shows.{{citation needed|date=December 2023}}\n\nThe Dixie Chicks appeared in the 2010 music documentary ''[[Sounds Like a Revolution]]'' about [[protest music]] in America. They sang \"You\" on the March 2011 release of ''[[Rare Bird Alert]]'', a [[Steve Martin]] bluegrass album, accompanied by the [[Steep Canyon Rangers]].<ref>{{cite magazine|author=Graff, Gary|url=https://www.billboard.com/music/music-news/dixie-chicks-record-new-song-eye-future-plans-957244/|title=Dixie Chicks Record New Song, Eye Future Plans|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|date=July 22, 2010|access-date=February 25, 2022|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130524201223/http://www.billboard.com/articles/photos/live/957244/dixie-chicks-record-new-song-eye-future-plans|archive-date=May 24, 2013}}</ref> In March 2011, Maines made a solo recording of the [[Beach Boys]] hit \"[[God Only Knows]]\" for the final episode of the HBO series ''[[Big Love]]''.<ref>{{Cite magazine|title=Natalie Maines Debuts New Song|url=https://people.com/celebrity/natalie-maines-sings-god-only-knows/|date=March 14, 2011|magazine=[[People (magazine)|People]]|access-date=June 26, 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110821073801/http://www.people.com/people/article/0,,20473643,00.html|archive-date=August 21, 2011}}</ref> In July 2011, Strayer and Maguire said that new music involving Maines is in the works.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theboot.com/2011/07/19/fans-first-coalition-dixie-chicks/|first=Cory|last=Stromblad|title=Dixie Chicks Join Fight Against Ticket Scalpers|work=The Boot|publisher=[[AOL]]|date=July 19, 2011|access-date=July 19, 2011|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110722115921/http://www.theboot.com/2011/07/19/fans-first-coalition-dixie-chicks|archive-date=July 22, 2011}}</ref> That October, following [[2011 Texas wildfires|a series of wildfires]] destroying homes and businesses throughout Texas, the Dixie Chicks played the Concert for Wildfire Relief in Austin. During the set, Maines stated that there was \"zero hesitation\" when the group was asked to do the show.<ref>{{cite web|title=Dixie Chicks headline concert for Texas wildfires relief|url=https://ew.com/article/2011/10/18/dixie-chicks-headline-concert-for-texas-wildfires-relief/|agency=Associated Press|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=October 18, 2011|access-date=June 25, 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111021050030/http://music-mix.ew.com/2011/10/18/dixie-chicks-headline-concert-for-texas-wildfires-relief/|archive-date=October 21, 2011}}</ref>\n\nIn July 2013, the Court Yard Hounds released their second album, ''[[Amelita (Court Yard Hounds album)|Amelita]]''. That month, the band replaced [[Lady Antebellum]] as headliners at Canada's [[Craven Country Jamboree]], and later performed at the [[Ottawa Bluesfest]] and the [[Cavendish Beach Music Festival]].<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/dixie-chicks-to-headline-canadian-festival-102353/ |title=Dixie Chicks to Headline Canadian Festival |magazine=Rolling Stone |date=December 26, 2012 |access-date=February 25, 2022 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140228165239/http://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/dixie-chicks-to-headline-canadian-festival-20121226 |archive-date=February 28, 2014 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.digitallounge.ca/bluesfest-2013-info-and-schedules/ |title=Bluesfest 2013 Info & Schedules \u2013 Ottawa Citizen Digital Lounge |publisher=Digital Lounge |date=June 4, 2013 |access-date=July 17, 2014 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140714182231/http://www.digitallounge.ca/bluesfest-2013-info-and-schedules/ |archive-date=July 14, 2014}}</ref> In October, the Dixie Chicks resumed touring for the [[Long Time Gone Tour]] through various cities across Canada and Europe. The tour incorporated the [[C2C: Country to Country]] festival held in London and [[Dublin]] during March 2014.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Mar 15, 2014: C2C: Country To Country 2014 at The O2 London, England |publisher= Concert Archives |url=https://www.concertarchives.org/concerts/c2c-country-to-country-2014 |access-date=June 24, 2022 |archive-date=June 24, 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220624162231/https://www.concertarchives.org/concerts/c2c-country-to-country-2014 |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\n===2016\u2013present: MMXVI World Tour, name change and ''Gaslighter''===\nIn June 2015, a European tour was scheduled to commence in [[Antwerp]] on April 16, 2016; the [[DCX MMXVI World Tour]] initially included dates for [[Switzerland]], [[The Netherlands]], [[Scandinavia]], the UK and Ireland, however in November 2015, the tour was extended into North America, with over forty shows scheduled across the United States and Canada.<ref>{{Cite news|title=Dixie Chicks To Launch North American Tour Next Summer|url=https://www.businessinsider.com/ap-the-dixie-chicks-to-launch-us-tour-next-summer-2015-11|date=November 16, 2015|work=[[Business Insider]]|agency=Associated Press|author=Mesfin Fekadu|access-date=June 25, 2020|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151116202639/http://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/dixie-chicks-tour_5649d8e9e4b045bf3defcdaf|archive-date=November 16, 2015}}</ref> The tour was extended to Australia and New Zealand, and was followed by a live album and video, ''DCX MMXVI Live''.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.dixiechicks.com/dcx-mmxvi-live-cassms|title=DCX MMXVI Live Out Now!|access-date=March 6, 2020|archive-date=October 21, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171021151957/http://www.dixiechicks.com/dcx-mmxvi-live-cassms/|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nOn the 50th anniversary of the [[Country Music Association Awards]] on November 2, 2016, the Dixie Chicks performed alongside [[Beyonc\u00e9]] on her song \"Daddy Lessons\". A studio version of the performance was released to digital outlets the following day.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/entertainthis/2016/11/02/beyonce-dixie-chicks-cma-awards-daddy-lessons/93207822/|title=Beyonc\u00e9 made country magic with the Dixie Chicks on 'Daddy Lessons'|website=USA Today|access-date=May 7, 2018|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170807231326/https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/entertainthis/2016/11/02/beyonce-dixie-chicks-cma-awards-daddy-lessons/93207822/|archive-date=August 7, 2017}}</ref> They also collaborated with [[Taylor Swift]] on her song \"[[Soon You'll Get Better]]\" from Swift's 2019 album ''[[Lover (album)|Lover]].''<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://hollywoodlife.com/2019/08/16/taylor-swift-tracklist-lover-songs/|title=Taylor Swift Reveals 'Lover' TrackList & Fans Are Freaking Out: We're 'Blessed'|last=Robidoux|first=Brandy|date=August 16, 2019|website=Hollywood Life|access-date=August 16, 2019|archive-date=August 16, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190816195044/https://hollywoodlife.com/2019/08/16/taylor-swift-tracklist-lover-songs/|url-status=dead}}</ref> On May 3, 2018, the Dixie Chicks' manager, Simon Renshaw, retired after having managed them since 1995. They signed with Ian Montone and Rick Yorn at Monotone/LBI Entertainment.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Halperin|first1=Shirley|last2=Trakin|first2=Roy|date=May 3, 2018|title=Dixie Chicks Sign With Ian Montone and Rick Yorn for Management|url=https://variety.com/2018/music/news/dixie-chicks-new-management-sign-ian-montone-rick-yorn-1202798154/|access-date=May 27, 2018|website=Variety|archive-date=May 27, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180527201453/http://variety.com/2018/music/news/dixie-chicks-new-management-sign-ian-montone-rick-yorn-1202798154/|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nOn June 25, 2020, the band changed their name to the Chicks, dropping the word \"[[Dixie]]\".<ref name=FloydIndependent>{{Cite news |date=January 1, 2021 |title=The Chicks: 'If George Floyd's murder hadn't happened, we might've waited to change our name' |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/music/features/the-chicks-interview-gaslighter-new-album-trump-george-floyd-bush-a9636596.html |access-date=July 1, 2023 |newspaper=The Independent |archive-date=July 1, 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230701202953/https://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/music/features/the-chicks-interview-gaslighter-new-album-trump-george-floyd-bush-a9636596.html |url-status=live }}</ref> The change followed criticism that the word had connotations of [[slavery in the United States]].<ref name=\":0\" /><ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2020/07/20/why-the-chicks-dropped-their-dixie|title=Why the Chicks Dropped Their \"Dixie\"|magazine=The New Yorker|author=Amanda Petrusich|date=July 13, 2020|access-date=July 13, 2020|archive-date=August 7, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200807215615/https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2020/07/20/why-the-chicks-dropped-their-dixie|url-status=live}}</ref>{{efn|The origin of the word \"Dixie\" is obscure, see [[Dixie#Origin of the name]].}} The band said they had picked \"that stupid name\" as teenagers, and had wanted to change it for years. They decided to change it when they saw the [[Modern display of the Confederate battle flag|Confederate flag]] described as \"the Dixie Swastika\" on social media in June 2020.<ref>{{cite magazine | url = https://variety.com/2020/music/news/dixie-chicks-explain-name-change-new-interview-1234701080/ | title = Ex-Dixie Chicks Explain Shortening 'Stupid' Name: 'We Wanted to Change It Years Ago' | first = Chris | last = Willman | date = July 8, 2020 | access-date = July 8, 2020 | magazine = [[Variety (magazine)|Variety]] | archive-date = July 8, 2020 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20200708220748/https://variety.com/2020/music/news/dixie-chicks-explain-name-change-new-interview-1234701080/ | url-status = live }}</ref> They were also inspired by the [[George Floyd protests]] and the [[Black Lives Matter]] movement, saying it \"definitely lit a fire in us to be on the right side of history\".<ref name=FloydIndependent/> They received the blessing of the [[The Chicks (duo)|Chicks]], a New Zealand duo, to share the name.<ref name=\":0\" /><ref>{{cite news |last1=Burgham |first1=Lydia |title=Kiwi band The Chicks on sharing name with The Dixie Chicks |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/entertainment/news/article.cfm?c_id=1501119&objectid=12343242 |newspaper=[[The New Zealand Herald]] |access-date=June 27, 2020 |date=June 26, 2020 |archive-date=June 26, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200626233253/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/entertainment/news/article.cfm?c_id=1501119&objectid=12343242 |url-status=live }}</ref> Alongside the name change, the Chicks released the [[protest song]] \"March March\" with a music video directed by Seanne Farmer, in tribute to [[social justice]] movements.<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite magazine|last=Willman|first=Chris|title=Dixie Chicks Officially Change Name to 'The Chicks'|url=https://variety.com/2020/music/news/dixie-chicks-change-name-1234689849/|magazine=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=June 25, 2020|access-date=June 25, 2020|archive-date=June 25, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200625172314/https://variety.com/2020/music/news/dixie-chicks-change-name-1234689849/|url-status=live}}</ref> They also introduced John Silva as their new manager,<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Halperin |first1=Shirley |last2=Willman |first2=Chris |title=The Chicks Change Not Just Name But Management, as John Silva Steps In (EXCLUSIVE) |url=https://variety.com/2020/music/news/chicks-change-management-john-silva-dixie-chicks-1234690445/ |magazine=Variety |date=June 25, 2020 |access-date=June 26, 2020 |archive-date=June 27, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200627065614/https://variety.com/2020/music/news/chicks-change-management-john-silva-dixie-chicks-1234690445/ |url-status=live }}</ref> with publicity by Cindi Berger of R&CPMK.<ref>{{cite web |last=Sanchez |first=Daniel |title=Rogers & C PMK-BMC Officially Merge; Superstar Musical Clientele Combined |url=https://www.digitalmusicnews.com/2019/07/30/rogers-cowan-pmk-bmc-merger/ |website=Digital Music News |date=July 30, 2019 |access-date=July 28, 2020 |archive-date=July 28, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200728232812/https://www.digitalmusicnews.com/2019/07/30/rogers-cowan-pmk-bmc-merger/ |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nOn July 17, 2020, Columbia released the Chicks' first new studio album in 14 years, ''[[Gaslighter (album)|Gaslighter]]'', produced by [[Jack Antonoff]].<ref>{{cite web|author=Strauss, Matthew|date=June 11, 2020|title=Dixie Chicks reveal new release date for new album 'Gaslighter'|url=https://pitchfork.com/news/dixie-chicks-reveal-new-release-for-new-album-gaslighter/|access-date=June 11, 2020|work=Pitchfork|archive-date=June 11, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200611182733/https://pitchfork.com/news/dixie-chicks-reveal-new-release-for-new-album-gaslighter/|url-status=live}}</ref> The first single, \"[[Gaslighter (song)|Gaslighter]]\", was released on March 4.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Blackwelder |first=Carson |date=4 March 2020 |title=Dixie Chicks drop 'Gaslighter,' their 1st new music in 14 years |url=https://abcnews.go.com/GMA/Culture/dixie-chicks-drop-gaslighter-music-14-years/story?id=69389829 |access-date=December 23, 2023 |agency=[[ABC News (United States)|ABC News]] |archive-date=December 23, 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231223230338/https://abcnews.go.com/GMA/Culture/dixie-chicks-drop-gaslighter-music-14-years/story?id=69389829 |url-status=live }}</ref> On August 20, the Chicks performed \"[[The Star-Spangled Banner]]\" at the [[2020 Democratic National Convention]].<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Lipshutz|first=Jason|date=August 20, 2020|title=The Chicks Sing National Anthem at the 2020 DNC: Watch the Performance|url=https://www.billboard.com/music/music-news/the-chicks-dnc-national-anthem-performance-9437899/|magazine=Billboard|access-date=February 25, 2022|archive-date=February 25, 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220225204136/https://www.billboard.com/music/music-news/the-chicks-dnc-national-anthem-performance-9437899/|url-status=live}}</ref> On December 22, 2023, founding bassist Laura Lynch died in a traffic collision near [[El Paso, Texas]], at the age of 65.<ref name=\":2\">{{Cite magazine |last=Zee |first=Michaela |date=December 23, 2023 |title=Laura Lynch, Dixie Chicks Founding Member, Dies at 65 |url=https://variety.com/2023/music/news/laura-lynch-dead-dixie-chicks-1235850102/ |access-date=December 23, 2023 |magazine=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]] |archive-date=December 23, 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231223230021/https://variety.com/2023/music/news/laura-lynch-dead-dixie-chicks-1235850102/ |url-status=live }}</ref> The Chicks issued a statement saying Lynch was \"a bright light\" whose \"undeniable talents helped propel us beyond busking on street corners to stages all across Texas and the mid-West\".<ref name=\":2\" />\n\n==Band members==\n[[File:DixieChicks-PressConference.jpg|thumb|The Dixie Chicks in 2006.]]\n\n'''Current members'''\n* [[Emily Strayer]] \u2013 vocals, banjo, (1995\u2013present)\n\n'''Former members'''\n* Laura Lynch \u2013 vocals, bass (1989\u20131995; died 2023)<ref name=\"LL1\">{{Cite news |last1=Deb |first1=Sopan |last2=Ortiz |first2=Aimee
